Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Liability for Adding a Rider (Irdaf) on a Hired Animal
Ruling on adding a rider and liability for animal's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hirer adds a rider to a hired animal and apply the qiyas to diyat to explain why half value is due.

Core Idea
Liability for adding a rider is divided equally by number, not weight, analogous to multiple wounds.

This lesson examines a specific case in ijarah: a hirer adds an extra rider behind him on the hired animal, and the animal dies. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling: the hirer guarantees half the animal's value if the animal can carry two and the rider holds himself; otherwise, full value. The reasoning is grounded in qiyas to the division of blood money (diyat) in cases of multiple wounds, where liability is split equally even if wounds differ in severity. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi fiqh treats shared causation in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Initial Ruling
The matn states: if a hirer adds a rider (irdaf) and the animal dies, he guarantees half the value. First, identify the act (irdaf) and the basic hukm (daman nisf al-qimah).
The phrase 'wa in atabat shart al-musta'jir' indicates the hirer's condition led to the death.
2
Apply the Animal's Capacity Condition
The commentary clarifies: if the animal can carry two and the rider holds himself, the hirer guarantees half. If the animal cannot carry two, he guarantees full value. Check the capacity condition as the first variable.
Weight is irrelevant; only number of riders matters, analogous to diyat.
3
Examine the Rider's Control
If the rider is a child who cannot hold himself, liability is proportional to his weight, not half. Distinguish this exception from the general rule.
This shows the 'illa is not purely number; lack of control shifts the basis.
4
Understand the Qiyas to Diyat
The proof: just as blood money for multiple wounds is divided equally regardless of severity, liability for a shared cause of death (riding) is divided equally by number of riders. Grasp the analogy: the cause of death is not precisely measurable, so equitable division by count.
The qiyas is jaliy: both involve shared causation with indeterminate impact.
5
Combine Hire and Liability
Despite guaranteeing half value, the hirer must still pay full hire if the animal died after reaching the destination. Two different considerations: hire for his own ride, liability for the extra rider.
This resolves the seeming contradiction of paying both damages and hire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن عطبت شرط المستأجر عند عقد الإجارة بالإرداف ضمن النصف، أي نصف قيمة الدابة جزاء كالشعير والسمسم من البر والحديد والآجر هلكت الداب. وإن عطبت صورة المسألة: أن رجلا استأجر دابة ليركبها، فأردف معه رجلا فعطبت الدابة، فإن كانت الدابة تطيق حمل اثنين، وكان الرديف مستمسكا بنفسه ضمن المستأجر نصف قيمة الدابة ولا اعتبار للثقل، لأن الدابة يعقرها جهل الراكب الخفيف ويخف عليها ركوب الثقيل لعلمه بالفروسية؛ ولأن الآدمي غير موزون، فلا يمكن معرفته بالوزن، فلا ينقسم الضمان على الثقل، بل يعتبر عدد الراكب كعدد الجناية في الجنايات، فإنه إذا جرح رجل رجلا جراحة واحدة، والآخر عشر جراحات خطأ فمات فالدية بينهما أنصافا؛ لأنه رب جراحة واحدة أكثر تأثيرا من عشر جراحات، وإن كانت الدابة لا تطيق ضمن جميع قيمتها كما قال المصنف في "الكافي"، وإن كان الرديف صغيرا لا يستمسك بنفسه، يضمن بقدر ثقله. وإنما قيد ضمان نصف القيمة بالارداف؛ لأنه لو حمله على عاتقه، وعطبت ضمن جميع قيمتها؛ لكون النفل يجتمع في مكان واحد فيشق على الدابة، وإن كانت تطيق حملهما، وإطلاق المصنف الإرداف يشمل ما إذا أردف ولد الناقة المستأجرة الذي ولدته بعد الإجارة، وإن كان ملك صاحبها؛ لعدم الإذن كما لو حمل على دابته شيئا آخر من ملك صاحبها، ذكره في "المحيط". خلفه بالإرداف: هو أن يجلس الراكب خلفه رجلا. ضمن النصف إلخ أي ضمن المستأجر نصف قيمة الدابة، ثم المالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمن المستأجر، وإن شاء ضمن ذلك الرجل، فإن ضمن المستأجر لا يرجع هو على ذلك الرجل مستأجرا كان أو مستعيرا، وإن ضمن ذلك الرجل رجع هو على المستأجر كان ذلك الرجل مستأجرا، وإن كان مستعيرا لا يرجع، ولم يتعرض المصنف لوجوب الأجر، والمنقول في "النهاية" و"المحيط" أنه يجب جميع الأجر إذا هلك بعد بلوغ المقصد مع تضمين نصف القيمة؛ لأنه استوفى المنفعة ولا يقال: كيف اجتمع الأجر والضمان مع امتناع جمعهما؛ لأنا نقول: إن الضمان لركوب غيره، والأجر لركوبه بنفسه فهما باعتبارين مختلفين فلا منع في الجمع. [البحر الرائق: ٤٤٨/٧] واعلم أن ضمان نصف القيمة لعله إذا كان الرديف غير المستأجر، فلو كان الكل؛ لأنه صار غاصبا ولا أجر هكذا في البحر" و"الفتح" وغيرهما.
And if it [the animal] dies [due to] the condition of the hirer at the time of the ijarah contract by adding a rider (irdaf), he guarantees half, i.e., half the value of the animal, as a penalty like barley and sesame from wheat and iron and brick the animal died. And the image of the issue: that a man hired an animal to ride it, and added a rider with him, and the animal died. If the animal can carry two, and the rider holds himself, then the hirer guarantees half the value of the animal, and no consideration is given to weight, because the animal is harmed by the ignorance of the light rider and made easy by the riding of the heavy rider due to his skill in horsemanship; and because the human is not weighed, so it is not possible to know by weight, so the liability is not divided according to weight, but rather the number of riders is considered like the number of crimes in injuries, for if a man wounds another with one wound, and another with ten wounds by mistake and he dies, the blood money is between them in halves; because sometimes one wound is more effective than ten wounds. And if the animal cannot carry [two], then he guarantees all its value as the author said in al-Kafi. And if the rider is a child who does not hold himself, he guarantees according to his weight. And the restriction of guarantee of half value to irdaf is because if he carried him on his shoulder and it dies, he guarantees full value because the load collects in one place and is difficult for the animal, even if it can carry both. And the author's unqualified mention of irdaf includes the case where he adds the offspring of the hired she-camel that was born after the ijarah, even if it is the property of its owner, due to lack of permission, just as if he carried something else owned by the owner on his animal. Mentioned in al-Muhit. And the meaning of irdaf is that the rider sits behind him a man. 'He guarantees half etc.' i.e., the hirer guarantees half the value of the animal. Then the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may hold the hirer liable, or he may hold that man liable. If he holds the hirer liable, he does not have recourse against that man, whether he was a hirer or a borrower. If he holds that man liable, he has recourse against the hirer if that man was a hirer, and if he was a borrower, he has no recourse. And the author did not address the obligation of the hire. And it is transmitted in al-Nihaya and al-Muhit that full hire is obligated if it dies after reaching the destination along with liability for half the value, because he utilized the benefit, and it is not said: how can hire and liability combine while they cannot be combined? For we say: The liability is for riding another, and the hire is for his own riding, so they are according to two different considerations, so there is no prevention of combination. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:448] And know that the guarantee of half value is perhaps when the rider is other than the hirer; if he were [the hirer himself?] then all [value] because he becomes a usurper and no hire; thus in al-Bahr and al-Fath and others.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary on the case of adding a rider (irdaf) to a hired animal. The matn states that if the animal dies due to the hirer adding a rider, he guarantees half the value. The commentary expands: the scenario is a man hires an animal to ride and then adds a rider behind him. If the animal can carry two and the rider holds himself, the hirer guarantees half the value, regardless of actual weight, because the number of riders is analogous to the number of wounds in diyat (blood money) where liability is divided equally even if one wound is more severe. If the animal cannot carry two, the hirer guarantees full value. If the rider is a child who cannot hold himself, liability is proportional to his weight. The commentary also distinguishes irdaf from carrying on the shoulder, which incurs full liability. The hirer has no recourse against the rider unless the rider was a hirer himself. Importantly, the hirer must still pay the full hire even though he is partially liable, because the two obligations are based on different considerations: liability is for the extra rider, hire is for his own ride.

Key Terms
الإرداف (al-irdāf): Adding a rider behind the original rider on the same animal.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability, guarantee, or compensation for loss.
الدية (al-diyah): Blood money paid for manslaughter or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, if a hired animal can carry two riders and the extra rider holds himself, what is the hirer's liability?
A) Full value of the animal.
B) Half value of the animal.
C) No liability because the animal could carry two.
D) Liability proportional to the rider's weight.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability for adding a rider (irdaf) is divided equally by the number of riders, not weight, based on qiyas to diyat.

Overloading the Hired Animal: Liability for Excess Weight
Ruling with qiyas expansion on overloading a hired animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between simultaneous and incremental acts in ijara, apply the Hanafi ruling for excess weight, and state the conditions for full versus partial liability.

Core Idea
Excess weight of same genus splits liability; different genus or incremental act triggers full liability.

When you hire an animal to carry a specific weight, what happens if you load more than agreed? The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between adding weight of the same type versus a different type, and between a single act (carrying) and a gradual act (grinding). This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying qiyas, helping you understand when the hirer guarantees only the excess and when he guarantees the full value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Start with the matn: the hirer guarantees only what exceeds the specified load, not the full value. Underline that this applies only when the excess is of the same genus and the animal was capable.
The Arabic 'ما زاد' explicitly limits liability to the increase.
2
Understand the exception for different genus
If the hirer loads a different type of cargo (e.g., iron instead of grain), full liability for the animal's value is imposed because the act is entirely beyond permission.
The text says 'وجب جميع القيمة'.
3
Examine the roles of hirer and owner
If only the owner loaded the extra, the hirer is not liable. If both loaded together, each is liable for half. If each brought a friend (not part of contract), no liability on the hirer.
These scenarios show liability tracks who caused the excess.
4
Analyze the qiyas with grinding
The commentary contrasts carrying (simultaneous load) with grinding (incremental). In grinding, each unit is a separate act; after the agreed amount, permission ends, so any extra makes the hirer fully liable. In carrying, the load is one batch, so only the excess is unauthorized.
This is a clear example of qiyas jaliy distinguishing two situations.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Apply the rule: the hirer pays only for the extra weight (value of excess) but still owes full rent because he benefited from the ride. The combination of liability and rent is not contradictory.
The author references 'Ghayat al-Bayan' for this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالزيادة على الحمل المسمى ما زاد. على الحمل المسمى بأن سمي قنطارا مثلا وحمل عليها أكثر منه: استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها مقدارا معينا، فحمل عليها أكثر منه فعطبت، فإن كان المستأجر هو الذي حملها، وكانت الدابة مطيقة يضمن ما زاد الثقل؛ لأنها هلكت بما هو مأذون فيه وغير مأذون فيه والسبب الثقل، فانقسم عليهما، وهذا إذا كانت الزيادة من جنس المسمى كما يشير إليه لفظ الزيادة، فلو حمل جنسا آخر غير المسمى وجب جميع القيمة، وإن حملها صاحب الدابة بيده وحده، فلا ضمان على المستأجر، وإن حملاه معا وجب النصف على المستأجر، ولو حمل كل واحد صديقا وحده لا ضمان على المستأجر، ويجعل حمل المستأجر ما كان مستحقا عليه بالعقد. (ملخصا) ما زاد: أي يضمن ما زاد على المسمى، لا يقال: ينبغي أن يضمن الجميع كما إذا استأجر ثورا ليطحن به عشر مخاتيم، فطحن بها أحد عشر مختوما، فهلك يضمن الجميع؛ لأنا نقول: إن الطحن يكون شيئا فشيئا، فإذا طحن العشرة انتهى الإذن، فبعد ذلك هو مخالف في استعماله الدابة بغير الإذن، فيضمن الجميع، بخلاف الحمل، فإنه يكون جملة، ولم يتعرض المصنف للأجر إذا هلك، وفي غاية "البيان أن عليه الكراء كاملا، ووجه اجتماع الضمان والأجر ما مر ذكره. (ملخصا)
And by increase over the specified load: what increases. On the specified load: for example, if he specified a qintar and loaded more than that on it: he hired an animal to carry a certain amount on it, then he loaded more than that on it, and it died. Then if the hirer himself loaded it, and the animal was capable, he guarantees the extra weight, because it died due to what is permitted and not permitted, and the cause is the weight, so it is divided between them. This is when the increase is of the same genus as the specified, as the word increase indicates. If he loaded a different genus other than the specified, then full value is obligatory. If the owner of the animal loaded it himself alone, then no liability on the hirer. If both loaded together, half is obligatory on the hirer. If each loaded a friend alone, no liability on the hirer. And the hirer's load is considered what was due on him by contract. (Summarized) 'What increases': i.e., he guarantees what increases over the specified. It should not be said: he should guarantee all, as if he hired an ox to grind ten makhatim [measures], then he ground eleven makhatim with it, and it died, he guarantees all. For we say: grinding is gradual, so when he ground ten, the permission ended, thereafter he is violating in using the animal without permission, so he guarantees all. Unlike carrying, for it is a single act. And the author did not address the hire if it dies, and in Ghayat al-Bayan that he owes full rent, and the point of combining liability and hire is what was mentioned earlier. (Summarized)
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary on overloading a hired animal. The matn states that if the hirer loads more than the specified amount, he guarantees only the excess weight, not the full value. The commentary explains: if the hirer himself loads the extra, and the animal could handle both the specified and excess, he guarantees only the additional weight because the death was caused by both licensed and unlicensed weight. However, if the extra load is of a different genus, he guarantees full value because it's a complete violation. If the owner loaded the extra, the hirer is not liable. If both loaded, half liability. The commentary distinguishes this from the case of grinding where each unit is separate; in carrying, the load is a single batch, so full liability is not triggered for the whole. The hirer still owes full rent because he benefited from the ride.

Key Terms
مختوم (makhtūm): A measure of grain (about 16 liters). Used as an example in the analogy with the grinding ox.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when the hirer loads extra weight of a different genus on the hired animal?
A) He guarantees only the excess weight.
B) He guarantees the full value of the animal.
C) He guarantees half the value.
D) He guarantees nothing.

Key Takeaway
When a hired animal dies from overloading, the hirer's liability is proportional: only the excess weight if same genus and simultaneous act, full value if different genus or incremental act.

Beating and Pulling the Hired Animal: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Dispute on liability for beating and pulling hired animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability for beating and pulling a hired animal and explain the proofs for each, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds full liability for animal death from beating or pulling because permission is conditional on safety.

This lesson examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The debate centers on whether a hirer who beats or pulls a hired animal, causing its death, must guarantee its value. Both positions rest on reasoning from the nature of permission in a contract. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify how implied conditions affect contractual liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
The act is beating (darb) and pulling (kabh) a hired animal, not mere driving (saqy). Driving is agreed upon as permissible without liability.
The dispute only concerns these two specific actions.
2
State the conflicting rulings
Abu Hanifa says the hirer is liable for the full value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no liability if the act is customary.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Customary acts are included in the absolute permission of the contract. Since beating and pulling are customary, they fall under the hirer’s implied permission.
This is based on the generality of the permission to use the animal.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Permission is restricted by an implied condition of safety. Beating and pulling are not necessary for riding; they are only for urging or stopping, and if they cause death, they exceed the safe use.
Abu Hanifa analogizes to passing on the road – one may walk but not cause harm.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the animal dies due to beating or pulling, Abu Hanifa requires the hirer to pay full compensation; the Sahibayn do not require compensation if the act was customary.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa’s view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالضرب والكبح: أي إذا استأجر دابة فضربها وكبحها أي جذبها إلى نفسه لتقف ولا تجري، فهلكت ضمن جميع القيمة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: لا يضمن إذا فعل فعلا متعارفا؛ لأن المتعارف مما يدخل تحت مطلق العقد، فكان حاصلا بإذنه، ولأبي حنيفة: أن الإذن مقيد بشرط السلامة بدونه وإنما هو للمبالغة فيتقيد بوصف السلامة كالمرور في الطريق، وإنما قيد بالضرب والكبح؛ لأنه لا يتضمن بالسوق؛ إذ يتحقق السوق اتفاقا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥٠/٧]
And by beating and pulling: i.e., if he hires an animal and beats it and pulls (kabh) i.e., draws it towards himself to stop and not run, and it dies, then he guarantees all its value according to Abu Hanifa. And [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: he does not guarantee if he did a customary action; because what is customary enters under the absolute contract, so it is covered by his permission. And Abu Hanifa's argument: that permission is restricted to the condition of safety; without it, it is only for urging (mubalagha), so it is restricted by the description of safety, like passing on the road. And it is restricted to beating and pulling because it is not included in driving (saqy); for driving is agreed upon. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:450]
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The issue: if a hirer strikes the animal or pulls its reins to stop it, and the animal dies, is he liable? Abu Hanifa says full liability because the permission to use the animal is conditional on safety—customary beating is only for urging (mubalagha) but not to the point of harm. The Sahibayn say no liability for customary beating because it is included in the absolute permission of the contract. The commentary notes that driving is unanimously permitted, but beating and pulling are distinguished because they are not inherent to riding. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view in this text, as the commentary supports it.

Key Terms
الكبح (al-kabh): Pulling the reins to stop or slow the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, what is the ruling if a hirer beats a hired animal customarily and it dies?
A) No liability because it is customary.
B) Full liability because permission is conditional on safety.
C) Half liability because of shared responsibility.
D) Liability only if excessive force is proven.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view is the mufta bihi: the hirer guarantees the animal if death results from beating or pulling, because permission is limited by safety.

Removing the Saddle and Using an Unsuitable Saddle: Liability by Consensus
Ruling on liability when using unsuitable saddle on hired donkey.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hirer changes the saddle of a hired donkey to an unsuitable one, and explain how the proof of ijma' supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Changing the saddle of a hired donkey to an unsuitable one creates full liability by consensus.

When you hire a donkey with a saddle, you have certain responsibilities. But what if you remove the original saddle and put on a saddle meant for a mule? The scholars agreed that this action makes you liable for any resulting damage. This lesson explains the ruling and its basis in scholarly consensus (ijma').

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What action does the text describe? (Removing the original saddle and using a saddle unsuitable for donkeys). What is the ruling? (The hirer guarantees full value – yadmanu).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited for this ruling? (Ijma' – consensus).
The text explicitly states 'yadmanu ijma'an' (he guarantees by consensus).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the consensus prove the ruling? (Because the scholars unanimously agree that such an act creates liability; there is no disagreement.)
The consensus is qat'i (definitive) in transmission and meaning.
4
Check for ikhtilaf
Is there any difference of opinion? (No, it is recorded as ijma', so all schools agree.)
5
Apply the principle
What does this teach about liability in ijarah? (Any change that makes the animal unsuitable for its normal use leads to full liability.)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونزع السرج يعني لو اكترى حمارا بسرج فنزع السرج، وأسرجه سرجا لا يسرج بمثله الحمر، يضمن إجماعا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥١/٧] بمثله بأن أسرج الحمار بسرج البرذون مثلا.
And removing the saddle means: if he hires a donkey with a saddle, then removes the saddle and saddles it with a saddle that donkeys are not usually saddled with, he guarantees by consensus. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:451] 'With its like': i.e., he saddles the donkey with a saddle of a mule (birdhawn) for example.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with evidence of consensus (ijma'). The case: a person hires a donkey with a saddle, then removes the saddle and puts on a different saddle that is not suitable for donkeys (e.g., a mule saddle). If the donkey dies, the hirer is liable for full value. The commentary adds that the consensus (ijma') covers this. The phrase 'bimitlihi' explains the example.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijmā'): Consensus of scholars as a source of law; here it establishes liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a donkey with a saddle, then removes it and puts a mule saddle on the donkey, causing injury. What is the ruling?
A) No liability because any saddle can be used.
B) Full liability by consensus.
C) Half liability because the donkey could bear it.
D) No liability if the saddle was comfortable.

Key Takeaway
Using an unsuitable saddle on a hired animal makes the hirer fully liable, and this is established by scholarly consensus.

Liability for Overloading a Hired Animal: Hanafi Ruling and Distinctions
Ruling with proof using qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) and istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on liability when a hired animal perishes due to overloading, distinguish between same-type and different-type excess, and apply the qiyas distinction between instantaneous loading and continuous grinding.

Core Idea
Overloading divides liability: only excess if same type, full if different; gradual acts trigger full liability, instantaneous acts trigger proportional liability.

When you hire an animal for transport, you agree on a specific load. What happens if you load more and the animal dies? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer: it depends on whether the extra load is of the same kind, and on how the work is done. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and a key analogy with milling that clarifies the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Read the passage: a hirer loads more than the agreed weight on a hired animal, and the animal dies. Determine the default ruling: he guarantees only the excess weight, not the whole value.
The excess must be of the same type (jins) as the named load.
2
Recognize the exceptions
The ruling changes if (a) the increase is of a different type – then full value is guaranteed; (b) the owner loads the animal alone – no liability on hirer; (c) both load together – half value; (d) each loads separately (e.g., hirer loads friend's goods, owner loads his own) – no liability on hirer.
The text often summarizes these from longer works like al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
3
Analyze the objection and answer
A student might object: why not guarantee the whole value, just like the case of an ox hired to grind ten units but used for eleven, where full liability applies? The answer distinguishes based on the nature of the work: grinding is continuous (shay'an fa shay'an), so after the permitted amount, further work is wholly unauthorized; loading is instantaneous (jumlatan), so the permitted and unpermitted acts are simultaneous.
The illa (effective cause) is the temporal structure of the action.
4
Consider the combination of guarantee and rent
Even though the hirer is liable for damage, he still owes the full rent. Why? Because guarantee compensates for the animal’s value (due to exceeding permission), while rent is for the benefit received. They are based on different considerations, so they can coexist.
This is explained in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Think of renting a truck or a cargo vehicle. The same principle applies: if you overload with the same type of goods, you only pay for the extra weight; if you switch to a different type, you may be liable for the whole vehicle’s value if it is damaged.
Modern mapping requires caution – physical damage and insurance may overlap, but the legal framework remains instructive.

Source Text

(ملخصا)
And for the increase beyond the named load, that which is increased; and for hitting and pulling the reins, and removing the saddle and pack-saddle, and if it is destroyed by the increase, and if it is destroyed is attached to 'and for hitting', and saddling with something with which it is not normally saddled, and taking a road other than the one specified, and if they differ. The owner of the goods is a guarantor, despite the prohibition of combining them; because we say: the guarantee is for someone else riding, and the rent is for his own riding, so they are two different considerations, so there is no prohibition in combining. On the named load: for example, if he named a qintar and loaded more than that upon it, he hired an animal to carry a specified amount, and he loaded more than that on it and it was destroyed; if the hirer himself loaded it and the animal was capable, he guarantees the excess weight; because it was destroyed by something both permitted and not permitted, and the cause is the weight, so it is divided between them. This is if the increase is of the same type as the named load, as the word 'increase' indicates. If he loads a different type not named, then the entire value is obligatory. And if the owner of the animal loaded it by himself alone, there is no guarantee on the hirer. And if they both loaded it together, half is obligatory on the hirer. And if each loaded a friend alone, there is no guarantee on the hirer, and the hirer's load is considered what was due upon him by the contract. (Summarized) 'That which increased': i.e., he guarantees what exceeds the named load. It should not be said that he should guarantee the whole, as when he hires an ox to grind ten makhatim with it, and he grinds eleven makhatim with it and it is destroyed, he guarantees the whole; because we say: grinding happens little by little, so when he grinds ten, the permission ends, then after that he is contravening by using the animal without permission, so he guarantees the whole. Unlike loading, because it happens all at once. And the author did not address the rent if it is destroyed, and in Ghayat al-Bayan he owes the full rent, and the reason for combining guarantee and rent is as previously mentioned. (Summarized)

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter of Ijarah concerning the liability of a hirer when he loads more than the agreed weight on a hired animal, and the animal perishes. The author clarifies that the hirer guarantees only the excess weight, not the full value, because the destruction is caused by both the permitted and unpermitted load. The guarantee is divided proportionally. However, if the increase is of a different type (not same genus as the named load), he guarantees the entire value. If the owner of the animal loads it alone, the hirer is not liable. If both load, half the value. If each loads separately (e.g., the hirer loads his friend's goods and the owner loads his own), the hirer is not liable. A comparison is made with milling, where because it occurs gradually, the guarantee is for the whole after the permitted amount is finished. This highlights the Hanafi principle of considering the nature of the action (continuous vs. instantaneous) in determining liability.

Key Terms
الحمل المسمى (al-haml al-musamma): The specific load that was agreed upon in the hire contract.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability to compensate for damage or loss; in this context, the obligation to pay the value of the animal or the excess.
الأجر (al-ajr): The rental payment owed for the use of the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires an animal to carry 10 kg of wheat, but loads 12 kg of the same wheat, and the animal dies, what does the Hanafi school say about the hirer's liability?
A) He guarantees the full value of the animal.
B) He guarantees only the value of the extra 2 kg.
C) He is not liable at all.
D) He guarantees half the value.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, overloading a hired animal does not automatically entail full liability; the outcome depends on whether the excess is of the same type and on the nature of the use (instantaneous vs. continuous).

Liability for Hitting or Pulling Reins of a Hired Animal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for hitting/pulling reins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on liability for hitting or pulling reins of a hired animal, explain their proofs, and apply the ruling to customary vs. excessive actions.

Core Idea
Customary actions may be covered by the hire contract; hitting and pulling reins are disputed.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a hirer who hits or pulls the reins of a hired animal, causing its death, is liable for its value. Abu Hanifa holds full liability, while the Sahibayn distinguish between customary and excessive actions. Understanding this dispute clarifies the scope of implied permission in hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is the hirer hitting the animal or pulling its reins (to stop it) resulting in death. The dispute: is the hirer liable for the full value?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa: liability for full value. His proof: permission is implicitly conditioned on safety, like passing through a road – exceeding that violates the contract.
Analogy to road: you may pass but are liable if you cause harm.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): no liability if the action is customary, because customary actions fall under the absolute permission of the contract.
Customary acts are impliedly permitted (urf).
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Abu Hanifa: any hitting/pulling causing death leads to full liability. Sahibayn: only excessive or unconventional actions incur liability.
Mufta bihi in later fatwa is often Abu Hanifa's view due to caution.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a specific case (e.g., gentle tug or violent strike), determine liability based on the two positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالضرب والكبح: أي إذا استأجر دابة فضربها وكبحها أي جذبها إلى نفسه لتقف ولا تجري، فهلكت ضمن جميع القيمة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يضمن إذا فعل فعلا متعارفا؛ لأن المتعارف مما يدخل تحت مطلق العقد، فكان حاصلا بإذنه، ولأبي حنيفة: أن الإذن مقيد بشرط السلامة بدونه وإنما هو للمبالغة فيتقيد بوصف السلامة كالمرور في الطريق، وإنما قيد بالضرب والكبح؛ لأنه لا يتضمن بالسوق؛ إذ يتحقق السوق اتفاقا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥٠/٧]
And hitting and pulling the reins: meaning if he hired an animal and hit it and pulled its reins, i.e., pulled it towards himself to make it stop and not run, and it died, he guarantees the entire value according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: he does not guarantee if he did a customary act, because the customary act falls under the absolute contract, so it is obtained by his permission. And for Abu Hanifa: that permission is restricted with the condition of safety, without which it is only for encouragement, so it is restricted by the description of safety, like passing through the road. And it was specified as hitting and pulling the reins because it is not included in 'driving' since driving occurs by agreement. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:450]
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a hirer who hits or pulls the reins of a hired animal, causing its death. Abu Hanifa rules that the hirer guarantees the full value because although the contract permits using the animal, it does not permit actions that harm it; permission is implicitly conditioned on safety. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that if the action is customary (e.g., gentle pulling to guide the animal), it is covered by the general permission of the contract, so no liability arises. However, if the action is excessive or unconventional, they would agree with liability. The text then explains that the dispute is specifically about hitting and pulling, not ordinary driving, because driving is uncontroversially permitted.

Key Terms
الضرب (al-darb): Hitting the animal; in this context, an action that may cause harm.
الكبح (al-kabh): Pulling the reins (to make the animal stop); a specific action that might cause injury.
متعارف (muta'araf): Customary or conventional action; an act that people normally do in such situations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa says liable only if action is excessive; Sahibayn say always liable.
B) Abu Hanifa says always liable; Sahibayn say liable only if action is excessive.
C) Both agree liability depends on whether the action is customary.
D) Both agree the hirer is never liable for customary actions.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa holds the hirer fully liable for hitting/pulling reins causing death, while the Sahibayn exempt customary actions; later fatwa often adopts Abu Hanifa's caution.

Ruling on Removing and Replacing the Saddle Without Permission
Ruling on hirer's liability for unsuitable saddle replacement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a hirer replaces the saddle with an unsuitable one and identify the basis of liability by consensus.

Core Idea
Using an unsuitable saddle on a hired animal makes the hirer liable by consensus.

In a hire contract (ijara), the hirer is entrusted with the animal and its equipment. Changing the equipment without the owner's permission is a breach of that trust. This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: if the hirer removes the saddle that came with the animal and replaces it with one that is unsuitable, he is liable for any damage, and this liability is established by consensus (ijma').

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is: a hirer removes the saddle that was part of the hire and replaces it with a saddle that is not suitable for that type of animal. The ruling: the hirer is liable (yadman) by consensus.
The liability is for the full value of the animal if harmed.
2
Recognize the Violation
The violation is using equipment that is not customary for the animal. The example given is using a horse saddle (saraj al-bardhawn) on a donkey. This is a misuse of the hired property.
The hirer's permission to use the animal does not extend to changing its essential equipment.
3
Understand the Basis of Liability
The liability is not based on negligence alone; it is a direct consequence of the unauthorized substitution. The text emphasizes that this is established by consensus (ijma'an), meaning all scholars agree on the ruling.
Consensus strengthens the authority of the ruling; it is not open to ijtihad.
4
Apply the Ruling to Similar Cases
Consider if the hirer changes the bridle or other essential equipment to something unsuitable. The same principle applies: he is liable if harm results. Also, if he adds extra weight or modifies the animal without permission, the ruling extends by analogy.
The key is that the change is unauthorized and unsuitable for the animal.

Source Text

ونزع السرج يعني لو اكترى حمارا بسرج فنزع السرج، وأسرجه سرجا لا يسرج بمثله الحمر، يضمن إجماعا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥١/٧] بمثله بأن أسرج الحمار بسرج البرذون مثلا.
And removing the saddle: meaning if he hired a donkey with a saddle, and removed the saddle, and saddled it with a saddle with which donkeys are not normally saddled, he is liable by consensus. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:451] 'With which' means, for example, he saddled the donkey with a saddle of a saddle-horse (bardhawn).

This is a concise ruling regarding the liability of a hirer who changes the saddle of a hired donkey. If the hirer removes the saddle that came with the hire and replaces it with a saddle that is not suited for that type of animal (e.g., a horse saddle on a donkey), and the animal is harmed, the hirer is liable for the full value. The commentator notes that this liability is established by consensus (ijma'), meaning there is no disagreement among scholars on this point, because the hirer has clearly violated the terms of the contract by using inappropriate equipment.

Key Terms
السرج (al-saraj): The saddle; equipment placed on the animal for riding.
إجماعا (ijma'an): By consensus; indicating that scholars unanimously agree on the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He is liable only for the cost of the saddle.
D) He is liable only if the donkey dies.

Key Takeaway
A hirer who replaces the saddle with an unsuitable one without permission is liable by consensus, regardless of whether damage actually occurs.

Route Deviation in Ijarah: Liability for Damage
Ruling on taking a different route and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on route deviation in hire contracts to determine whether the hirer is liable for loss.

Core Idea
A hirer is liable only if the alternate route is worse than the contracted one.

In hire contracts, the specified route is a binding condition. This lesson examines the liability of a hirer who deviates from that route. The ruling distinguishes between customary and non-customary routes, and between equivalent and inferior alternatives. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assigning responsibility when goods are damaged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the hirer taking a different route from the one agreed. The ruling is that the hirer may be liable for damage, depending on the nature of the alternate route.
2
Determine the condition for no liability
If the alternate route is one that people commonly use, and there is no difference (tafawut) in terms of roughness, length, or danger, then the hirer is not liable.
The route must be customary and equivalent.
3
Identify the exception that triggers liability
If the alternate route is not customary (not used by people), or if it is customary but there is a significant difference (rougher, longer, or more dangerous), then the hirer is fully liable for the value of the goods.
Tafawut (difference) in safety or distance is key.
4
Apply to scenarios
Consider cases: (a) a driver takes a detour that is equally safe and commonly used – no liability; (b) a driver takes a shorter but more dangerous mountain road – liability applies even if it is used by some.
The same principle applies to modern hire contracts like courier services.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسلوك طريق إلخ عطف على "وبالضرب" أي أن عطبت بسلوك] أي إذا استأجر رجلا ليحمل له متاعا، له الطريق، فأخذ في طريق آخر مما لا يسلكه الناس، فعطب ضمن الكل، فإن كان مما يسلكه الناس فهلك، فلا ضمان عليه إذا لم يكن بين الطريقين تفاوت، أما إذا كان بينهما تفاوت بأن كان أحدهما أوعر أو أبعد أو أخوف مما عينه المالك، ضمن كل قيمته. (ملا مسكين باختصار) وعين
And taking a different road, etc. is attached to 'and for hitting', i.e., that it is destroyed by taking (a different road): meaning if he hired a man to carry goods for him, having the road (specified), and he took another road that is not used by people, and it was destroyed, he guarantees the whole. If it is a road used by people and it was destroyed, there is no guarantee on him if there is no difference between the two roads. However, if there is a difference between them, such that one is rougher or longer or more frightening than what the owner specified, he guarantees its full value. (Mulla Miskin, abbreviated) And specified.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage covers the liability of a hirer who deviates from the specified route. The ruling is: if the hirer takes a path not normally used by people and the goods are destroyed, he is fully liable. If he takes a path that people commonly use and the goods are destroyed, he is not liable provided that there is no difference in danger or distance compared to the agreed route. But if the alternative route is clearly worse (rougher, longer, more dangerous), then he is liable even if people use it. The legal reasoning is that the contract implicitly restricts the route to the one agreed upon or to routes of similar safety and convenience.

Key Terms
سلوك طريق (suluk tariq): Taking a road; deviating from the contracted route.
تفاوت (tafawut): Difference; disparity between the contracted route and the actual route taken in terms of safety, distance, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the route is shorter.
B) If the route is equally safe and not more dangerous.
C) If the hirer informed the owner.
D) If the owner did not specify the route.

Key Takeaway
A hirer is liable for loss only when the alternate route is either non-customary or, if customary, significantly worse than the contracted route.

Carrying Goods by Sea Instead of Land: When the Carrier Violates the Contractual Route
Ruling and commentary on carrier's liability for sea transport when contract specified land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a carrier hired for land carriage transports goods by sea, and apply the condition of taqyid to determine liability.

Core Idea
A carrier who violates a contractual restriction to land guarantees the full value if goods are lost at sea.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding hired carriage (ijara). The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary addresses what happens when a carrier, hired to transport goods on land, instead carries them by sea. The ruling hinges on whether the contract explicitly restricted the method of transport to land. We will analyze the conditions, the liability, and the rationale behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracting parties and the restriction
The hirer (musta'jir) hires a carrier (mukari) to transport goods. The key term is taqyid (restriction): the contract explicitly states carriage must be on land.
If no restriction is mentioned, the carrier may choose the route.
2
Determine the consequence of violation when goods are lost
If the carrier violates the land restriction by taking the sea route and the goods are destroyed, he is liable for the full value of the goods.
The liability is wajib because the risk of sea is greater and the hirer did not consent.
3
Distinguish the safe arrival scenario
If the goods arrive safely at the destination despite the sea route, the carrier is entitled to the full rent.
The rent is earned because the service was completed; the violation does not void the contract's compensation.
4
Understand the rationale and clarify a common misunderstanding
The commentator clarifies that this issue is about damage to the goods, not to the hired animal. The ruling is based on the benefit of the restriction due to sea danger.
This prevents confusion with other fiqh topics about hired animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحمله في البحر الكل، وإن بلغ فله الأجر، وبزرع رطبة وأذن بالبر ما نقص، للمكاري يضمن وقد أذن المؤجر مفعول يضمن ولا أجر، وبخياطة قباء، وأمر بقميص قيمة ثوبه، وله أخذ القباء، ودفع أجر مثله. [ثم شرح:] وحمله في البحر إلخ [بالجر عطف على قوله : "وسلوك" أي ويضمن أيضا بحمله أي بحمل المكاري المتاع. (عيني)] أي إذا استأجر رجلا ليحمل متاعا في البر، فحمله في البحر كما يحمل الناس، وعطب المتاع ضمن الكل، وهذا إذا قيد المستأجر بحمله في البر ; لأن التقييد مفيد بخطر البحر وبندرة السلامة فيه وإن لم يقيد بحمله في البر لا ضمان. واعلم أن هذه المسألة والتي تقدمها في سلوك طريق غير ما عينه ليستا بمتعلقتين بمسائل عطب الدابة المؤجرة كما يوهمه ظاهر كلام المصنف، بل هما متعلقتان بهلاك المتاع، ولهذا فسرهما الشارح ملا مسكين على هذا التفسير المذكور في هذه المسألة ومسألة سلوك طريق غير ما عينه كما قدمناه، فلا تغفل. ولذا قال في "فتح الله المعين على قول الشارح استأجر رجلا ليحمل متاعا إلخ، أشار بهذا التفسير إلى أن حمل كلام المصنف على ظاهره غير صحيح؛ لأن ظاهره أن الدابة عطبت بالحمل في البحر، وهذا لا وجه له فتدبر. (حموي) الكل إلخ: يتعلق بالمسائل المذكورة كلها من قوله وبالضرب إلخ، والتقدير ويضمن الكل أي جميع القيمة؛ لأن الواجب في جميعها جميع القيمة. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٧٦/٢] وإن بلغ إلخ: هذا متعلق بالمسألتين المذكورتين أي إن بلغ المكاري المتاع في هاتين الصورتين سالما إلى الموضع الذي اشترط، فله الأجر، وإنما وجب الأجر لارتفاع الخلاف، ولا يلزم اجتماع الأجر والضمان؛ لأنهما في حالتين. ملتقطا من البحر وغيره)
And carrying it into the sea: the whole; and if it arrives, he gets the rent; and for planting fresh fodder while permission was for wheat: what is diminished; the carrier guarantees; and the owner has permitted is the object of 'guarantees'; and no rent; and for sewing a qaba while he ordered a shirt: the value of his cloth, and he may take the qaba and pay its equivalent rent. Then explanation: 'And carrying it into the sea etc.' is attached to his saying 'and taking' by jar, i.e., he also guarantees by carrying it, i.e., by the carrier carrying the goods. (Ayni) Meaning: if he hired a man to carry goods on land, and he carried it by sea as people carry, and the goods were destroyed, he guarantees the whole; this is if the hirer restricted (the contract) to carrying on land, because the restriction is beneficial due to the danger of the sea and the rarity of safety therein. And if he did not restrict to land, there is no guarantee. And know that this issue and the preceding one regarding taking a different route are not related to issues of destruction of the hired animal as the apparent meaning of the author's words might suggest; rather, they are related to the destruction of the goods. Therefore the commentator Mulla Miskin interpreted them as such. So do not be heedless. Hence it is said in Fath Allah al-Mu'een on the commentator's statement 'he hired a man to carry goods etc.': he indicated by this interpretation that taking the author's words at face value is incorrect, because the apparent meaning is that the animal was destroyed by carrying into the sea, and this has no basis; so ponder. (Hamwi) 'The whole etc.' is connected to all the mentioned issues from his saying 'and for hitting' etc., and the estimated meaning is 'and he guarantees the whole', i.e., the entire value; because the obligation in all of them is the entire value. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:276] 'And if it arrives etc.': this relates to the two mentioned issues, i.e., if the carrier delivers the goods in these two situations safely to the specified place, he gets the rent; and the rent is obligatory because the dispute is removed, and combining rent and guarantee is not required because they are in two different states. (Summarized from al-Bahr and others)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a hirer is contracted to carry goods on land but instead transports them by sea. The ruling distinguishes based on whether the contract explicitly restricted carriage to land. If it did, and the goods are destroyed at sea, the carrier (hirer) is liable for the full value. However, if the goods arrive safely, he is entitled to the full rent, because the risk was assumed. If the contract did not restrict to land, there is no liability for sea carriage. The commentator emphasizes that this issue and the previous one about taking a different route are about damage to the goods, not to the hired animal. This clarifies a common misconception that might arise from the text's placement.

Key Terms
المكاري (al-mukari): The carrier; the person hired to transport goods.
التقييد (al-taqyid): Restriction; a condition placed in the contract, here specifically to carry on land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a carrier to transport goods on land, and the carrier transports them by sea without permission, and the goods sink, what is the ruling?
A) The carrier is not liable if the sea route is commonly used.
B) The carrier is liable for the full value of the goods.
C) The carrier is liable only for half the value.
D) The carrier does not receive any rent but is not liable.

Key Takeaway
A carrier's liability for goods lost at sea depends on whether the contract explicitly restricted carriage to land; if restricted, full value is guaranteed.

Tenant Planting a Different Crop: Harm Determines Ruling
Ruling on planting a more harmful crop than permitted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a tenant plants a different crop than permitted, distinguishing between more harmful and less harmful crops.

Core Idea
Planting a more harmful crop than permitted makes the tenant a usurper: he compensates damage and forfeits rent.

In agricultural leases (ijara), the owner may specify which crop to plant. What happens if the tenant disregards this and plants something else? Hanafi fiqh distinguishes based on the harm level: if the tenant plants a more harmful crop, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and loses the right to rent while being liable for damage; if the crop is less harmful, he remains entitled to rent and owes no compensation. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A tenant hires land for cultivation; the owner permits a specific crop (e.g., wheat). The tenant plants a different crop (e.g., fresh fodder).
The key is whether the planted crop is more or less harmful than the permitted crop.
2
Compare the harm level
Determine if the planted crop is more harmful to the land (e.g., due to root spread, water needs) or less harmful. The text uses ratbah (fresh fodder) as an example of a more harmful crop.
The harm is assessed relative to the permitted crop, not in absolute terms.
3
Apply the ruling
If more harmful: the tenant becomes a usurper (ghasib). He must compensate the owner for the decrease in land value, and is not entitled to any rent. If less harmful: the tenant is not liable for damage and must pay the full agreed rent.
The distinction is based on the contravention of the owner's restriction to a worse condition.
4
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The tenant's act is analogous to usurpation (ghasb) because he occupies the land with a use that is more harmful than permitted, violating the owner's restriction. The ruling follows from the principle that a usurper bears liability and forfeits any claim to compensation.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to the established ruling on usurpation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزرع رطبة إلى صورته أن يستأجر أحد أرضا للزراعة، فأذن المؤجر بزراعة البر، وزرعها المستأجر رطبة، فحينئذ يضمن المستأجر ما نقص من الأرض؛ لأن الرطبة أعظم ضررا من البر؛ لانتشار عروقها وكثرة الحاجة إلى سقيها، فكان خلافا لتقييد المؤجر إلى ما هو شر، فيضمن كما قد مر، ولا أجر؛ لأنه صار غاصبا حيث أشغل الأرض بجنس آخر، وإذا زرع ما هو أقل ضررا فلا ضمان ويجب الأجر. (هكذا في الشروح مع زيادة (توضيح)
And for planting fresh fodder: its scenario is that someone hires land for cultivation, and the owner permits planting wheat, but the tenant plants fresh fodder (ratbah). Then the tenant guarantees what is diminished from the land, because fresh fodder is more harmful than wheat, due to the spreading of its roots and the greater need for watering. So it is a violation of the owner's restriction to something more harmful, so he guarantees as previously, and no rent; because he has become a usurper since he occupied the land with a different type. And if he plants something less harmful, there is no guarantee and the rent is obligatory. (Thus in the commentaries with additional clarification)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This ruling addresses the scenario of a hired agricultural land where the owner permitted a specific crop (wheat), but the tenant plants a different, more harmful crop (ratbah, fresh fodder). The ruling is that the tenant must compensate for the damage caused to the land (the reduction in value due to the harmful crop) and is not entitled to any rent because his act amounts to usurpation (ghasb). The rationale is that ratbah has more extensive roots and requires more water, thus harming the land more than wheat. Conversely, if the tenant plants a crop that is less harmful than the permitted one, he does not compensate and must pay the full rent.

Key Terms
الرطبة (al-ratbah): Fresh fodder (green forage), a crop considered more damaging to soil due to its root system and water needs.
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; one who wrongfully takes possession of another's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A tenant is allowed to plant wheat but instead plants a crop that is less harmful to the land. What is the ruling?
A) He must compensate for any damage and pays no rent.
B) He is not liable for damage and must pay the full rent.
C) He is exempt from rent but must compensate.
D) The contract becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on unauthorized crop change hinges on harm: more harmful = usurper (no rent + damage); less harmful = rent due, no damage liability.

Tailor Makes a Different Garment: Owner's Options
Ruling on owner's khiyar for a tailor's deviation to a similar garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the cloth owner when a tailor makes a different garment and apply the rule of ajr al-mithl in a fasid ijara contract.

Core Idea
When a tailor deviates but the garment is similar in benefit, the owner chooses between compensation and acceptance with fair hire.

What happens when you give cloth to a tailor with clear instructions, but he returns something different? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling when the tailor makes a qaba instead of a shirt. The law recognizes partial conformity and grants the owner a choice, balancing the tailor's breach with the garment's utility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the breach
Recognize this as an ijara (hire) contract where the tailor acted contrary to the owner's order. The owner gave cloth and specified a shirt; the tailor made a qaba.
The contract becomes fasid (voidable) due to the deviation, but the owner may still ratify it.
2
State the owner's two options
The owner may either (1) reject the qaba and claim the full value of his cloth, or (2) accept the qaba and pay ajr al-mithl (fair hire), capped by the agreed wage.
Ajr al-mithl is the market rate for similar work, not exceeding the named dirhams.
3
Analyze the rational proof (qiyas)
The ruling is based on the similarity of benefit: a qaba is used like a shirt (both cover the body). Thus there is partial conformity, justifying the option.
The illa is the unity of basic benefit: covering and protection from heat and cold.
4
Extend to other garments (trousers)
The same ruling applies if the tailor makes trousers (sirwal), according to the most sound opinion, because the basic benefit is common.
This extension is supported by al-Fath and relies on the same illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبخياطة قباء إلخ : أي دفع رجل ثوبا إلى خياط، وأمره أن يخيطه قميصا بدرهم فخاطه قباء، وعمل بخلاف قوله، فلرب الثوب الخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمة ثوبه، وترك القباء، وإن شاء أخذ القباء ودفع أجر مثله؛ لأنهما متقاربان في المنفعة؛ لأن القباء بقد وسطه ينتفع به انتفاع القميص، ففيه الموافقة والمخالفة، فيميل إلى أي الجهتين شاء، لكن في صورة دفع الأجر يجب أجر المثل؛ لقصور جهة الموافقة ولا يجاوز به الدراهم المسماة كما هو حكم الإجارة الفاسدة، قال في "الفتح": وكذا إذا خاطه سراويل في الأصح للاتحاد في أصل المنفعة من حيث الستر ودفع الحر والبرد "حموى" والقباء ما تلبسه الأتراك مكان القميص فارسي معرب. (ملخصا)
And for sewing a qaba etc.: meaning a man gave a cloth to a tailor and ordered him to sew it as a shirt for a dirham, but he sewed it as a qaba, and acted contrary to his statement. The owner of the cloth has the choice: if he wishes, he can hold him liable for the value of his cloth and leave the qaba; and if he wishes, he can take the qaba and pay its equivalent hire. Because the two are close in benefit; because the qaba, with its slit in the middle, is used like a shirt. So there is both conformity and opposition, and he may incline to whichever side he wants. But in the case of paying the hire, the equivalent hire (ajr al-mithl) is obligatory, due to the deficiency in the aspect of conformity, and it does not exceed the named dirhams as is the rule of a fasid (voidable) lease. It is said in al-Fath: Similarly, if he sewed it as a sirwal (trousers), according to the most sound opinion, because of the unity in the basic benefit in terms of covering and protection from heat and cold. (Hamwi) And qaba is what the Turks wear in place of a shirt, a Persian word arabicized. (Summarized)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when a tailor makes a garment different from what was ordered. The owner of the cloth has two options: (1) He can reject the incorrect garment and claim the full value of his cloth from the tailor (daman). (2) He can accept the qaba (the garment made) and pay the tailor the fair market hire (ajr al-mithl) for his work, but not exceeding the agreed price (one dirham). This is because the qaba and shirt are similar in utility, so there is partial conformity. The option belongs to the owner because the tailor has acted contrary to instructions. The commentator adds that this ruling also applies if the tailor makes trousers (sirwal) instead, according to the most sound opinion, as the basic benefit of covering is common. The term 'qaba' is identified as a Turkish garment akin to a shirt.

Key Terms
القباء (al-qaba): A type of outer garment with a slit in the middle, similar to a shirt, commonly worn by Turks.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market hire; the usual wage for similar work.
الخيار (al-khiyar): The right to choose between alternatives; here the owner's option to either claim damages or accept the garment and pay ajr al-mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A tailor is asked to sew a shirt from a cloth but instead sews a qaba. The owner chooses to take the qaba. What must he pay?
A) The agreed price of one dirham.
B) The market value of the qaba.
C) The equivalent hire (ajr al-mithl) for tailoring, not exceeding the named wage.
D) Nothing, because the tailor did the wrong job.

Key Takeaway
When a tailor deviates to a similar garment, the owner has a choice: either claim cloth value or accept the garment and pay fair hire capped at the agreed wage.

Carrier's Liability When Deviating from Agreed Route
Ruling on carrier's liability when deviating from the agreed route

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a hired carrier deviates from the agreed route, and apply the rule that guarantee and wage do not combine.

Core Idea
Deviation from contract terms makes the carrier a guarantor for lost goods, forfeiting the wage.

In ijarah, the carrier (makkari) is an ajir bound to the specified route or mode of transport. If he departs from this, he breaches the contract. This lesson explains the consequence: either he is liable for the full value if goods are lost, or he gets the wage if they arrive safely—but never both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the carrier carrying goods by sea instead of the agreed land route. The ruling: if goods are lost, he guarantees the full value; if they arrive safely, he receives the wage.
The ruling is conditional on the outcome of the goods.
2
Determine the condition that triggers the ruling
The condition is the deviation (taghyir al-tariq). This breach of the contract's terms changes the carrier's status from a mere ajir to a dāmin (guarantor) in case of loss.
Deviation must be without the owner's consent.
3
Apply the ruling to the two scenarios
Scenario 1: goods lost → carrier must pay full value (damān) and earns no wage. Scenario 2: goods safe → carrier gets the wage, and the contract is fulfilled despite the deviation.
The wage is earned only if the service is completed (goods reach safely).
4
Understand the underlying principle
The principle: guarantee (damān) and wage (ujrah) do not combine when the carrier breaches the contract. Once he deviates, he takes on the risk; if loss occurs, he compensates and forfeits his wage.
This is based on the idea that the deviation nullifies the original contract's protection.
5
Distinguish from related issues
The commentary clarifies that this ruling concerns loss of the goods themselves, not destruction of the hired animal. Confusing the two is a common misunderstanding.
The author warns against misinterpreting the text as applying to animal injury.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحمله في البحر الكل، وإن بلغ فله الأجر، ... [لأن الضمان والأجر لا يجتمعان والحال أنه قد أمر يضمن قيمة ثوبه لرب الثوب] واعلم أن هذه المسألة والتي تقدمها في سلوك طريق غير ما عينه ليستا بمتعلقتين بمسائل عطب الدابة المؤجرة كما يوهمه ظاهر كلام المصنف، بل هما متعلقتان بهلاك المتاع، ولهذا فسرهما الشارح ملا مسكين على هذا التفسير المذكور في هذه المسألة ومسألة سلوك طريق غير ما عينه كما قدمناه، فلا تغفل. ولذا قال في "فتح الله المعين على قول الشارح استأجر رجلا ليحمل متاعا إلخ، أشار بهذا التفسير إلى أن حمل كلام المصنف على ظاهره غير صحيح؛ لأن ظاهره أن الدابة عطبت بالحمل في البحر، وهذا لا وجه له. فتدبر. (حموي)
And his carrying it in the sea: (he guarantees) the whole, and if it reaches (safely), then he has the wage. ... Know that this issue and the one preceding it about taking a road other than the one specified are not related to issues of the hired animal being ruined as the apparent meaning of the author’s words suggests; rather, they are related to the destruction of the goods. ...
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on ijarah regarding a carrier (makkari) who is hired to transport goods by land but instead carries them by sea. The passage clarifies that if the goods are lost, he guarantees the full value because he deviated from the agreed terms; if they arrive safely, he is entitled to the wage. The commentary emphasizes that this ruling concerns loss of the goods themselves, not destruction of the hired animal. The author cautions against misunderstanding the text, which might be misinterpreted as referring to the animal's death.

Key Terms
مكاري (makkārī): A person hired to carry goods or transport items, often with animals.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage; guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a carrier hired for land transport carries goods by sea and the goods are lost?
A) He guarantees only part of the value
B) He guarantees the full value and loses the wage
C) He does not guarantee anything but loses the wage
D) He guarantees the full value but still gets the wage if he completes the journey

Key Takeaway
A carrier who deviates from the agreed route becomes a guarantor: if goods are lost, he must pay full value and forgoes the wage; if goods arrive safely, he receives the wage.

Lessee Planting Unauthorized Crop: Guarantee and Wage
Ruling on lessee planting a different crop

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a lessee who plants a crop different from the lessor's authorization, distinguishing between more harmful and less harmful crops and the consequences for guarantee and wage.

Core Idea
Planting a more harmful crop than authorized makes the lessee a usurper — he must compensate and forfeits his wage.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in lease of agricultural land: when the lessor authorizes one crop and the lessee plants another. The Hanafi school sets a clear rule based on harm: if the planted crop is more harmful, the lessee is treated as a usurper (ghasib) and must guarantee any loss in land value while losing his wage; if less harmful, he is entitled to the wage and owes no compensation. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the principles of lease contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authorized and planted crop
Determine what crop the lessor allowed and what the lessee actually planted. This sets the baseline for comparison.
The authorization is a condition of the lease; deviation may breach the contract.
2
Compare the harm of the planted crop to the authorized one
Assess whether the planted crop causes more damage to the land (e.g., deeper roots, more water consumption). The Hanafi ruling hinges on this comparison.
Alfalfa is considered more harmful than wheat due to spreading roots and high water needs.
3
Determine if the lessee becomes a usurper
If the planted crop is more harmful, the lessee is treated as a ghāṣib because he used the land in a way not permitted, exceeding the authorization.
A ghāṣib is strictly liable and cannot claim compensation for his work.
4
Apply the consequence for guarantee and wage
If more harmful: lessee guarantees any deficiency in land value and receives no wage. If less harmful: no guarantee and wage is obligatory.
This follows the principle that unauthorized beneficial use that harms the owner triggers liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزرع رطبة وأذن بالبر ما نقص، [لأن الرطبة أعظم ضررا من البر؛ لانتشار عروقها وكثرة الحاجة إلى سقيها، فكان خلافا لتقييد المؤجر إلى ما هو شر، فيضمن كما قد مر، ولا أجر؛ لأنه صار غاصبا حيث أشغل الأرض بجنس آخر، وإذا زرع ما هو أقل ضررا فلا ضمان ويجب الأجر.]
And with planting alfalfa while (the lessor) authorized wheat: whatever deficiency (occurs), he guarantees; because alfalfa is more harmful than wheat due to the spreading of its roots and greater need for watering, so it is contrary to the lessor's restriction to something worse, so he guarantees as previously mentioned, and there is no wage; because he became a usurper (ghasib) by occupying the land with another type. And if he plants something less harmful, there is no guarantee and the wage is obligatory.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This ruling deals with a lease of land for cultivation. If the lessor specifies a crop (e.g., wheat) and the lessee plants a different, more harmful crop (e.g., alfalfa), the lessee must compensate for any reduction in the land's value and receives no wage for his work. He is considered a usurper (ghasib) because he used the land contrary to permission. Conversely, if he plants a less harmful crop, he is not liable and is entitled to the wage.

Key Terms
غاصب (ghāṣib): One who unlawfully takes possession of property; a usurper.
رطبة (raṭbah): Alfalfa or a similar crop with deep roots that damages land more than grains.
بر (burr): Wheat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lessor authorizes wheat cultivation and the lessee plants alfalfa (which is more harmful), what is the ruling?
A) The lessee gets the full wage and no guarantee
B) The lessee must guarantee the deficiency but gets the wage
C) The lessee must guarantee the deficiency and receives no wage
D) The lessee is not liable nor entitled to wage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi lease law, a lessee who plants a more harmful crop than authorized must guarantee the land's deficiency and receives no wage; planting a less harmful crop avoids liability and entitles him to the wage.

Tailor Makes a Different Garment: Owner's Option in Fasid Ijarah
Ruling on owner's option when tailor deviates to a similar garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the owner's two options when a tailor deviates from instructions and explain why the ruling depends on similarity of benefit.

Core Idea
When a tailor makes a different but similar garment, the owner may choose between taking it with fair wage or claiming cloth value.

Imagine you give a tailor cloth and order a shirt for a fixed price, but he sews a cloak instead. Is the contract void? Do you have to pay? The Hanafi school gives you a choice, based on whether the garments serve a similar purpose. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and the breach
Recognize that a valid contract of ijarah (hiring for work) was formed, but the tailor deviated from the express order. This makes the contract fasid (defective) because the work performed does not match the specification.
The cloth owner's order is a condition; violation makes the contract invalid in terms of the agreed work.
2
State the owner's two options
The owner may either: (1) hold the tailor liable for the cloth's value and refuse the qaba, or (2) accept the qaba and pay the tailor the fair market wage (ajr al-mithl) for making it.
These are mutually exclusive – the owner cannot both keep the garment and claim full compensation.
3
Understand the rationale: similarity in benefit
The option exists because a shirt and a qaba are similar in benefit – both cover the body and protect against heat and cold. The qaba is like a shirt with an opening. This principle extends to other garments like trousers.
If the garments were not similar (e.g., a shirt vs. a coat), the owner would have the right to reject the garment entirely and claim full compensation.
4
Apply the fasid ijarah rule on wages
If the owner chooses to keep the qaba, he must pay ajr al-mithl (fair wage) but not exceeding the named wage (1 dirham). This limitation comes from the rule of fasid ijarah: the customary wage is due, capped by the agreed price.
The named wage acts as a ceiling to prevent the owner from being charged more than originally agreed.
5
Extend to other cases
Al-Fatḥ (al-Hindī) states that the same ruling applies if the tailor makes trousers, since trousers also share the essential benefit of covering and protecting. The key is unity in the core benefit.
The extension is based on the same illa (effective cause) of similar utility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبخياطة قباء إلخ : أي دفع رجل ثوبا إلى خياط، وأمره أن يخيطه قميصا بدرهم فخاطه قباء، وعمل بخلاف قوله، فلرب الثوب الخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمة ثوبه، وترك القباء، وإن شاء أخذ القباء ودفع أجر مثله؛ لأنهما متقاربان في المنفعة؛ لأن القباء بقد وسطه ينتفع به انتفاع القميص، ففيه الموافقة والمخالفة، فيميل إلى أي الجهتين شاء، لكن في صورة دفع الأجر يجب أجر المثل؛ لقصور جهة الموافقة ولا يجاوز به الدراهم المسماة كما هو حكم الإجارة الفاسدة، قال في "الفتح": وكذا إذا خاطه سراويل في الأصح للاتحاد في أصل المنفعة من حيث الستر ودفع الحر والبرد "حموى" والقباء ما تلبسه الأتراك مكان القميص فارسي معرب. (ملخصا)
And with tailoring a qaba (cloak): i.e., a man gave cloth to a tailor and ordered him to sew it as a shirt for a dirham, but he sewed it as a qaba (cloak), acting contrary to his statement. So the owner of the cloth has the option: if he wishes, he can hold him liable for the value of his cloth and leave the qaba; if he wishes, he can take the qaba and pay its like wage. Because the two are similar in benefit; since the qaba, with its waist opening, benefits like the shirt. So there is both agreement and disagreement, and he may incline to whichever side he wishes. But in the case of paying the wage, the like wage is obligatory due to the deficiency of the agreement side, and it does not exceed the named dirhams as is the ruling for a fasid ijarah.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This is a ruling on a tailor who disobeys orders by making a different garment (qaba instead of shirt). The owner has a choice: either demand compensation for the cloth and keep the qaba, or accept the qaba and pay the tailor the fair wage (ajr al-mithl), limited to the agreed-upon price because the contract is fasid. The similarity in benefit (both cover and protect against heat/cold) allows the option. The same applies if he makes trousers instead.

Key Terms
قباء (qabāʾ): A cloak or outer garment, usually open and worn over other clothes.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for the work done, not the agreed price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a tailor, ordered to make a shirt for 1 dirham, makes a qaba (cloak) instead?
A) The tailor must compensate the full value of the cloth and return the qaba
B) The owner can only take the qaba and pay the named wage
C) The owner may either claim the cloth value and leave the qaba, or take the qaba and pay the like wage
D) The tailor gets no wage and must pay the cloth value

Key Takeaway
When a tailor deviates to a similar garment, the owner may choose to either take the garment and pay a fair wage (capped at the agreed price) or claim compensation for the cloth and refuse the garment.
