Definition and Ruling of Fasid Ijarah
Definition and general ruling of fasid ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fasid ijarah, distinguish it from batil ijarah, state the ruling of ajr al-mithl, and identify the conditions that render an ijarah contract fasid.

Core Idea
An ijarah is fasid when valid in essence but flawed in description; hirer must pay ajr al-mithl after actual use.

Having completed the discussion of valid ijarah, the text now turns to invalid ijarah. The author explains why this chapter follows naturally, and clarifies the critical distinction between fasid (invalid) and batil (void) contracts—a distinction unique to the Hanafi school in mu'amalat. This lesson will parse the definition of fasid ijarah, its ruling (ajr al-mithl), and the conditions that cause it.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the three categories
Understand that ijarah can be sahih (valid), fasid (invalid), or batil (void). Fasid is valid in essence but flawed in description; batil is not valid at all in essence or description.
The text explicitly states: 'fasid is legislated in its essence but not in its description; batil is not legislated at all.'
2
Identify the ruling of fasid ijarah
The ruling for fasid ijarah is wajib: the hirer must pay ajr al-mithl (like wage) only after actually benefiting from the service. Mere ability to use does not obligate payment, unlike valid ijarah where payment is due upon availability.
This difference from valid ijarah is critical: ajr al-mithl is due 'after delivery and actual utilization of the benefit.'
3
Recognize the conditions causing fasid
According to Al-Karkhi's summary, any fundamental ignorance (jahalah) in the thing hired, wage, duration, or work makes the ijarah fasid. Additionally, stipulating extra conditions that are not from the requirements of the contract (e.g., plastering the house, repairing, planting trees) also invalidates.
Not every condition invalidates; conditions that are part of the contract's inherent requirements (like payment upon return) do not cause fasid.
4
Apply the key distinction from fasid sale
In fasid sale, taking possession transfers ownership; the buyer can sell the item. In fasid ijarah, taking possession does not transfer ownership of the benefit; the hirer cannot sub-lease without incurring liability for ajr al-mithl, and the original lessor can cancel the contract.
This practical difference: the hirer is not a usurper (ghasib) but also does not own the benefit by possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإجارة الفاسدة: [ أخرها عن الصحيحة؛ لأن الأصل في عقود أهل الإسلام الصحة. (فتح)] لما فرغ من بيان الإجارة الصحيحة شرع في بيان الفاسدة، وفي بيان ما يكون مفسدا، ولا يخفى أن ذكر الإجارة الفاسدة بعد صحيحها لا يحتاج إلى معذرة، فهي في محلها، وعبر بالفاسد دون الباطل مع أنه مشتمل على الفاسد والباطل؛ لكثرة فروعه. واعلم أن الإجارة والبيع سيان في كونهما صحيحا وفاسدا وباطلا، فالإجارة الصحيحة كالبيع ما يكون مشروعا بأصله ووصفه، والإجارة الفاسدة يكون مشروعا بأصله دون وصفه وحكمه وجوب أجر المثل، والباطلة ما لم تكن مشروعة أصلا، وحكمه أنه لا أجر فيه لكن في الإجارة الفاسدة والبيع الفاسد فرق فإن الفاسد من البيع يملك بالقبض، والفاسد من الإجارة لا يملك المنافع بالقبض حتى لو قبضها المستأجر ليس له أن يؤاجر، ولو آجرها وجب أجر المثل، ولا يكون غاصبا، وللآجر الأول أن ينقض هذه الإجارة. (ملتقط عن البحر وغيره بتوضيح) الشرط: أي الشروط المعهودة المتقدمة في باب البيع الفاسد التي ليست من مقتضى العقد لا كل شرط؛ لأن الإجارة عقد معاوضة محضة تقال وتفسخ، فكانت كالبيع، فكل ما أفسد البيع أفسدها، وقد ضبطه الشيخ أبو الحسن الكرخي في "مختصره"، فقال: إذا كان ما وقع عليه عقد الإجارة مجهولا في نفسه أو في أجرة أو في مدة الإجارة أو في العمل المستأجر عليه، فالإجارة فاسدة وكل جهالة تدخل في البيع، فتفسده من جهة الجهالة، فكذلك هي في الإجارة [رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۷/۲] والشروط التي تفسدها تفصيلا كاشتراط تطيين الدار ،ومرمتها أو تعليق باب عليها، أو إدخال جذع على المستأجر، وكذا اشتراط كري نهر في الأرض، أو ضرب مسناة عليها أو حفر بئر فيها، أو أن يسرقنها على المستأجر، وكذلك اشتراط رد الأرض المكروبة، وكذا لو شرط إن انقطع الماء عن الرحى، فالأجر عليه، وكذا إن تكارى دابة إلى بغداد على أنه إن رزق شيئا أعطاه أو إن بلغت بغداد فله كذا، وإلا فلا شيء له، فهي فاسدة، وعليه أجر مثل ما سار عليها، وكذا لو استأجر عبدا شهرا على أنه إن مرض فيه عمل في الشهر الذي بعده بقدر الأيام التي مرض فيها، كذا في غاية البيان"، فخرج من الشروط المفسدة ما يقتضيه العقد كاشتراط يدفع له الأجر إذا رجع من السفر. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥٣/٧] أجر مثله إلخ: أي بعد التسليم واستيفاء المستأجر المنفعة؛ لأن الأجر في الفاسد لا يجب بمجرد التمكن بل لابد من وجود الاستيفاء بالفعل، بخلاف الإجارة حيث يكفي لوجوب المسمى مجرد التمكن فتح باختصار"، أقول: وينبغي يستثني من هذه القاعدة أي كون أجر المثل في الإجارة الفاسدة للآجر الإجارات التي تنعقد فاسدة ابتداء، ثم تنقلب صحيحة، وإن لم يصرحوا به كما سيأتي بعض صورها، فإن فيها للآجر المسمى.
Chapter on Invalid Ijarah: ... Now that he has completed explaining the valid ijarah, he begins explaining the invalid, and explaining what renders it invalid. ... Know that ijarah and sale are alike in being valid, invalid, and void. A valid ijarah, like sale, is that which is legislated in its essence and description. An invalid (fasid) ijarah is legislated in its essence but not in its description, and its ruling is the obligation of the like wage (ajr al-mithl). A void (batil) ijarah is not legislated at all, and its ruling is that there is no wage. ... The condition: i.e., the known conditions previously mentioned in the chapter on invalid sale that are not from the requirements of the contract, not every condition. ... The conditions that invalidate it in detail: such as stipulating the plastering of the house, its repair, or hanging a door, or inserting a beam on the lessee, etc.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This is the beginning of the chapter on invalid ijarah. The author explains why it is placed after valid ijarah, and defines terms: fasid (invalid) vs. batil (void). A fasid ijarah is valid in its essence (the contract is for hire) but flawed in some condition. The ruling for fasid ijarah is that the hirer must pay the like wage (ajr al-mithl) after actually benefiting from the service. The key conditions that invalidate it are any fundamental ignorance (jahalah) in the thing hired, wage, duration, or work. The passage lists specific examples like stipulating the lessor must plaster the house, plant trees, etc. The wage in fasid ijarah is due only after actual use, not upon mere ability to use, unlike valid ijarah.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A contract of hire that is valid in its essence but flawed in its description (e.g., due to ignorance of a key term). Its ruling is wajib to pay ajr al-mithl after use.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for the service rendered, as opposed to the wage named in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The contract is void and no wage is due
B) The hirer must pay the named wage whether he uses the service or not
C) The hirer must pay the like wage after actually using the service
D) The contract becomes valid after possession

Key Takeaway
Fasid ijarah requires ajr al-mithl after actual use; the contract is not void but flawed in description, and the hirer does not own the benefit by possession.

Definition and Ruling of Fasid Ijara
Definition and ruling of fasid ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a fasid ijara, state its ruling (wajib of ujr al-mithl), and distinguish it from valid and batil ijara.

Core Idea
A fasid ijara is valid in principle but invalid in description; compensation is ujr al-mithl.

The Hanafi school classifies contracts into valid (sahih), voidable (fasid), and void (batil). This lesson focuses on the fasid ijara, where the essential elements are present but a condition renders it defective. The key ruling is that if the benefit is used, the lessee must pay ujr al-mithl (market rate), not the named wage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Distinguish valid (sahih), fasid, and batil based on the contract's principle (asl) and description (wasf).
2
Understand the definition of fasid
A fasid contract is legislated in its principle (asl) but not in its description (wasf).
This means its essential elements are present, but a condition makes it defective.
3
Note the ruling: ujr al-mithl
For a fasid ijara, if the benefit is used, the lessee must pay ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage), not the named wage.
The named wage is not enforceable due to the defect.
4
Compare with valid and batil
Valid ijara has both asl and wasf; batil ijara has neither; fasid has asl but not wasf.
This is parallel to sale in categorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يفسد الإجارة الشرط، وله أجر مثله. باب الإجارة الفاسدة: [ أخرها عن الصحيحة؛ لأن الأصل في عقود أهل الإسلام الصحة. (فتح)] لما فرغ من بيان الإجارة الصحيحة شرع في بيان الفاسدة، وفي بيان ما يكون مفسدا، ولا يخفى أن ذكر الإجارة الفاسدة بعد صحيحها لا يحتاج إلى معذرة، فهي في محلها، وعبر بالفاسد دون الباطل مع أنه مشتمل على الفاسد والباطل؛ لكثرة فروعه. واعلم أن الإجارة والبيع سيان في كونهما صحيحا وفاسدا وباطلا، فالإجارة الصحيحة كالبيع ما يكون مشروعا بأصله ووصفه، والإجارة الفاسدة يكون مشروعا بأصله دون وصفه وحكمه وجوب أجر المثل، والباطلة ما لم تكن مشروعة أصلا، وحكمه أنه لا أجر فيه لكن في الإجارة الفاسدة والبيع الفاسد فرق فإن الفاسد من البيع يملك بالقبض، والفاسد من الإجارة لا يملك المنافع بالقبض حتى لو قبضها المستأجر ليس له أن يؤاجر، ولو آجرها وجب أجر المثل، ولا يكون غاصبا، وللآجر الأول أن ينقض هذه الإجارة. (ملتقط عن البحر وغيره بتوضيح)
Conditions invalidate the lease, and there is for him its equivalent wage. Chapter of Invalid Lease: [He mentioned it after the valid one because the basis in contracts of Muslims is validity. (Fath)] After finishing the explanation of valid lease, he began explaining the invalid one, and explaining what invalidates it, and it is not hidden that mentioning the invalid lease after the valid one does not need an excuse, so it is in its proper place. He used 'fasid' (voidable) instead of 'batil' (void) even though it includes both fasid and batil, because of the abundance of its subsidiary branches. Know that lease and sale are equal in being valid, voidable, and void. So valid lease like valid sale is that which is legislated in its principle and description. Invalid lease is that which is legislated in its principle but not in its description, and its ruling is the obligation of the equivalent wage. Void lease is that which is not legislated at all, and its ruling is that there is no wage in it. But there is a difference between voidable lease and voidable sale: the voidable in sale becomes owned by possession, while the voidable in lease does not own the benefits by possession, so even if the lessee takes possession, he may not sublease; if he does sublease, the equivalent wage is obligatory, and he is not a usurper, and the first lessor can rescind this lease. (Summarized from Al-Bahr and others with clarification).
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage defines the three categories of lease (valid, voidable, void) and compares lease with sale. The matn states that conditions invalidate the lease and the compensation is ujr al-mithl. The commentator explains why the chapter is placed after valid lease: the principle is validity, so first valid is taught, then the exception. He uses 'fasid' because it covers both fasid and batil in practice due to many sub-branches. Lease and sale are analogous in categories. However, a key difference: in sale, a fasid contract transfers ownership upon taking possession (qabd), whereas in lease, the lessee does not own the benefits by possession alone; if he subleases, he must pay ujr al-mithl but is not a usurper, and the original lessor can cancel the sublease. This distinction arises because benefits (manafi') are not considered substantive property independent of contract in the same way as physical objects.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A lease contract that is valid in its principle (asl) but invalid in its description (wasf), requiring ujr al-mithl
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent wage or market rate for the benefit, not the named wage
شبهة العقد (shubhat al-aqd): A semblance or appearance of a valid contract that gives some legal effect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on compensation in a fasid ijara (voidable lease) according to the Hanafi school?
A) The named wage (musamma) is due.
B) No compensation is due.
C) The equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl) is due.
D) Compensation is at the discretion of the lessor.

Key Takeaway
A fasid ijara is valid in principle but defective in description; compensation is wajib as ujr al-mithl, not the named wage.

Fasid Bay' vs Fasid Ijara: The Effect of Possession
Comparison between fasid sale and fasid lease on possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the key difference between a voidable sale and a voidable lease concerning ownership by possession and apply it to subleasing scenarios.

Core Idea
Possession of a fasid sale transfers ownership; possession of a fasid lease does not transfer ownership of benefits.

Although lease and sale are parallel in their tripartite categorization, their legal effects differ when the contract is fasid. In a fasid sale, taking possession (qabd) transfers ownership of the item, enabling the buyer to dispose of it. In a fasid lease, possession does not confer ownership of the benefits; the lessee may not sublease without the owner's consent. If he does, he must pay ujr al-mithl, yet he is not considered a usurper, and the original lessor retains the right to rescind the sublease.

Guided Path
1
Recall the common categorization
Both sale and ijara share the same three categories: valid, fasid, batil.
2
Learn the rule for fasid bay'
In a voidable sale, possession (qabd) results in ownership of the sold item. The buyer can dispose of it freely.
This is based on the principle that qabd in sale transfers property.
3
Learn the rule for fasid ijara
In a voidable lease, possession does not transfer ownership of the benefits. The lessee cannot sublease; if he does, the sublease is not binding on the original lessor.
Benefits (manafi') are not owned by possession alone.
4
Analyse the sublease scenario
If the lessee subleases, he must pay ujr al-mithl to the sublessee, but he is not a usurper. The original lessor can rescind the sublease.
The lessor's right to rescind shows the original lease remains not fully transferable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح)] لما فرغ من بيان الإجارة الصحيحة شرع في بيان الفاسدة، وفي بيان ما يكون مفسدا، ولا يخفى أن ذكر الإجارة الفاسدة بعد صحيحها لا يحتاج إلى معذرة، فهي في محلها، وعبر بالفاسد دون الباطل مع أنه مشتمل على الفاسد والباطل؛ لكثرة فروعه. واعلم أن الإجارة والبيع سيان في كونهما صحيحا وفاسدا وباطلا، فالإجارة الصحيحة كالبيع ما يكون مشروعا بأصله ووصفه، والإجارة الفاسدة يكون مشروعا بأصله دون وصفه وحكمه وجوب أجر المثل، والباطلة ما لم تكن مشروعة أصلا، وحكمه أنه لا أجر فيه لكن في الإجارة الفاسدة والبيع الفاسد فرق فإن الفاسد من البيع يملك بالقبض، والفاسد من الإجارة لا يملك المنافع بالقبض حتى لو قبضها المستأجر ليس له أن يؤاجر، ولو آجرها وجب أجر المثل، ولا يكون غاصبا، وللآجر الأول أن ينقض هذه الإجارة. Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of the subject matter
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A voidable sale valid in principle but defective in description
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation; taking property unlawfully

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a lessee under a fasid lease subleases the property without permission?
A) The sublease is valid and binding on the original lessor.
B) The sublease is void; the lessee is a usurper.
C) The sublease is not binding on the original lessor; the lessee pays ujr al-mithl and the original lessor can rescind.
D) The sublease is valid only if the lessee pays the original lessor the named wage.

Key Takeaway
The effect of possession differs fundamentally between fasid sale and fasid lease: sale transfers ownership, lease does not.

Invalidating Conditions in Ijara Contracts
Listing invalidating conditions and ruling for fasid ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify conditions that invalidate an ijara contract and state the consequence (ujr al-mithl) for fasid leases.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in object, rent, duration, or work invalidates the lease; lessee pays market rate after using the benefit.

This passage draws an analogy between sale and lease: conditions that invalidate sale due to uncertainty also invalidate ijara. The Hanafi jurist Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi codified the principle: if the leased item, rent, duration, or work is unknown, the contract is fasid. Several illustrative examples follow, along with the critical exception for conditions inherent in the contract (muqtada al-aqd).

Guided Path
1
Grasp the General Principle
Understand that ijara is a commutative contract like sale; therefore, uncertainty (jahala) that would invalidate a sale also invalidates a lease. Identify the four key areas of uncertainty: object, rent, duration, and work.
This principle is stated by al-Karkhi and is foundational for the examples.
2
Analyze the Examples of Invalidating Conditions
Go through each example in the text: stipulating additional work (plastering, repairing, digging), conditional rent based on outcomes, or extra obligations on the lessee. Note that each introduces uncertainty.
3
Distinguish Valid Conditions from Invalid Ones
Conditions that are part of the contract's inherent requirements (muqtada al-aqd), such as paying rent upon return from travel, do not invalidate. Learn to identify what is integral to the lease.
This distinction is critical for correct application.
4
Apply the Consequence of Invalidity
If the lease is fasid, the named rent is void, and ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) is due only after the lessee actually uses the service or benefit. This differs from a valid lease where the named rent is due upon mere ability.
Note the exception: leases that start fasid but later become valid confer the named rent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط: أي الشروط المعهودة المتقدمة في باب البيع الفاسد التي ليست من مقتضى العقد لا كل شرط؛ لأن الإجارة عقد معاوضة محضة تقال وتفسخ، فكانت كالبيع، فكل ما أفسد البيع أفسدها، وقد ضبطه الشيخ أبو الحسن الكرخي في "مختصره"، فقال: إذا كان ما وقع عليه عقد الإجارة مجهولا في نفسه أو في أجرة أو في مدة الإجارة أو في العمل المستأجر عليه، فالإجارة فاسدة وكل جهالة تدخل في البيع، فتفسده من جهة الجهالة، فكذلك هي في الإجارة [رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۷/۲] والشروط التي تفسدها تفصيلا كاشتراط تطيين الدار ،ومرمتها أو تعليق باب عليها، أو إدخال جذع على المستأجر، وكذا اشتراط كري نهر في الأرض، أو ضرب مسناة عليها أو حفر بئر فيها، أو أن يسرقنها على المستأجر، وكذلك اشتراط رد الأرض المكروبة، وكذا لو شرط إن انقطع الماء عن الرحى، فالأجر عليه، وكذا إن تكارى دابة إلى بغداد على أنه إن رزق شيئا أعطاه أو إن بلغت بغداد فله كذا، وإلا فلا شيء له، فهي فاسدة، وعليه أجر مثل ما سار عليها، وكذا لو استأجر عبدا شهرا على أنه إن مرض فيه عمل في الشهر الذي بعده بقدر الأيام التي مرض فيها، كذا في غاية البيان", فخرج من الشروط المفسدة ما يقتضيه العقد كاشتراط يدفع له الأجر إذا رجع من السفر. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥٣/٧] أجر مثله إلخ: أي بعد التسليم واستيفاء المستأجر المنفعة؛ لأن الأجر في الفاسد لا يجب بمجرد التمكن بل لابد من وجود الاستيفاء بالفعل، بخلاف الإجارة حيث يكفي لوجوب المسمى مجرد التمكن فتح باختصار", أقول: وينبغي يستثني من هذه القاعدة أي كون أجر المثل في الإجارة الفاسدة للآجر الإجارات التي تنعقد فاسدة ابتداء، ثم تنقلب صحيحة، وإن لم يصرحوا به كما سيأتي بعض صورها، فإن فيها للآجر المسمى.
The condition: i.e., the known conditions mentioned earlier in the chapter of invalid sale that are not from the requirements of the contract, not every condition; because lease is a pure commutative contract, revocable and resissible, so it is like sale. Thus everything that invalidates sale invalidates it. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi codified this in his Mukhtasar, saying: If what the lease contract is concluded upon is unknown in itself, or in its rent, or in the duration of the lease, or in the work rented for, then the lease is invalid. And every uncertainty that enters sale and invalidates it due to uncertainty, so too in lease. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 277/2] The conditions that invalidate it in detail: such as stipulating the plastering of the house or its repair, or hanging a door on it, or inserting a beam on the lessee; similarly stipulating the digging of a canal in the land, or building a bank on it, or digging a well in it, or that he should steal it from the lessee; similarly stipulating the return of the land tilled; similarly if he stipulates that if water stops from the millstone the rent is on him; similarly if he hires a mount to Baghdad on condition that if he obtains something he gives it, or if he reaches Baghdad then he gets such and such, otherwise nothing for him; then it is invalid, and on him the equivalent wage of what he traveled on; similarly if he hires a slave for a month on condition that if he falls ill in it, he will work in the following month for the number of days he fell ill. (From Ghayat al-Bayan). So the invalidating conditions exclude what the contract requires, such as stipulating that he pays him the rent upon return from travel. [Bahr al-Raiq: 453/7] 'Its equivalent wage' etc.: i.e., after delivery and the lessee's utilization of the benefit; because the wage in the invalid lease is not obligatory merely by ability, but actual utilization must occur, unlike the valid lease where the named wage becomes obligatory by mere ability (Fath briefly). I say: There should be excepted from this rule (i.e., that ujr al-mithl in invalid lease is for the lessor) those leases that are initially concluded as invalid but then become valid, even if they did not explicitly mention it, as some examples will come, for in them the lessor gets the named wage.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage elaborates on what invalidates an ijara contract. Drawing from the analogy with sale, any condition that is not part of the contract's requirement (muqtada al-aqd) can invalidate. The principle: absolute uncertainty (jahala) in the object itself, the rent, the duration, or the work invalidates. Specific examples: requiring the lessor to plaster the house, repair, hang a door, or insert a beam; requiring digging a canal, building a bank, or digging a well; condition that the lessee must return the land tilled; condition that if water stops the millstone the rent is still due; hiring to Baghdad with condition that if he gets something he gives it, or if he reaches Baghdad he gets something, otherwise nothing; hiring a slave for a month with condition that if he falls ill he will work extra days in the next month. Also, conditions that are part of the contract's requirement (like paying rent on return from travel) do not invalidate. The passage also explains that in fasid ijara, ujr al-mithl is due only after actual utilization, not upon mere ability as in valid leases. It also notes an exception: leases that start as fasid but later become valid give the named wage.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or lack of knowledge about a fundamental element of the contract
مقتضى العقد (muqtada al-aqd): The inherent requirements of the contract that are implicit in its nature
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Equivalent wage; market rate for the benefit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following conditions does NOT invalidate a lease according to the text?
A) Stipulating that the lessee must plaster the house.
B) Stipulating that the rent is paid upon return from travel.
C) Stipulating that if water stops, rent is still due.
D) Stipulating that the hired animal will only be taken if something is obtained.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any condition in an ijara contract that introduces uncertainty (jahala) in the object, rent, duration, or work makes the contract fasid, with ujr al-mithl due only after actual utilization.

Dispute on Ujr al-Mithl Exceeding Named Rent in Invalid Lease
Explaining Hanafi view that ujr al-mithl cannot exceed named rent vs. Zufar/Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school caps ujr al-mithl at the named rent in a fasid ijara and evaluate the counter-argument of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Benefits are not valuable in themselves; only the semblance of a contract gives them value up to the named rent.

How do you calculate payment when a lease is invalid? Must you pay the full market rate, or only what was agreed? This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle: ujr al-mithl is capped at the named rent, contrary to some other schools. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the nature of benefits (manafi') and the role of contractual semblance (shubhat al-aqd).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: in a fasid ijara, ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) is owed but cannot exceed the named rent (musamma).
This is the position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Zufar (within Hanafi school) and al-Shafi'i hold that ujr al-mithl is due in full, without cap, by analogy with fasid sales of physical goods.
This is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disagreement.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the qiyas: in a fasid sale of a physical object, the buyer must pay the full market price (qimah), not the named price. Similarly, in a fasid lease, the hirer should pay the full ujr al-mithl.
The opposing school treats benefits (manafi') like physical 'ayn.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: benefits are not valuable in themselves; they only acquire value through a valid contract. In a fasid contract, only a semblance (shubha) of the contract exists, limited to the named amount. Thus ujr al-mithl is capped at the named rent.
The key distinction: manafi' are non-existent before use, unlike physical goods.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if named rent is less than market rate, the Hanafi recipient gets only the named amount, while Zufar/Shafi'i would give market rate.
This affects compensation in invalid leases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجاوز به المسمى، فإن أجر دارا كل شهر بدرهم صح في شهر فقط إلا أن أي بأجر المثل على شرط أنها كل شهر بدرهم العقد واحد فقط الكل، وكل شهر سكن ساعة منه صح فيه، وإن استأجرها سنة يسمى لم يسم أجر كل شهر، العقد أي الدار بعشرة دراهم مثلا صح، وإن العقد لا يجاوز به المسمى إلخ فإن كان مساويا لأجر المثل، أو زاد عليه فأجر المثل، وإن كان أقل، فالمسمى، هذا إذا لم يكن الفساد. من جهالة المسمى، أو عدم التسمية كما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله: "لا يجاوز المسمى" فإنه إذا كان الفساد بأحد هذين الوجهين يجب أجر المثل بالغا ما بلغ. واعلم أن الحكم بأن لا يجاوز أجر المثل المسمى مذهب أصحابنا الثلاثة، وأما عند زفر والشافعي رحمة: يجب أجر المثل بالغا ما بلغ في الكل اعتبارا ببيع الأعيان لنا: أن المنافع غير متقومة بنفسها، وإنما يتقوم بالعقد الشرعي للضرورة، فإذا فسدت الإجارة وجب أن لا يجب الأجرة، لعدم العقد الشرعي . إلا أن الفاسد كل عقد ملحق بصحيحه؛ لكونه من تبعا له ضرورة، فيكون له قيمة في قدر ما وجد فيه شبهة العقد، وهو قدر المسمى، فيجب المسمى بالغا ما بلغ، وفيما زاد على المسمى لم يوجد فيه عقد، ولا شبهة عقد، فلا يتقوم، ويبقى على الأصل تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥/٨] صح في شهر لأن كلمة "كل" إذا دخلت على مجهول وأفراده غير معلومة انصرف إلى الواحد؛ لكونه معلوما، فإذا تم الشهر الأول لكل واحد منهما نقض الإجارة بشرط حضور الآخر، وإن كان غائبا لا يجوز بالإجماع. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦/٨] أن إلا أن يسمى الكل: [ أي كل شهر عددا بأن يقول: أجرتك داري عشرة أشهر كل شهر بدرهم. (فتح)] أي يعين كل الأشهر؛ لأنه حينئذ تعلم المدة، فيصح العقد فيها بالإجماع. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۷/۲] وكل شهر سكن إلخ: أي صح العقد في كل شهر سكن ساعة الحصول رضاهما بذلك، ولم يكن للمؤجر إخراجه إلى أن ينقض، ولو فسخ أثناء الشهر لم ينفسخ، وقيل: ينفسخ إذا خرج الشهر ، ولو قال في أثناء الشهر: فسخت رأس الشهر، ينفسخ إذا أهل الشهر فيكون فسخا مضافا ولو عجل أجرة شهرين أو ثلاثة وقبض الأجرة لا يكون لواحد منهما الفسخ في قدر المعجل أجرته [ رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۷/۲] لأنه بالتقديم زالت الجهالة في ذلك القدر فيكون كالمسمى. (زيلعي) كذا في الفتح، قال الشارح وهذا أي صحة العقد في كل شهر "سكن منه ساعة" . هو القياس وقد مال إليه بعض المتأخرين، وفي ظاهر الرواية لكل منهما الخيار في الليلة الأولى من الشهر الداخل ويومها انتهى، وقال في "الفتح" على قول الشارح: وفي ظاهر الرواية إلخ وبه يفتى؛ لأن في اعتبار الساعة حرجا عظيما. (زيلعي) وإن لم يسم إلخ الأن المدة معلومة ألا ترى أن إجارة شهر واحد تصح وإن لم يسم قسط كل يوم. (فتح)] إذا بين الأجرة جملة جاز العقد؛ لأن المنفعة صارت معلومة ببيان المدة والأجرة معلومة، وإن لم يبين القسط كل شهر، فإذا صح وجب أن يقسم على الشهور على السواء، ولا يعتبر تفاوت الأسعار باختلاف الزمان. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٧/٨]
It does not exceed the named wage. So if one rents a house each month for a dirham, it is valid in one month only, unless the entire [period] is named. [Commentary:] with ujr al-mithl on condition that each month is a dirham, the contract is only one [month]. And every month in which he resides an hour, it is valid therein. If he rents it for a year and does not name the rent per month, but names the total, e.g., ten dirhams, the contract is valid. And the contract does not exceed the named wage etc. So if [ujr al-mithl] equals or exceeds [the named], it is ujr al-mithl; if it is less, then the named. This is when the invalidity is not due to uncertainty of the named or lack of naming, as the author pointed out by saying 'does not exceed the named.' For when the invalidity is due to one of these two, ujr al-mithl is necessary whatever it amounts to. Know that the ruling that ujr al-mithl does not exceed the named is the madhhab of our three imams. According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, may mercy be upon them: ujr al-mithl is necessary whatever it amounts to in all cases, by analogy with the sale of physical objects. Our proof: Benefits are not valuable in themselves; they only become valuable through a valid contract out of necessity. So when the lease is corrupted, it becomes necessary that no rent should be obligatory due to the absence of a valid contract. However, every corrupted contract is attached to its valid one because it follows it out of necessity, so it has value to the extent that a semblance of a contract exists, which is the amount of the named wage. Thus the named is obligatory whatever it amounts to. For what exceeds the named, there is no contract and no semblance of a contract, so it does not become valuable, and remains on the original [non-valuable state]. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq: 35/8) 'Valid in one month' because the word 'kull' (each) when applied to something unknown and its individuals are unknown, it refers to one unit because it is known. So when the first month is completed, each of them has the right to rescind the lease on condition of the other's presence; if absent, it is not permissible by consensus. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq: 36/8) That is, unless he names the whole: [by saying: I rent you my house for ten months at a dirham per month (Fath)] i.e., he specifies all the months; because then the duration is known, so the contract is valid in all by consensus. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 277/2] 'And every month in which he resides an hour' etc.: i.e., the contract is valid in every month in which he resides an hour due to their mutual consent, and the lessor may not evict him until it ends. If he rescinds during the month, the lease is not rescinded. Some say it is rescinded when the month ends. If he says during the month: I rescind at the beginning of the month, it is rescinded when the new month begins, and it is a deferred rescission. Similarly, if he pays the rent for two or three months in advance and takes possession, neither of them can rescind in the amount of the advanced rent [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 277/2] because by advancing, the uncertainty in that amount is removed, so it is like the named. (Zayla'i) So in Fath, the commentator said that this (the validity of the contract in every month in which he resides an hour) is the qiyas, and some later scholars inclined to it. In the zahir al-riwayah, each has the option during the first night of the coming month and its day. End. And in al-Fath on the commentator's saying: 'In zahir al-riwayah etc.' and this is the basis for fatwa because considering an hour causes great hardship. (Zayla'i) 'If he does not name [the rent per month]' etc.: [Because the duration is known; do you not see that a lease for one month is valid even if he does not name the installment for each day? (Fath)] When he specifies the total rent in a lump sum, the contract is valid because the benefit becomes known by specifying the duration and the rent is known, even if he does not specify the installment per month. So when it is valid, it must be divided equally among the months, and fluctuations of prices over time are not considered. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq: 37/8)
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage delves into the details of ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) in fasid ijara. The general rule is that ujr al-mithl is wajib, but it is capped at the named rent (musamma). The Hanafi imams (excluding Zufar) hold that ujr al-mithl cannot exceed the musamma. Zufar and al-Shafi'i disagree, saying ujr al-mithl is due in full regardless, by analogy with fasid sale of physical goods. The Hanafi proof is that benefits (manafi') are not inherently valuable; they only have value through a valid contract. In a fasid contract, since the contract is not valid, no rent would be due ordinarily. However, the fasid contract is attached to its valid counterpart out of necessity, so it has value only to the extent that a semblance of a contract (shubhat al-aqd) exists, which is limited to the named amount. Thus the named amount is obligatory as a maximum. The passage then applies this to examples: renting a house per month without specifying total; only the first month is valid due to ambiguity of 'kull' (each). Various sub-rulings: if the rent is advanced, uncertainty is removed and the amount becomes like musamma. The passage also discusses the option to rescind at the end of each month in the zahir al-riwayah, which is preferred due to hardship of the qiyas ruling.

Key Terms
المسمى (al-musamma): The named or specified rent in the contract
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent wage or market rate for the benefit
شبهة العقد (shubhat al-aqd): A legal semblance or appearance of a valid contract that gives limited effect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on ujr al-mithl in a fasid ijara contract?
A) Ujr al-mithl is always the full market rate.
B) Ujr al-mithl is capped at the named rent (musamma).
C) Ujr al-mithl is only due if the named rent is unspecified.
D) Ujr al-mithl is not due at all in a fasid contract.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid lease, the Hanafi school caps ujr al-mithl at the named rent because benefits lack inherent value and only gain value through the semblance of a valid contract.

Fasid Ijarah: The Named Rent Is Not Exceeded
Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on rent in fasid ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on rent in fasid ijarah, explain the distinction based on the type of defect, and evaluate the opposing argument of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
In a fasid ijarah, the named rent binds unless ignorance of that named amount causes the defect.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq tackles a key disagreement in ijarah: what rent is due when the contract is invalid? The Hanafi school differentiates defects: if the defect is not due to ignorance of the named rent, the named rent is an upper limit; otherwise, fair rent is due. This nuance contrasts with the view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who always demand fair rent. Understanding this dispute refines your grasp of how benefits (manafi') are valued in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the opening lines: 'لا يجاوز به المسمى' (the named rent is not exceeded). Under what conditions is the named rent binding? If the named rent equals or exceeds the fair rent, fair rent is due; if it is less, the named rent is due. But this applies only when the defect is not ignorance of the named amount or lack of naming.
The exact rule: if the cause of fasād is not jahāla of the musamma or lack of tasmiya, the musamma is not exceeded.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The text names Zufar and al-Shafi'i: they hold that fair rent (ajr al-mithl) is always due, regardless of the defect. They base this on analogy to sale of goods.
Zufar is a Hanafi but here aligns with Shafi'i; intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their proof (dalīl): in a fasid sale of goods, the fair price (qīma) is always due. They analogize ijarah to sale, arguing that benefits should be treated like goods.
The analogy is qiyās in its clearest form.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: benefits (manāfiʿ) are not intrinsically valuable; they only acquire value through a valid contract. A fasid contract only creates a semblance of contract (shubha) in the named amount, so only that amount is due. Beyond the named amount, there is no semblance, so it remains non‑valuable.
Key phrase: 'المنافع غير متقومة بنفسها' – benefits have no inherent value.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If the named rent is 100 and fair rent is 150, Hanafis say only 100 is due; Zufar/Shafiʿi say 150. This affects the lessor's compensation in a fasid contract.
The dispute only arises when the named rent is less than the fair rent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
الإجارة الفاسدة
لا يجاوز به المسمى، فإن أجر دارا كل شهر بدرهم صح في شهر فقط إلا أن يسمى الكل، وكل شهر سكن ساعة منه صح فيه، وإن استأجرها سنة يسمى لم يسم أجر كل شهر، العقد أي الدار بعشرة دراهم مثلا صح، وإن العقد لا يجاوز به المسمى إلخ فإن كان مساويا لأجر المثل، أو زاد عليه فأجر المثل، وإن كان أقل، فالمسمى، هذا إذا لم يكن الفساد. من جهالة المسمى، أو عدم التسمية كما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله: "لا يجاوز المسمى" فإنه إذا كان الفساد بأحد هذين الوجهين يجب أجر المثل بالغا ما بلغ.
واعلم أن الحكم بأن لا يجاوز أجر المثل المسمى مذهب أصحابنا الثلاثة، وأما عند زفر والشافعي رحمة: يجب أجر المثل بالغا ما بلغ في الكل اعتبارا ببيع الأعيان لنا: أن المنافع غير متقومة بنفسها، وإنما يتقوم بالعقد الشرعي للضرورة، فإذا فسدت الإجارة وجب أن لا يجب الأجرة، لعدم العقد الشرعي . إلا أن الفاسد كل عقد ملحق بصحيحه؛ لكونه من تبعا له ضرورة، فيكون له قيمة في قدر ما وجد فيه شبهة العقد، وهو قدر المسمى، فيجب المسمى بالغا ما بلغ، وفيما زاد على المسمى لم يوجد فيه عقد، ولا شبهة عقد، فلا يتقوم، ويبقى على الأصل تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥/٨] صح في شهر لأن كلمة "كل" إذا دخلت على مجهول وأفراده غير معلومة انصرف إلى الواحد؛ لكونه معلوما، فإذا تم الشهر الأول لكل واحد منهما نقض الإجارة بشرط حضور الآخر، وإن كان غائبا لا يجوز بالإجماع. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦/٨]
أن إلا أن يسمى الكل: [ أي كل شهر عددا بأن يقول: أجرتك داري عشرة أشهر كل شهر بدرهم. (فتح)] أي يعين كل الأشهر؛ لأنه حينئذ تعلم المدة، فيصح العقد فيها بالإجماع. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۷/۲] وكل شهر سكن إلخ: أي صح العقد في كل شهر سكن ساعة الحصول رضاهما بذلك، ولم يكن للمؤجر إخراجه إلى أن ينقض، ولو فسخ أثناء الشهر لم ينفسخ، وقيل: ينفسخ إذا خرج الشهر ، ولو قال في أثناء الشهر: فسخت رأس الشهر، ينفسخ إذا أهل الشهر فيكون فسخا مضافا ولو عجل أجرة شهرين أو ثلاثة وقبض الأجرة لا يكون لواحد منهما الفسخ في قدر المعجل أجرته [ رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۷/۲] لأنه بالتقديم زالت الجهالة في ذلك القدر فيكون كالمسمى. (زيلعي) كذا في الفتح، قال الشارح وهذا أي صحة العقد في كل شهر "سكن منه ساعة" . هو القياس وقد مال إليه بعض المتأخرين، وفي ظاهر الرواية لكل منهما الخيار في الليلة الأولى من الشهر الداخل ويومها انتهى، وقال في "الفتح" على قول الشارح: وفي ظاهر الرواية إلخ وبه يفتى؛ لأن في اعتبار الساعة حرجا عظيما. (زيلعي) وإن لم يسم إلخ الأن المدة معلومة ألا ترى أن إجارة شهر واحد تصح وإن لم يسم قسط كل يوم. (فتح)] إذا بين الأجرة جملة جاز العقد؛ لأن المنفعة صارت معلومة ببيان المدة والأجرة معلومة، وإن لم يبين القسط كل شهر، فإذا صح وجب أن يقسم على الشهور على السواء، ولا يعتبر تفاوت الأسعار باختلاف الزمان. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٧/٨]
Book of Ijarah. Fasid Ijarah. The named rent is not exceeded. If one rents a house each month for a dirham, it is valid only in one month unless he names the total. And each month that he resides for an hour of it, it is valid in it. If he rents it for a year without naming the rent for each month, the contract is valid for the house with ten dirhams for example. And the contract does not exceed the named rent etc. If it is equal to the fair rent or exceeds it, then the fair rent; if it is less, then the named rent. This is if the invalidity is not due to ignorance of the named rent or lack of naming, as indicated by the author: 'does not exceed the named rent'. If the invalidity is one of these two, then fair rent is obligatory whatever it may be. Know that the ruling that the named rent is not exceeded by the fair rent is the madhhab of our three imams. As for Zufar and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them: fair rent is obligatory whatever it may be in all cases, by analogy to sale of goods. Our proof: benefits are not valuable in themselves; they only become valuable through a valid contract due to necessity. If the ijarah is invalid, it is necessary that rent is not obligatory due to lack of a valid contract. However, every invalid contract is annexed to its valid counterpart because it follows it by necessity. So it has value in the extent where semblance of contract exists, which is the amount named. Thus the named rent is obligatory whatever it may be. In what exceeds the named rent, there is no contract nor semblance of contract, so it is not valuable and remains on the original principle. [Minhaj al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:35] It is valid in one month because when the word 'kull' (each) enters on an unknown and its individuals are unknown, it turns to one because it is known. When the first month ends, each of them can terminate the contract with the condition of the other's presence; if absent, it is not permissible by consensus. [Minhaj al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:36] That unless he names the total, meaning each month by number, saying: I rented you my house for ten months each month for a dirham. He specifies all months because then the term is known, so the contract is valid in them by consensus. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:277] And each month he resides etc.: the contract is valid in each month he resides for an hour due to their mutual satisfaction. The lessor cannot evict him until it ends. If he cancels during the month, it is not cancelled. It is said: it cancels when the month ends. If he says during the month: I cancel at the start of the month, it cancels when the month begins, so it is a deferred cancellation. If he advances rent for two or three months and receives the rent, neither can cancel in the portion of the advanced rent [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:277] because by advancing, the ignorance is removed in that portion, so it is like the named rent. (Zayla'i) Thus in al-Fath. The commentator said: This, meaning the validity of the contract in each month he resides for an hour, is qiyas. Some later scholars inclined to it. In zahir al-riwayah, each has the option in the first night of the incoming month and its day. End. He said in al-Fath on the commentator's statement: 'In zahir al-riwayah etc.' and by it fatwa is given because considering the hour causes great difficulty. (Zayla'i) If he does not name etc.: Now the term is known. Do you not see that the rental of one month is valid even if he does not name the daily portion? (Fath) If he declares the total rent, the contract is valid because the benefit becomes known by specifying the term, and the rent is known, even if he does not specify the monthly installment. When valid, it is divided equally over the months, and fluctuation of prices over time is not considered. [Minhaj al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:37]
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the rulings of fasid (invalid) ijarah from the Hanafi perspective. It opens by stating the core ruling: in a fasid ijarah, the named rent (musamma) is not exceeded. Two scenarios are distinguished: if the defect is not due to ignorance of the named amount or lack of naming, then the rent equals the named rent if it is less than the fair rent, otherwise the fair rent. If the defect is due to ignorance of the named rent or lack of naming, then fair rent is obligatory in full. The text then presents an inter-madhhab dispute: the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) maintain the above, while Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that fair rent is always due, analogizing to sale of goods. The Hanafi proof is that benefits (manafi') are not intrinsically valuable; they only acquire value through a valid contract. In a fasid contract, only the named amount has a semblance of a valid contract, so only that amount is owed. The text then explains the one-month rule when 'kull' (each) is used ambiguously: it is valid for one month only unless the total is specified. Further commentary discusses details like cancellation, advance payment, and the sufficiency of naming the total rent without monthly breakdown. The passage concludes by stating that the monthly division is equal and price fluctuations are ignored.

Key Terms
المسمى (al-musamma): The rent specifically named in the contract by the parties.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market value of the benefit, determined by custom and comparable contracts.
منفعة (manfa'a): The usufruct or benefit from the leased asset, which is the object of the ijarah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in a fasid ijarah where the named rent is less than the fair rent and the defect is NOT ignorance of the named amount, what is the due rent?
A) The fair rent
B) The named rent
C) No rent
D) The average of named and fair rent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the named rent in a fasid ijarah is an upper limit; it is not exceeded unless the defect is ignorance of that named amount itself.

The Validity of Renting a Bathhouse and the Role of Custom
Ruling on ijara of hammam and its proof via custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates the ijara of a hammam despite jahalah, and identify the role of custom (ta'aruf) in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
Custom ('urf) can override qiyas in mu'amalat, making rental of a bathhouse valid despite uncertainty.

Imagine paying to use a public bathhouse where you don't know exactly how much water you'll use or how long you'll stay. Intuitively, this seems like a contract full of uncertainty (gharar). Yet the Hanafi school declares such a rental valid. This passage explains why: widespread custom (ta'aruf) serves as evidence, overriding the strict qiyas that would otherwise invalidate it. The lesson illustrates a fundamental principle of Hanafi mu'amalat: custom can legitimize transactions that pure analogy would reject.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is renting a bathhouse (hammam) for men to bathe in. The ruling is valid (sahih); the owner may take the fee.
This is stated clearly at the beginning: 'صح له أخذ الأجرة'.
2
Recognize the potential defect
Such a contract involves jahalah (ignorance) about two key elements: the amount of water consumed and the duration of use. In standard ijarah, these must be known.
The text explicitly mentions: 'فإن فيها جهالة فإنه لا يعلم فيها مقدار الماء، ولا مقدار القعود'.
3
Understand the objections
Some scholars disliked the bathhouse itself (based on a hadith), and others thought the contract might be invalid due to the uncertainty. Qiyas would reject it because it involves destroying property (the water) with ignorance.
The commentator notes that qiyas would reject it: 'وإن كان القياس يأباه'.
4
See the Hanafi justification
The ruling is based on two evidences: the action of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra) who entered a bathhouse at al-Juhfa, and the widespread custom (ta'aruf) of people in all cities paying for baths. This custom amounts to consensus (ijma') indicating permissibility.
The text states: 'دل إجماعهم على جواز ذلك'.
5
Extract the principle
The underlying principle is istihsan (juristic preference): when custom is pervasive, it overrides the strict qiyas that would otherwise invalidate the contract due to uncertainty.
This is a classic application of 'urf as a source of law in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجرة الحمام أي إذا آجر أحد حمامه ليغتسل فيه الرجال صح له أخذ الأجرة، وإنما ذكر هذه المسألة في هذا لباب مع أنه عقد لبيان الفاسد، إما لأن بعض العلماء خالف في ذلك ،وكرهه قال الشارح: وبعض العلماء كره الحمام؛ لما روي عنه عليه أنه سماه شر بيت وقال عثمان الله إنه بيت الشيطان وإما لأنه كان مظنة أن تفسد نذه الإجارة؛ لأن فيها جهالة فإنه لا يعلم فيها مقدار الماء، ولا مقدار القعود، فنبه على أنها صحيحة، وجه لجواز : أنه علي دخل الحمام بالجحفة، وتعارف الناس بذلك، فإن الناس في سائر الأمصار يدفعون أجرة الحمام، دل إجماعهم على جواز ذلك، وإن كان القياس يأباه؛ لوروده على إتلاف العين مع الجهالة، ولم يعتبروا هذه –
The rental of the bathhouse: if one rents his bathhouse for men to bathe in, it is permissible for him to take the rent. He mentioned this issue in this chapter even though it is a valid contract, to explain the invalid, either because some scholars opposed it and disliked it. The commentator said: Some scholars disliked the bathhouse because it is narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he called it the worst house and said: 'Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, it is the house of the devil. Or because it was thought that this ijarah might be invalid because there is ignorance in it: the amount of water is not known, nor the duration of sitting. So he pointed out that it is valid. The basis for its permissibility: that 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) entered the bathhouse at al-Juhfa, and people have customarily done this, for people in all cities pay the rent of the bathhouse. Their consensus indicates its permissibility, even though qiyas would reject it because it involves destruction of property with ignorance. And they did not consider this –
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of renting a bathhouse (hammam). The author notes that this issue is brought up in the chapter on fasid ijarah even though it is a valid contract, to clarify that it is not invalid despite potential defects. Some scholars disliked it due to a hadith calling the bathhouse a bad place. Others thought it might be invalid due to uncertainty (jahalah) about the amount of water used and the duration of stay. The ruling is that it is valid, supported by the practice of 'Ali (ra) and the widespread custom (ta'aruf) of people paying for baths in all cities. This custom amounts to a form of consensus (ijma') indicating permissibility, even though qiyas (analogy) would consider it invalid due to destroying the property (water) with uncertainty. The Hanafi school thus permits it based on custom overriding qiyas (istihsan).

Key Terms
أجرة الحمام (ujrat al-hammam): The fee paid for using a public bathhouse; the contract of ijarah for such use.
تعارف (ta'aruf): Customary practice or general usage that is widespread among people.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; in this context, strict analogy that would require specification of water and time to avoid gharar.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; setting aside strict qiyas in favor of a more appropriate ruling based on custom, necessity, or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the Hanafi school validates the rental of a bathhouse despite the uncertainty in water and duration?
A) Because 'Ali ibn Abi Talib entered a bathhouse at al-Juhfa.
B) Because the contract specifies the exact amount of water.
C) Because there is a clear hadith permitting it.
D) Because of the widespread custom of people paying for it.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) can validate contracts that strict analogy would deem invalid due to uncertainty.

Calculating an Unspecified Lease Term: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains how to fix an unspecified lease term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on calculating an unspecified lease term and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
When a lease term begins mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts every month as 30 days; the Sahibayn count the first month by days and the rest by lunar months.

When a lease is for a duration like 'one year' but the start date is not mentioned, the term begins at the time of the contract. But what if the contract is signed in the middle of a month? How are the months counted? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differ on this point. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and identifies the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract scenario
Consider a lease contract made on a specific date, say the 10th of Muharram, for a term of 'one year' without specifying the start. Determine whether the term begins immediately after the contract.
The default rule is that the term starts from the contract time itself, as established by the text.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, because the first month cannot be a full lunar month (since part of it has passed), the gap is filled by counting days from the consecutive month. This results in every month being counted as 30 days, totaling 360 days for a year.
His reasoning: the first month is completed by days from the following month, and so on for all months.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the first incomplete month is counted by the remaining days, while the subsequent full months are counted as true lunar months based on moon sightings.
Their reasoning: lunar months are the norm when possible; the first month is an exception because it has already started.
4
Understand the ta'lil (reasoning) behind each view
Abu Hanifa argues that if the first month is completed by days from the next month, the same will apply to all months, making the entire term a fixed number of days. The Sahibayn prioritize the lunar standard for complete months.
The dispute is based on qiyas and istihsan, not on textual evidence.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: all months are counted as 30 days each. This is the zahir al-riwayah and is upheld by later authorities.
If the contract is made at the beginning of a new month (i.e., on the night of the crescent), then lunar months are used by agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وابتداء المدة وقت العقد، فإن كان حين يهل يعتبر الأهلة، وإلا فالأيام، وصح أجرة الحمام لتعارف الناس. (الشرح:) قال: رابتداء المدة: لما كانت السنة منكرة غير معينة أفاد أن هذا المنكر يعين بقرينة الحال، ويكون أول مدة الإجارة لوقت الذي يلي العقد؛ لأن في مثله يتعين الزمان الذي يلي العقد كالأجل، واليمين لا يكلم فلانا شهرا؛ لأنه ولم يتعين عقيب العقد لصارت مجهولة والظاهر من حالهما أنهما يعقدان العقد الصحيح فتعين عقيب العقد. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٧/٨] رقت العقد : [ أي من وقت العقد وهذا إذا كان العقد مطلقا، وإن بين مدة تعين ذلك لأن الأوقات كلها في حكم الإجارة سواء، وفي مثله يتعين الزمان الذي يعقب السبب كما في الآجال بأن باع إلى شهر، والأيمان بأن حلف لا يكلم فلانا شهرا حيث اعتبر فيهما الابتداء بعد الفراغ من التكلم. [فتح: ٢٤٤/٣] (درر) حين يهل : وقال صاحب "النهاية": بضم الياء وفتح الهاء على صيغة البناء للمفعول أي يبصر الهلال، قال: وأراد ه اليوم الأول، قال الاتقاني: في هذه الإرادة نظر بل المراد بـ"حين يهل "الهلال" أول الليلة الأولى من الشهر كذا ن "الحموي"، وقال ابن قاضي زاده وليس المراد بقوله : "اليوم الأول" تفسير معنى "حين يهل"؛ إذ قد علم معناه من التفسير السابق قطعا بل مراده بذلك بيان أثر قوله حين" يهل، وليس المراد معناه الحقيقي، بل المراد معناه لعرفي، وهو اليوم الأول من الشهر تكملة البحر الرائق: ۳۷/۸] الأهلة: [حتى لو نقص شهر كان عليه كمال الأخيرة. (بدائع)] يعني إذا وقع عقد الإجارة في ليلة الهلال أو يومها ولم يعين في الابتداء المدة تعتبر المدة بالأهلة فيكون شهور السنة كلها بالأهلة، وإن كان بعد ما مضى شيء من الشهر يعتبر أن بالأيام، وهو يعتبر كل شهر ثلاثون يوما، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما يتم ا لأول بالأيام والباقي بالأهلة؛ لأن الأصل في الشهور اعتبارها بالأهلة عند الإمكان وقد أمكن ذلك في الشهور المتخللة تعذر في الأول فيكمل بأيام الشهر الذي بعد جميع الشهور، وله أن الشهر الأول يتم بأيام تليه من الشهر المتصل ه فيبدأ الشهر الثاني بالأيام ضرورة وهكذا إلى آخر المدة كل شهر ثلاثون يوما والسنة ثلث مائة وستون يوما، ذكر في "الذخيرة" إذا استأجر في أثناء الشهر يعتبر الكل بالأيام بالاتفاق تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٧/٨]
And the beginning of the term is at the time of the contract. If it is at the time of the new moon (when the crescent is seen), then lunar months are considered; otherwise, days. And the hiring of a bathhouse is valid due to the custom of the people. Commentary: He said: The beginning of the term: Since the year was indefinite and unspecified, it indicates that this indefinite matter is specified by contextual indication, and the first term of the lease is the time following the contract; because in similar cases, the time following the contract is specified, like the deadline and the oath 'I will not speak to so-and-so for a month' because if it were not specified immediately after the contract, it would become unknown, and the apparent situation of the two parties is that they conclude a valid contract, so it is specified immediately after the contract. (Tatimmat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/37) "following the contract" i.e., from the time of the contract. This is when the contract is absolute; if a term is specified, it is specified because all times are equal in lease contracts, and in similar cases the time following the cause is specified, as in deadlines where one sells for a month, and oaths where one swears not to speak to so-and-so for a month, where the beginning is considered after finishing speaking. (Fath 3/244) (Durar) "at the time of the new moon": The author of al-Nihayah said: with a damma on the ya and a fatha on the ha in the passive voice meaning the crescent is seen. He said: He meant the first day. Al-Atqani said: There is consideration in this intention; rather what is meant by 'when the crescent is seen' is the first night of the month. So in al-Hamawi, and Ibn Qadi Zadah said: He did not intend by his saying 'the first day' an interpretation of the meaning of 'when the crescent is seen' because its meaning is certainly known from the previous interpretation; rather he intended thereby to clarify the effect of his saying 'when the crescent is seen,' and not the literal meaning, but the customary meaning, which is the first day of the month. (Tatimmat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/37) The lunar months: So that if a month is incomplete, he must complete it as the last [thirty days]. (Bada'i') Means: If the lease contract occurs on the night of the new moon or its day and the beginning of the term was not specified, the term is considered by lunar months, so all months of the year are lunar months. But if some time of the month has already passed, it is considered by days, and each month is considered thirty days. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first month is completed by days and the rest by lunar months; because the principle for months is to consider them by lunar months when possible, and it is possible for the intervening months, but impossible for the first, so it is completed by the days of the month following all the months. And for him (Abu Hanifa), the first month is completed by the days that follow it from the consecutive month, so the second month begins with days necessarily, and so on until the end of the term: each month thirty days and the year three hundred and sixty days. It is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah: If one hires in the middle of the month, all is considered by days by agreement. (Tatimmat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/37)
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about how to determine the term of a lease when the duration is mentioned but the start is ambiguous (e.g., 'for one year' without specifying from when). The text explains that the beginning of the lease term is at the time of the contract itself, unless otherwise specified. If the contract is made on the night of the new moon or the first day of a lunar month, then the term is calculated using lunar months. If it is made after some days of the month have passed, then the term is calculated by days (each month counted as 30 days). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ: they say the first incomplete month is completed by days, and the remaining full months are lunar months. The reasoning is that lunar months are the norm for months when possible; for the first month that has already started, it is not possible to count a full lunar month, so it is completed by days from the next month. Abu Hanifa argues that the first month should also be completed by days from the consecutive month, leading to all months being 30 days. Both positions are based on qiyas and istihsan. The text also notes that if the hiring occurs in the middle of a month, all months are by days by agreement. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, and the mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's.

Key Terms
أهلّة (ahillah): Lunar months based on actual sighting of the moon, not fixed 30-day months.
ابتداء المدة (ibtidā' al-muddah): The beginning of the lease term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a lease is contracted on the 10th of Muharram for one year without specifying the start, how is the term calculated?
A) All months by lunar calendar, so the term ends on the 10th of Muharram next year.
B) The first incomplete month is counted by days, and the remaining months by lunar months.
C) Each month is counted as 30 days, totaling 360 days.
D) The term begins from the next full month, and the days before are ignored.

Key Takeaway
When a lease term is unspecified and the contract is signed mid-month, the Hanafi mufta bihi position counts every month as 30 days to ensure certainty.

Validity of Hiring a Bathhouse Due to Custom
Declares the hire of a bathhouse valid due to custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a bathhouse and explain how custom (ta'āruf) overcomes apparent uncertainty (gharar).

Core Idea
A lease with apparent uncertainty is valid if custom makes it acceptable.

You have learned that uncertainty (gharar) in a contract can render it invalid. But what if the uncertainty is minor and people routinely accept it? This lesson examines the lease of a bathhouse (ḥammām), where the exact amount of water and duration are unknown. The Hanafi school declares it valid because widespread custom (ta'āruf) transforms such uncertainty into acceptable risk.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the apparent problem
Identify the source of uncertainty in a bathhouse lease: the user does not know how much water will be used or how long they will stay.
This would normally invalidate a lease under the rule against gharar.
2
See the Hanafi solution
The Hanafi school relies on custom (ta'āruf al-nās) and the Prophet's own practice of entering a bathhouse at al-Juhfah.
Custom here is a source of law that can override qiyas.
3
Understand the limits
This tolerance applies only when the uncertainty is minor and does not lead to dispute. If exposure of awrah occurs, the ruling may change.
The same principle applies to women, whose need is even greater.
4
Apply the principle
Consider other contracts with similar uncertainties: if custom accepts them, they are valid. This is a key concept in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح أجرة الحمام لتعارف الناس. (الشرح:) يعني إذا آجر أحد حمامه ليغتسل فيه الرجال صح له أخذ الأجرة، وإنما ذكر هذه المسألة في هذا الباب مع أنه عقد لبيان الفاسد، إما لأن بعض العلماء خالف في ذلك، وكرهه قال الشارح: وبعض العلماء كره الحمام؛ لما روي عنه عليه أنه سماه شر بيت وقال عثمان الله إنه بيت الشيطان وإما لأنه كان مظنة أن تفسد نذه الإجارة؛ لأن فيها جهالة فإنه لا يعلم فيها مقدار الماء، ولا مقدار القعود، فنبه على أنها صحيحة، وجه لجواز : أنه علي دخل الحمام بالجحفة، وتعارف الناس بذلك، فإن الناس في سائر الأمصار يدفعون أجرة الحمام، دل إجماعهم على جواز ذلك، وإن كان القياس يأباه؛ لوروده على إتلاف العين مع الجهالة، ولم يعتبروا هذه – الجهالة؛ لأنها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة، والنساء فيه كالرجال هو الصحيح؛ للحاجة، بل حاجتهن أكثر؛ لكثرة أسباب اغتسالهن، وكراهة عثمان محمول على ما فيه من كشف العورة، قاله في الدر" و"الزيلعي"، وفي "الأشباه": يكره له دخول الحمام في ،قول وقيل إلا لمريضة أو نفساء، والمعتمد عدم الكراهة مطلقا قلت ولا شك في زماننا في الكراهة؛ لتحقق كشف العورة، كذا في "الدر". (ملتقط من الفتح والتكملة و رد المحتار)
And the hiring fee of the bathhouse is valid due to the custom of the people. Commentary: Meaning if someone leases his bathhouse for men to bathe in, it is valid for him to take the fee. He only mentioned this issue in this chapter, even though it is a contract, to explain the invalid, either because some scholars disagreed and disliked it. The commentator said: Some scholars disliked the bathhouse due to what was narrated from him (the Prophet) that he called it the worst house, and Uthman said it is the house of Shaytan. Or because it was likely that this lease would be invalid due to uncertainty, for one does not know the amount of water used nor the duration of sitting. So he noted that it is valid. The basis for permissibility: that he (the Prophet) entered the bathhouse at al-Juhfah, and the custom of people is established on this. People in all cities pay the bathhouse fee, and their consensus indicates its permissibility, even if analogy would reject it because it involves destruction of property with uncertainty. They did not consider this uncertainty because it does not lead to dispute. Women are like men in this; that is the correct view due to necessity, rather their need is greater due to many reasons for bathing. The dislike attributed to Uthman is interpreted as due to the exposure of the private parts. This is stated in al-Durr and al-Zayla'i. In al-Ashbah: it is disliked for him to enter the bathhouse according to one view, and it is said except for a sick woman or a woman in nifas. The relied-upon view is no dislike absolutely. I say: In our time there is no doubt in the dislike due to the actual exposure of the private parts. Thus in al-Durr. (Compiled from al-Fath, al-Takmilah, and Radd al-Muhtar).
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement declaring the validity of taking wages for hiring a bathhouse (hamam). The author includes this in the section on invalid leases despite the contract being valid, to address that some scholars (like Uthman) considered it disliked or invalid due to uncertainty (gharar) in the amount of water or time. The text responds by citing the Prophet's own practice of entering a bathhouse at al-Juhfah, and the continuous custom (ta'aruf) of people across cities paying for it, which amounts to consensus (ijma). Even though analogy (qiyas) would oppose it because it involves consuming property with uncertainty, the custom overrides that. The text also notes that women are included, and their need is even greater. The dislike attributed to Uthman is explained as due to the uncovering of awrah, not the lease itself. The contemporary ruling may vary due to increased exposure of private parts. This belongs to Zahir al-Riwayah; the mufta bihi is that it is valid without dislike unless it involves haram exposure.

Key Terms
تعارف الناس (ta'āruf al-nās): The widespread customary practice of people that removes uncertainty (gharar) from a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider the hire of a bathhouse valid despite uncertainty in water and time?
A) Because the amount of water is always fixed.
B) Because the Prophet forbade questioning.
C) Because custom (ta'āruf) removes the uncertainty and the Prophet himself entered a bathhouse.
D) Because women need it more.

Key Takeaway
A lease with minor uncertainty is valid if widespread custom (ta'āruf) makes it acceptable, as in hiring a bathhouse.

Wages for Acts of Worship: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Lists invalid wages for specific services with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wages for acts of worship (adhan, hajj, imamah, teaching Quran/fiqh) and explain the proof and response to the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Acts of worship are personal; wages invalidate the lease because the benefit is intangible.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary addresses a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can one be hired to perform acts of worship like the call to prayer, leading prayer, or teaching the Quran? The Hanafi school, relying on explicit prophetic instructions and the nature of worship, prohibits it, while Shafi'i allows it under certain conditions. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts of worship in dispute
List the specific acts mentioned: adhan, hajj, imamah (leading prayer), teaching Quran, and teaching fiqh. Note that these are all acts of worship that are not obligatory upon the hiree (i.e., the person being hired is not personally obligated to perform them for the employer).
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The Hanafi school rules that taking a wage for these acts is not valid. The basis is that these are 'ta'at' (acts of worship) that are specific to the Muslim; the reward goes to the doer, so hiring someone to do them for a wage is like leasing an act that has no tangible benefit for the payer. The Prophet's instructions (e.g., to Uthman not to take wages for adhan) and the hadith 'Read the Quran and do not eat by means of it' are cited.
The passage also clarifies that if one simply asks someone to perform hajj or adhan without a formal lease (ijarah), it is permissible to give compensation voluntarily.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such leases are valid because the actions are known, not obligatory upon the hiree, and the employer benefits from the performance. The hiree is doing work that could be done by anyone, so it is analogous to other permissible leases.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between acts of worship and ordinary work. In worship, the primary benefit is religious for the doer; even if the payer benefits (e.g., hearing the Quran), it is incidental. The lease would be exchanging money for a purely religious act, which is not permissible. The hadith and analogy with fasting and prayer support this.
The passage emphasizes that the contract is batil (void), not merely fasid, because the subject matter is not valid for lease.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: Hanafis cannot stipulate a wage for these services; any payment must be a voluntary gift (hiba). Shafi'is may stipulate a wage contractually. The mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school is prohibition, based on stronger textual evidence.
Also note the exception for cupping: Hanafis permit wages for cupping because it is a customary medical service, not a pure act of worship, despite the Zahiri objection.

Source Text

والحجام، لا أجرة عسب التيس والأذان والحج والإمامة وتعليم القرآن والفقه، (الشرح:) والحجام: أي جاز أخذ أجرة الحجام؛ لما روي أنه عليها احتجم وأعطى الحجام أجرته، وبه جرى التعارف بين الناس من لدن رسول الله الله إلى يومنا هذا، فانعقد إجماعا، وقالت الظاهرية: لا يجوز؛ لما روي أنه عليها نهى عن عسب التيس وكسب الحجام وقفيز الطحان قلنا هذا الحديث منسوخ؛ لما روي أنه عليه قال له رجل: إن لي عيالا وغلاما حجاما، أفأطعم عيالي من کسبه؟ قال: تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٨/٨] قال في "الفتح": فإن قلت: حيث كان الحديث منسوخا فعدم الجواز في عسب التيس وقفيز الطحان مشكل. قلت: النسخ بالنسبة لكسب الحجام فقط لا مطلقا، هذا ما ظهر لي ثم رأيت التصريح به في كلام الزيلعي والله الحمد انتهى أقول ووجه ذكر هذه المسألة في هذا الباب مع أنها صحيحة كون الاختلاف في صحتها وفساده نعم. السحت عسب التيس [التيس هو الذكر من المعز إذا حال عليه الحول والمراد الفحل مطلقا. والعسب: ضرابه ويقال ماؤه كذا في "الصحاح" وذكر في المجمل أن العسب الكراء الذي يؤخذ على ضراب الفحل. (عيني)] أي لا يصح أخذ الأجر على الأذان وكذا الحج والإمامة وتعليم القرآن والفقه؛ لأن هذه طاعات، وكل طاعة يختص بأدائها مسلم لا يصح أخذ الأجر عليها. وصورة المسألة أن يقول : استأجرتك بكذا على أن تحج عني أو تؤذن أما إذا أمره بالحج أو الأذان من غير ذكر الإجارة، فيجوز، قال في "الهداية": والأصل: أن كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم لا يجوز الاستئجار عليه عندنا، وعند الشافعي: يصح في كل ما لا يتعين على الأجير؛ لأنه استئجار على عمل معلوم غير متعين عليه، فيجوز. ولنا قوله عليها: "اقرؤا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به، وفي آخر ما عهد رسول الله إلى عثمان بن أبي العاص: "وإن اتخذت مؤذنا فلا تأخذ على الأذان أجرا؛ ولأن القربة متى حصلت وقعت عن العامل، ولهذا تعتبر أهليته، فلا يجوز أخذ الأجر من غيره كما في الصوم والصلاة؛ ولأن التعليم مما لا يقدر المعلم عليه إلا بمعنى من قبل المتعلم، فيكون ملزما
And cupping, and no wage for the stud fee of a goat, neither for the call to prayer (adhan), nor for hajj, nor for leading prayer (imamah), nor for teaching Quran, nor for fiqh. Commentary: Cupping: i.e., it is permissible to take the wage for cupping; because it is narrated that he (the Prophet) was cupped and gave the cupper his wage. And custom has continued accordingly from the time of the Messenger of Allah to this day, so it became a consensus. The Zahiriyyah said: it is not permissible; due to the narration that he forbade the stud fee of a goat, the earnings of a cupper, and the measure of a miller. We say: this hadith is abrogated; because it is narrated that a man said to him: I have dependents and a slave who is a cupper, may I feed my dependents from his earnings? He said... (Tatimmat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/38). Al-Fath said: If you say: Since the hadith was abrogated, the non-permissibility in the stud fee of a goat and the miller's measure is problematic. I say: The abrogation is only regarding the earnings of the cupper, not absolutely. This is what appeared to me, then I saw explicit mention in the words of al-Zayla'i. Praise be to Allah. I say: The reason for mentioning this issue in this chapter, even though it is valid, is because of the difference of opinion regarding its validity and invalidity. Yes. The forbidden (suht) stud fee of a goat: The goat is the male, when a year has passed over it; the intended meaning is the stallion absolutely. Al-Asb means mating, or its fluid. In al-Sihah: Al-Asb is the rent taken for the mating of a stallion. (Fath) i.e., if someone hires a stallion to cover females, it is not valid for the owner to take the fee; due to his saying: 'Indeed from the goat', and the fee of the prostitute, and because its intended fruit is unknown, since it may impregnate or not, so it is gharar; and because his fluid has no value; and because the owner has undertaken what he cannot deliver. Thus in al-Fath, al-Hamawi from al-Birjandi. I say: This contract is of the invalid (batil) contracts, not corrupt (fasid), as understood from the reasoning for its invalidity. Pay attention. And the call to prayer etc.: (by jar, particle, connected to 'stud') i.e., it is not valid to take a wage for the call to prayer, and similarly for hajj, leading prayer, teaching Quran and fiqh; because these are acts of worship, and every act of worship that is specific to a Muslim to perform, it is not valid to take a wage for it. The scenario is that he says: I hire you for such-and-such to perform hajj for me or to call the adhan. But if he commands him to perform hajj or the adhan without mentioning a lease, it is permissible. Al-Hidayah says: The principle: Every act of worship that is specific to the Muslim is not permissible to lease him for it according to us. According to al-Shafi'i: It is valid in everything that is not obligatory upon the hiree, because it is a lease for a known action not specifically incumbent on him, so it is valid. Our proof is his saying: 'Read the Quran and do not eat by means of it,' and in the last testament of the Messenger of Allah to Uthman ibn Abi al-'As: 'If you appoint a mu'adhdhin, do not take a wage for the adhan;' and because whenever an act of worship occurs, it takes place for the doer, and therefore his eligibility is considered; it is not valid to take a wage from someone else like in fasting and prayer; and because teaching is something the teacher cannot do except with the consent of the learner, so it becomes binding.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of taking wages for certain services. It first addresses cupping (hijama), which the Hanafi school permits based on the Prophet's practice and continuous custom, despite a conflicting hadith that was abrogated. The Zahiris disagreed. Then it discusses the stud fee of a goat ('asb al-tays), which is prohibited because it involves gharar (uncertainty whether fertilization occurs) and the fluid has no recognized value; the contract is considered batil (void), not merely fasid. Finally, it covers wages for acts of worship: adhan, hajj, imamah, teaching Quran and fiqh. According to the Hanafi school, these are not permitted because they are acts of worship specific to the performer, and any benefit goes to the doer, not the payer. The Shafi'i school differs, allowing wages for such acts if they are not obligatory upon the hiree. The Hanafi proofs include hadith forbidding eating by means of the Quran and the Prophet's instruction to Uthman not to take wages for adhan. The passage also clarifies that if one simply asks someone to perform hajj or adhan without a formal lease, it is permissible to give compensation as a gift, not as a wage. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah; the mufta bihi is the Hanafi position that these must be done for free.

Key Terms
عسب التيس (asb al-tays): The fee taken for allowing a male goat (or any male animal) to mate with females.
سحت (suht): Forbidden (haram) earnings; specifically used for ill-gotten gain from unlawful transactions like stud fees and prostitution.
طاعة (ta'a): Act of worship (obedience to Allah). In this context, acts that bring reward and are specific to Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it takes too much time and cannot be quantified.
D) Because the caller must be a male Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits wages for acts of worship because they are personal to the performer; the only permissible compensation is a voluntary gift.
