Three Cases of Invalid Hire: Cupping, Stallion Breeding, and Acts of Worship
States and proves rulings on three types of invalid hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on each of three types of hire (cupping, stallion breeding, and worship acts), identify the proof for each, and explain why the ruling for teaching Quran was later modified.

Core Idea
Cupping hire is valid by consensus; stallion breeding is void by gharar; worship hire is invalid because reward belongs to the doer, not the payer.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents three distinct rulings on invalid hire (ijarah fasidah). Each ruling is supported by hadith proofs and demonstrates how the Hanafi school applies principles of gharar, the nature of worship, and the role of necessity. You will learn not only the rulings but also how later scholars adapted one of them for practical need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
Read the passage and extract the three distinct scenarios discussed: cupping, stallion breeding, and acts of worship (adhan, Hajj, imamah, teaching Quran/fiqh).
Each case has a different ruling and reasoning.
2
Extract the ruling for each case
Note the legal classification: cupping hire is valid (sahih); stallion breeding is invalid (batil); acts of worship are originally invalid (fasid) but with a later exception for teaching Quran.
The passage uses both 'fasid' and 'batil'; the author clarifies that stallion breeding is batil (void) not just fasid.
3
Locate the dalil for each ruling
Find the evidence cited: for cupping, the Prophet's practice and consensus; for stallion, the hadith forbidding 'asb al-tays and reasoning of gharar; for worship, the hadiths 'Recite Quran and do not eat by it' and the covenant to Uthman regarding adhan.
The Hanafis respond to the Zahiri objection by claiming the hadith against cupping is abrogated.
4
Examine the inter-madhhab disputes
The passage mentions the Zahiris who oppose hire for cupping and the Shafi'is who allow hire for non-obligatory acts of worship. Understand their proofs and the Hanafi responses.
This step helps in comparative fiqh analysis.
5
Note the later fatwa change
The final sentence states that the fatwa today permits hiring for teaching Quran but not for singing and wailing. Understand why necessity (darurah) allowed this exception, and that it does not abrogate the original principle.
This illustrates how Hanafi fiqh adapts to practical needs without discarding foundational rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإجارة الفاسدة
كتاب الإجارة
١٦٠
والحجام، لا أجرة عسب التيس والأذان والحج والإمامة وتعليم القرآن والفقه،
- الجهالة؛ لأنها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة، والنساء فيه كالرجال هو الصحيح؛ للحاجة، بل حاجتهن أكثر؛ لكثرة أسباب اغتسالهن، وكراهة عثمان محمول على ما فيه من كشف العورة، قاله في الدر" و"الزيلعي"، وفي "الأشباه": يكره له دخول الحمام في ،قول وقيل إلا لمريضة أو نفساء، والمعتمد عدم الكراهة مطلقا قلت ولا شك في زماننا في الكراهة؛ لتحقق كشف العورة، كذا في "الدر". (ملتقط من الفتح والتكملة و رد المحتار) والحجام: أي جاز أخذ أجرة الحجام؛ لما روي أنه عليها احتجم وأعطى الحجام أجرته، وبه جرى التعارف بيز الناس من لدن رسول الله الله إلى يومنا هذا، فانعقد إجماعا، وقالت الظاهرية: لا يجوز؛ لما روي أنه عليها نهى عن عسب التيس وكسب الحجام وقفيز الطحان قلنا هذا الحديث منسوخ؛ لما روي أنه عليه قال له رجل: إن لي عيالا وغلاما حجاما، أفأطعم عيالي من کسبه؟ قال: تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٨/٨] قال في "الفتح": فإن قلت: حيث كان الحديث منسوخا فعدم الجواز في عسب التيس وقفيز الطحان مشكل. قلت: النسخ بالنسبة لكسب الحجام فقط لا مطلقا، هذا ما ظهر لي ثم رأيت التصريح به في كلام الزيلعي والله الحمد انتهى أقول ووجه ذكر هذه المسألة في هذا الباب مع أنها صحيحة كون الاختلاف في صحتها وفساده
نعم.
السحت عسب
كما مر مشروحا. عسب التيس [التيس هو الذكر من المعز إذا حال عليه الحول والمراد الفحل مطلقا. والعسب: ضرابه ويقال ماؤه كذا في "الصحاح" وذكر في المجمل أن العسب الكراء الذي يؤخذ على ضراب الفحل. (فتح)] أي إذ استأجر أحد فحلا لينزو على الإناث، فلا يصح للمؤجر أخذ الأجرة؛ لقوله عليه: "إن من التيس، ومهر البغي، ولأن ثمرته المقصودة غير معلومة؛ لأنه قد يلقح، وقد لا يلقح، فهو غرر؛ ولأنه لا قيم لمائه؛ ولأن المؤجر التزم ما لا قدرة له على تسليمه، كذا في "الفتح" "الحموي" عن "البرجندي"، أقول: إن هذا العقد من العقود الباطلة لا الفاسدة كما يفهم من تعليل عدم صحته، فتنبه له. والأذان إلخ : [ بالجر عطف على "عسب" وكذا ما بعده إلى قوله: "والفقه". (عيني)] أي لا يصح أخذ الأجر على الأذان وكذا الحج والإمامة وتعليم القرآن والفقه؛ لأن هذه طاعات، وكل طاعة يختص بأدائها مسلم لا يصح
عن
أخذ الأجر عليها. وصورة المسألة أن يقول : استأجرتك بكذا على أن تحج عني أو تؤذن أما إذا أمره بالحج أو الأذان من غير ذكر الإجارة، فيجوز، قال في "الهداية": والأصل: أن كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم لا يجوز الاستئجار عليه عندنا، وعند
الشافعي: يصح في كل ما لا يتعين على الأجير؛ لأنه استئجار على عمل معلوم غير متعين عليه، فيجوز. ولنا قوله عليها: "اقرؤا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به، وفي آخر ما عهد رسول الله إلى عثمان بن أبي العاص: "وإن اتخذت مؤذنا فلا تأخذ على الأذان أجرا؛ ولأن القربة متى حصلت وقعت عن العامل، ولهذا تعتبر أهليته، فلا يجوز أخذ الأجر من غيره كما في الصوم والصلاة؛ ولأن التعليم مما لا يقدر المعلم عليه إلا بمعنى من قبل المتعلم، فيكون ملزما =
ما لا يقدر على تسليمه، فلا يصح. انتهى
والفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن ولا يجوز على الغناء، والنوح
The invalid hire. Book of Hire. 160. And the cupper, and there is no hire for the stallion's stud fee, and the call to prayer, Hajj, leading prayer, teaching Quran and jurisprudence. Cupping: meaning it is permissible to take the hire of the cupper; because it is related that he (peace be upon him) was cupped and gave the cupper his wage, and customaries have continued among people from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to our day, so it has become as if there is consensus. The Zahiris said: It is not permissible; because it is related that he (peace be upon him) forbade the stud fee of the goat, the earning of the cupper, and the miller's measure. We say: This hadith is abrogated; because it is related that he (peace be upon him) said to a man: I have dependents and a cupper slave, should I feed my family from his earnings? [Then commentary on abrogation only for cupping]. The stallion's stud fee: meaning if someone hires a stallion to mount females, it is not valid for the owner to take the hire; because of his saying: 'Indeed, from the goat (i.e., its stud fee) and the prostitute's dowry', and because its intended outcome is unknown; for it may impregnate and may not, so it is a gamble; and because his fluid has no value; and because the owner undertook what he cannot deliver. The call to prayer etc.: meaning it is not valid to take hire for the call to prayer, Hajj, leading prayer, teaching Quran and jurisprudence; because these are acts of worship, and every act of worship specific to a Muslim, it is not valid to take hire for it. The scenario is that he says: I hire you for such-and-such to perform Hajj for me or to call the adhan. But if he orders him to do Hajj or adhan without mentioning hire, it is permissible. Al-Hidayah says: The principle is that every act of worship specific to a Muslim, hiring for it is not valid according to us; according to al-Shafi'i, it is valid in everything that is not incumbent upon the hiree; because it is hiring for a known work not incumbent upon him, so it is valid. Our proof is his saying: 'Recite the Quran and do not eat by it', and in the last covenant of the Messenger of Allah to Uthman ibn Abi al-As: 'If you appoint a mu'adhdhin, do not take a hire for the adhan'; and because a devotional act when performed, it is performed for the doer, so his eligibility is considered, so taking hire from another is not permissible as in fasting and prayer; and because teaching is something the teacher cannot do except by the understanding of the student, so it is binding on what he cannot deliver, so it is not valid. The fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran, and it is not permissible for singing and wailing.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers three distinct rulings on invalid hire (ijarah fasidah). First, hiring a cupper (hijamah) is valid. The author provides proof: the Prophet himself was cupped and paid the cupper, and this practice has continued by consensus. The Zahiri school objects citing a hadith forbidding the cupper's earnings, but the Hanafis respond that this hadith is abrogated by later practice and another hadith where the Prophet permitted feeding one's family from a cupper slave's earnings. Second, hiring a stallion for breeding is invalid. The author lists reasons: the hadith forbidding such earnings, the uncertainty of fertilization (gharar), the valuelessness of the fluid, and the inability to guarantee delivery. He notes this is a batil (void) contract, not merely fasid. Third, hiring for acts of worship specific to Muslims—adhan, Hajj, imamah, teaching Quran and fiqh—is invalid. The Hanafis base this on hadiths forbidding payment for Quran recitation and adhan, and on the principle that devotional acts belong to the doer; one cannot be paid for another's worship. The Shafi'i school disagrees, allowing hire for non-obligatory acts, but the Hanafis hold firmly to their view. However, the author notes that the current fatwa (from later Hanafi scholars) permits hiring for teaching Quran due to necessity, but not for singing and wailing (which are sinful). This reflects the Hanafi juristic shift from original ruling to practical accommodation.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijārah al-fāsidah): A contract of hire that is invalid due to a defect in the subject matter or consideration, but not fundamentally void (batil).
عسب التيس (asb al-tays): The fee paid for breeding a male goat/stallion with females; considered invalid hire.
طاعة (ṭāʿah): An act of worship or obedience to Allah that is specific to Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafis consider hiring for adhan invalid, according to this passage?
A) Because adhan is a communal obligation and cannot be delegated.
B) Because the Prophet forbade taking hire for adhan in his covenant to Uthman.
C) Because the adhan is a ritual that must be performed with pure intention.
D) Because the mu'adhdhin must be trustworthy and payment compromises that.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hire for cupping by consensus but invalidates hire for stallion breeding due to gharar and hire for devotional acts because the reward belongs to the doer; however, a later fatwa permits teaching Quran due to necessity.

The Hanafi Rule: Hiring for Worship-Specific Acts is Void
States the Hanafi rule on hiring for worship and its exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that hiring for acts of worship specific to Muslims is void (batil) and identify which acts qualify as such.

Core Idea
Hiring for personal worship is void because reward cannot be transferred.

This lesson establishes the foundational Hanafi principle on hiring for worship. The rule is clear: any contract for an act of worship that only a Muslim can perform is void. But what counts as worship? Let's examine the definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Rule
Locate the phrase that states the general rule on hiring for worship-specific acts.
The phrase 'كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم فالاستئجار باطل'
2
Define 'ṭāʿah yakhtaṣṣu bihā al-muslim'
Determine what acts fall under this category. Think of acts like prayer, fasting, Hajj, and teaching Quran.
These are acts that are both devotional (qurbah) and exclusive to Muslims.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The text mentions a reasoning (ta'lil): when a devotional act is performed, its reward goes to the doer. If hired, the reward would go to the hirer, which is impossible.
This reasoning is contested in the Hajj case, as we'll see.
4
Note the Consequence: Batil
The contract for such hire is batil (void ab initio), meaning it has no legal effect; no fee is owed.
This is distinct from fasid (invalid but potentially correctable).
5
Contrast with Exceptions
Briefly note that building mosques and bridges are exceptions, but we will explore them in the next lesson.
This prepares for the expansion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المذهب عندنا: أن كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم فالاستئجار باطل، بخلاف بناء المساجد والقناطر، ويشكل على تعليلهم بأن القربة إذا صدرت من أهلها وقعت عنه، فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة من غيره الحج عن الغير؛ لأنه يقع عن الأمر على الصحيح مع أن نية الأمر ليست بشرط، وكان العامل عاملا لآمره لا لنفسه مع أنه طاعة، وعلى قول محمد: لا يقع له إلا ثواب النفقة، فيبقى الإشكال بأن ثوابه وقع لغير الفاعل مع أنه قربة، فيشكل على قولهم: "القربة متى وقعت يقع ثوابها لفاعلها لا لغيره، وتخصيص تعليم القرآن والفقه يشير إلى أنه لو استأجر لتعليم الخط أو الكتابة أو علم الأدب أو الشعر أو الحساب أو الطب جاز كذا في "الفتح" و"ملا مسكين".
Then the school (madhhab) according to us: that every act of worship specific to a Muslim, hiring for it is void, unlike building mosques and bridges. And it is problematic for their reasoning that when a devotional act is performed by its people, it is performed for them, so it is not permissible to take hire from another, like Hajj on behalf of another; because it is performed for the one who ordered it according to the sound view, even though the intention of the orderer is not a condition, and the worker works for his orderer not for himself even though it is an act of worship. And according to Muhammad, he only gets the reward of expenditure, so the difficulty remains that its reward goes to other than the doer even though it is a devotional act, so it is problematic for their statement: 'When a devotional act occurs, its reward falls for its doer, not for others.' And the specification of teaching Quran and jurisprudence indicates that if he hires for teaching handwriting, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, or medicine, it is permissible, as in al-Fath and Mulla Miskeen.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on hiring for acts of worship. The core rule: any act of worship specific to Muslims (like prayer, fasting, Hajj, Quran teaching) cannot be hired out; such contracts are batil (void). The exception is building mosques and bridges, which are instrumental in worship but not worship themselves. The author then addresses a potential contradiction: if devotional acts cannot be hired, how can one hire someone to perform Hajj on behalf of another? He explains that in Hajj, the performer does it on behalf of the hirer, so the reward goes to the hirer, not the performer—contrary to the general principle. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the performer only gets the reward of expenditure (thawab al-nafaqah). This shows the complexity: the principle that reward belongs to the doer has exceptions. The passage also clarifies that hiring for secular skills like calligraphy, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, and medicine is permissible because they are not acts of worship specific to Muslims.

Key Terms
طاعة يختص بها المسلم (ṭāʿah yakhtaṣṣu bihā al-muslim): An act of worship that is specific to Muslims, such as prayer, fasting, Hajj, Quran teaching.
باطل (bāṭil): Void contract with no legal effect; cannot be validated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following contracts is batil?
A) Hiring a builder to construct a mosque.
B) Hiring a teacher to teach Quran.
C) Hiring a doctor to treat a patient.
D) Hiring a calligrapher to write a book.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: any contract for an act of worship specific to Muslims is void; only means-to-worship or secular acts can be hired.

The Exception of Mosques and the Hajj Dispute
Discusses exceptions to the hiring rule and the Hajj paradox.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why building mosques and bridges is an exception to the hiring rule, and analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on hiring for Hajj.

Core Idea
Means to worship can be hired; but Hajj on behalf of another creates a paradox.

The previous lesson established the rule against hiring for worship-specific acts. But the text notes exceptions: building mosques and bridges are permissible. More perplexing is the case of Hajj on behalf of another, which appears to contradict the general principle. In this lesson, we examine these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Exception
Find the phrase that introduces an exception to the general rule: 'بخلاف بناء المساجد والقناطر'.
Building mosques and bridges are means to worship, not worship itself.
2
Understand Why They Are Excepted
These acts are not worship-specific; they are instrumental. The reward for building is separate from the act of worship performed in the mosque.
This distinction is crucial for analogizing to modern projects.
3
Locate the Hajj Issue
The author says hiring for Hajj on behalf of another is problematic for the reasoning. Identify the sentence starting with 'ويشكل على تعليلهم'.
Hajj is worship-specific, yet hiring it is considered valid.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Two views: Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf say the reward goes to the hirer; Muhammad says the performer only gets reward for expenditure.
Both agree the contract is not batil, but the reward distribution differs.
5
Evaluate the Reasoning Challenge
If the general rule is that reward goes to the doer, how can Hajj hiring be valid? The text presents this as a problem (إشكال).
This shows that the rule has limits; the exception for Hajj is based on special evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المذهب عندنا: أن كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم فالاستئجار باطل، بخلاف بناء المساجد والقناطر، ويشكل على تعليلهم بأن القربة إذا صدرت من أهلها وقعت عنه، فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة من غيره الحج عن الغير؛ لأنه يقع عن الأمر على الصحيح مع أن نية الأمر ليست بشرط، وكان العامل عاملا لآمره لا لنفسه مع أنه طاعة، وعلى قول محمد: لا يقع له إلا ثواب النفقة، فيبقى الإشكال بأن ثوابه وقع لغير الفاعل مع أنه قربة، فيشكل على قولهم: "القربة متى وقعت يقع ثوابها لفاعلها لا لغيره، وتخصيص تعليم القرآن والفقه يشير إلى أنه لو استأجر لتعليم الخط أو الكتابة أو علم الأدب أو الشعر أو الحساب أو الطب جاز كذا في "الفتح" و"ملا مسكين".
Then the school (madhhab) according to us: that every act of worship specific to a Muslim, hiring for it is void, unlike building mosques and bridges. And it is problematic for their reasoning that when a devotional act is performed by its people, it is performed for them, so it is not permissible to take hire from another, like Hajj on behalf of another; because it is performed for the one who ordered it according to the sound view, even though the intention of the orderer is not a condition, and the worker works for his orderer not for himself even though it is an act of worship. And according to Muhammad, he only gets the reward of expenditure, so the difficulty remains that its reward goes to other than the doer even though it is a devotional act, so it is problematic for their statement: 'When a devotional act occurs, its reward falls for its doer, not for others.' And the specification of teaching Quran and jurisprudence indicates that if he hires for teaching handwriting, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, or medicine, it is permissible, as in al-Fath and Mulla Miskeen.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on hiring for acts of worship. The core rule: any act of worship specific to Muslims (like prayer, fasting, Hajj, Quran teaching) cannot be hired out; such contracts are batil (void). The exception is building mosques and bridges, which are instrumental in worship but not worship themselves. The author then addresses a potential contradiction: if devotional acts cannot be hired, how can one hire someone to perform Hajj on behalf of another? He explains that in Hajj, the performer does it on behalf of the hirer, so the reward goes to the hirer, not the performer—contrary to the general principle. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the performer only gets the reward of expenditure (thawab al-nafaqah). This shows the complexity: the principle that reward belongs to the doer has exceptions. The passage also clarifies that hiring for secular skills like calligraphy, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, and medicine is permissible because they are not acts of worship specific to Muslims.

Key Terms
نيابة (niyābah): Proxy; representation in acts of worship, specifically Hajj.
ثواب النفقة (thawāb al-nafaqah): The reward for the expenditure incurred in performing the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Building mosques/bridges is an exception because they are means, not worship; Hajj on behalf is a special exception with an intra-Hanafi reward dispute.

Permissible Hiring: Secular Skills and Worldly Acts
Specifies permissible hiring for secular skills and the underlying distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between worship-specific acts and secular acts in the context of hiring, and apply the rule to determine validity of contracts for various skills.

Core Idea
Any skill that is not exclusive to Muslim worship can be hired; the line is drawn by intent.

The passage concludes by specifying that teaching Quran and jurisprudence are worship-specific, but teaching secular skills like handwriting, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, and medicine is permissible. This lesson explores the distinction and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Specific Examples
Find the list of permissible skills: teaching handwriting (الخط), writing (الكتابة), literature (علم الأدب), poetry (الشعر), arithmetic (الحساب), medicine (الطب).
These are all worldly sciences (ʻulūm dunyawiyyah).
2
Understand the Principle of Distinction
The key is whether the act is an act of worship specific to Muslims (ṭāʿah yakhtaṣṣu bihā al-muslim) or a general worldly benefit.
Teaching Quran is worship-specific because it involves the word of Allah and is a form of devotion.
3
Apply the Rule to New Examples
Use the rule to determine if hiring for a skill like calligraphy (artistic writing) is valid. Calligraphy can be secular or religious depending on intent.
The text specifically allows 'khatt' (handwriting) which implies secular script.
4
Note the Source Authority
The author cites al-Fath and Mulla Miskeen as sources for the permissibility of hiring for these skills.
This shows the ruling is from later Hanafi fatwa literature (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
5
Review the Rationale
These skills are not inherently worship; they are worldly tools that can be used for good or bad. Their permissibility in hiring is based on their neutral nature.
This contrasts with acts like prayer, which are inherently worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المذهب عندنا: أن كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم فالاستئجار باطل، بخلاف بناء المساجد والقناطر، ويشكل على تعليلهم بأن القربة إذا صدرت من أهلها وقعت عنه، فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة من غيره الحج عن الغير؛ لأنه يقع عن الأمر على الصحيح مع أن نية الأمر ليست بشرط، وكان العامل عاملا لآمره لا لنفسه مع أنه طاعة، وعلى قول محمد: لا يقع له إلا ثواب النفقة، فيبقى الإشكال بأن ثوابه وقع لغير الفاعل مع أنه قربة، فيشكل على قولهم: "القربة متى وقعت يقع ثوابها لفاعلها لا لغيره، وتخصيص تعليم القرآن والفقه يشير إلى أنه لو استأجر لتعليم الخط أو الكتابة أو علم الأدب أو الشعر أو الحساب أو الطب جاز كذا في "الفتح" و"ملا مسكين".

The author then addresses a potential contradiction: if devotional acts cannot be hired, how can one hire someone to perform Hajj on behalf of another? He explains that in Hajj, the performer does it on behalf of the hirer, so the reward goes to the hirer, not the performer—contrary to the general principle. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the performer only gets the reward of expenditure (thawab al-nafaqah). This shows the complexity: the principle that reward belongs to the doer has exceptions. The passage also clarifies that hiring for secular skills like calligraphy, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, and medicine is permissible because they are not acts of worship specific to Muslims.

Key Terms
تعليم الخط (taʿlīm al-khaṭṭ): Teaching handwriting/calligraphy as a secular art.
تعليم القرآن (taʿlīm al-Qurʾān): Teaching the Quran as a devotional act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, which of the following is permissible to be hired for?
A) Teaching the Quran.
B) Teaching Islamic jurisprudence (fiqh).
C) Teaching arithmetic.
D) Leading prayers in a mosque.

Key Takeaway
Any skill not exclusive to Muslim worship can be hired; the list includes handwriting, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, and medicine.

Later Hanafi Fatwa on Hiring for Teaching Quran and Religious Duties
Later Hanafi fatwa on hire for teaching and religious duties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the later Hanafi position allowing hire for teaching Quran and religious duties, and explain the rationale of necessity (darurah).

Core Idea
Necessity permits hire for worship when religious knowledge risks being lost.

This passage presents a landmark later Hanafi fatwa that permitted hiring for teaching Quran, leading prayer, and similar religious duties. The original school position prohibited such contracts, but later scholars from Balkh invoked istihsan (juridical preference) and darurah (necessity) due to the decline in volunteerism and the risk of religious knowledge being lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original Hanafi position
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) originally held that hiring for acts of worship (teaching Quran, imamah) is not permissible—the contract is batil (void).
This is the qawl qadim (old view).
2
Identify the later fatwa and its proponents
The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) of Balkh gave a fatwa allowing hire for teaching Quran, fiqh, imamah, adhan, iqamah, and preaching. They relied on istihsan and necessity.
These are the fuqaha of Balkh, known for their practical approach.
3
Understand the rationale (istihsan + darurah)
The reason cited is 'khashyat dhiya' al-Qur'an' (fear of loss of the Quran) due to people's laziness and disinclination to volunteer. Necessity justifies deviating from the original ruling.
This is a clear application of usul al-fiqh: necessity overrides prohibition (al-daruratu tubihu al-mahzurat).
4
Note the scope and conditions
The permissibility extends to teaching Quran and fiqh, imamah, adhan, iqamah, and preaching. However, it does not extend to hiring a mushaf (Quran copy) or books of fiqh because there is no custom ('adam al-ta'aruf).
The exception shows that the ruling is limited to services, not objects.
5
Recognize the disputed sub-issue: Quran recitation at graves
The passage mentions a difference of opinion on hiring for reciting Quran at the grave. Some permit it, but others (including Ibn Abidin and Taj al-Shari'ah) strongly forbid it, stating that no reward is earned.
This sub-issue remains controversial and not part of the settled fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على جواز الاستئجار : هذا هو مذهب المتأخرين من مشايخ بلخ استحسنوا ذلك؛ لظهور التواني في الأمور الدينية، وكسل الناس في الاحتساب، وكذا يجوز على الإمامة في هذا اليوم؛ لأن للأئمة كانت لهم عطيات في بيت المال، وانقطعت اليوم بسبب استيلاء الظلمة عليها، وفي روضة الزندويستي : كان شيخنا أبو محمد عبد . الخيز اخزي يقول: في زماننا يجوز للإمام والمؤذن والمعلم أخذ الأجرة، ولا يجوز استئجار المصحف وكتب الفقه؛ لعدم التعارف. (عيني) لتعليم القرآن: اعلم أن في أكثر المتون اقتصروا على ذكر تعليم القرآن لكن زيد عليه كما في "الدر المختار" وغيره تعليم الفقه والإمامة والأذان والإقامة والوعظ، فهذا مجموع ما أفتى به المتأخرون من مشايخنا، وهم البلخيون على خلاف ما ذهب إليه الإمام وصاحباه واتفقت كلمتهم في الشروح والفتاوى على التعليل بالضرورة، وهي خشية ضياع القرآن وصرحوا بأن أصل المذهب عدم الجواز.
الله
قال في "الفتح" نقلا عن "الجوهرة": واختلفوا في الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن على القبر مدة معلومة، والمختار أنه يجوز، ورده في رد المحتار" بكلام طويل، وقال قد أطنب في رده صاحب "تبيين" المحارم" مستندا إلى النقول الصريحة، فمن جملة كلامه قال تاج الشريعة في شرح "الهداية": إن القرآن بالأجرة لا يستحق الثواب لا للميت ولا للقاري. وقال العيني في شرح الهداية: ويمنع القاري للدنيا والآخذ والمعطي آلمان انتهى بقدر الحاجة، والتفصيل فيه فليطالع لمه.
ولا يجوز على الغناء [البكاء على الميت وتعديد محاسنه] لأنها معصية، وعقد الإجارة يستحق بها تسليم المعقود عليه شرعا ولا يجوز أن يستحق على المرء شيء يكون به عاصيا؛ كي لا تصير المعصية مضافة إلى الشرع، فلا يجب الأجر بهذا العقد، وإن أعطاء الأجر وقبضه لا يحل له ويجب عليه رده على صاحبه، وفي "شرح الكافي": لا تجوز الإجارة على شيء من الغناء والنوح والمزامير والطبل أو شيء من اللهو، ولا على الحداء وقراءة الشعر ولا غيره، ولا أجر في ذلك، والطبل إنما كان منهيا إذا كان للهو، أما إذا كان لغيره فلا بأس به كطبل الغزاة وطبل العرس والقافلة من العيني وحواشي الهداية)
On the permissibility of hiring: This is the madhhab of the later scholars from the mashayikh of Balkh; they deemed it good (istihsan) due to the apparent laziness in religious matters and people's disinclination to volunteer. Similarly, it is permissible for imamah today because imams used to receive stipends from the treasury, but these have been cut off due to tyrants' takeover. In Rawdat al-Zandawisti: Our teacher Abu Muhammad Abd al-Khayr al-Azji used to say: In our time, it is permissible for the imam, mu'adhdhin, and teacher to take payment, but it is not permissible to hire a mushaf or books of fiqh due to lack of custom. (Ayni) For teaching the Quran: Know that most texts restricted to teaching Quran, but it has been added, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others, teaching fiqh, imamah, adhan, iqamah, and preaching. This is the total of what the later scholars from our mashayikh, the Balkhis, gave fatwa on, contrary to what Imam (Abu Hanifa) and his two companions held. And their word agreed in the commentaries and fatwas on the reasoning of necessity, which is fear of the loss of the Quran, and they affirmed that the original madhhab is non-permissibility. Allah. Al-Fath quoted from al-Jawharah: They differed about hiring for recitation of Quran at the grave for a known period; the chosen view is that it is permissible. But this was rejected by Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar with long discussion. The author of Tabyin al-Maharam went into detail refuting it with clear texts. Among his statements: Taj al-Shari'ah in his commentary on al-Hidayah said: Indeed, the Quran recited for payment does not earn reward neither for the deceased nor for the reciter. Al-Ayni in his commentary on al-Hidayah said: The reciter for worldly gain is forbidden, and both the taker and giver are sinners. End as needed, and the details should be studied. And it is not permissible for singing [wailing over the deceased and enumerating their virtues] because it is sin, and the contract of hire requires the delivery of the contracted object lawfully, and it is not permissible that a person becomes sinful through it, so that sin not be attributed to the Shariah. So no wage is obligatory by this contract, and if he gives the wage and takes it, it is not lawful for him and he must return it to its owner. In Sharh al-Kafi: Hiring is not permissible for anything of singing, wailing, flutes, drums, or anything of amusement, nor for driving camels with song or reciting poetry, etc., and there is no wage in that. The drum is only prohibited if it is for amusement; if for other purposes, there is no harm, like the drum of warriors, wedding, and caravan, from al-Ayni and margins of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents the later Hanafi fatwa (from the Balkhi scholars) that allows hiring for teaching Quran, leading prayer, adhan, etc., due to necessity — people are too lazy to volunteer, and religious knowledge risks being lost. This is istihsan (juridical preference), and it contradicts the original Hanafi position of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The fatwa also extends to imamah because imams no longer receive state stipends. However, hiring for reciting Quran at graves is controversial; some permit it, others forbid it, with strong opinions that such recitation earns no reward. The passage then addresses hiring for singing and wailing (over the dead): it is strictly prohibited because it is a sin. The reason is that a hire contract cannot obligate sinful acts, as that would impute sin to the Shariah. If someone pays for such services, the payment is unlawful and must be returned. Instruments like drums are only prohibited if used for amusement; drums for war, weddings, or caravans are allowed.

Key Terms
الاستئجار (al-istiʼjār): Hiring; a contract of lease or employment for a specific benefit.
استحسان (istihsān): Juridical preference; departing from a clear analogy based on a stronger consideration (e.g., necessity or custom).
ضرورة (ḍarūrah): Necessity that permits the otherwise forbidden; here, the risk of losing Quranic knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Balkhi scholars allow hiring for teaching Quran despite the original prohibition?
A) They found a hadith permitting it.
B) They feared the Quran would be lost if people were not paid to teach it.
C) Imam Abu Hanifa changed his view later.
D) The government required it.

Key Takeaway
The original Hanafi prohibition on hire for worship was relaxed by later scholars due to necessity (darurah), making it permissible today to pay for teaching Quran and religious duties.

Prohibition of Hiring for Singing and Wailing
Prohibition of hiring for singing and wailing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why hiring for singing and wailing is void in Hanafi law and identify the exceptions for drums.

Core Idea
A hire contract for sin is void because it would attribute sin to the Shariah.

This passage addresses the prohibition of hiring for singing, wailing over the dead, and other forms of amusement. The Hanafi ruling is clear: such contracts are void because the subject matter is sinful. The payment must be returned. However, drums for legitimate purposes like war, weddings, and caravans are exempt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited activities
The passage lists singing (ghina'), wailing (nuh) over the dead, flutes (mazamir), drums (tabl) for amusement, driving camels with song (hida'), and reciting poetry for entertainment. All are considered sin (ma'siyah).
The focus is on hire for these acts.
2
Understand the legal reason
The reason given: a hire contract requires delivery of a permissible (halal) benefit. A sinful act cannot be contracted because it would impute that sin to the Shariah (fi iḍāfat al-ma'siyah ilā al-shar').
This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi muamalat.
3
State the consequence of the void contract
The contract is batil (void). No wage is obligatory. If payment has been given and taken, it must be returned (it is not halal for the recipient).
The recipient is a sinner for taking payment for sin.
4
Recognize the exception: drums for non-amusement
Drums are only prohibited when used for amusement (lahw). They are allowed for war (tabl al-ghuzat), weddings (tabl al-'urs), and caravans (tabl al-qafilah).
The exception shows that the prohibition depends on intention and usage.

Hiring for Teaching the Quran: The Hanafi Shift from Prohibition to Permissibility
States the contemporary fatwa and Hanafi principle on hiring for religious acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on hiring for teaching the Quran, explain the later fatwa of permissibility, and identify the reasoning based on necessity.

Core Idea
Teaching Quran is a non-hireable act of worship, but later scholars permitted it to prevent its loss.

Can a teacher be paid to teach the Quran? The Hanafi school initially held that acts of worship specific to Muslims cannot be hired for. However, a later shift in fatwa permitted it due to the necessity of preserving Quranic knowledge. In this lesson, we trace the original principle, the intra-madhhab dispute, and the reasoning behind the ruling that prevails today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contemporary fatwa
Note that the passage opens with: 'The fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran, and it is not permissible for singing.' This is the operative ruling.
The ruling distinguishes between permissible (Quran teaching) and impermissible (singing).
2
Understand the original Hanafi principle
The text states: 'every act of obedience specific to a Muslim, hiring for it is invalid.' This is the foundational principle from the founding imams.
Exceptions like building mosques/bridges are noted, but teaching the Quran is not an exception in the original view.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
The original position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds hiring for teaching invalid. The later Balkhi scholars issued a fatwa of permissibility due to necessity.
The necessity is 'fear of loss of the Quran' due to people's laziness in voluntary teaching.
4
Examine the reasoning and qualifiers
The text discusses the problematic analogy with Hajj and then specifies that teaching calligraphy, writing, etc., is permissible. This shows that only purely religious acts are contested.
The later fatwa also extends to imamah, adhan, etc., under the same necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن ولا يجوز على الغناء، والنوح = ما لا يقدر على تسليمه، فلا يصح. انتهى. الإجارة. ثم المذهب عندنا: أن كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم فالاستئجار باطل، بخلاف بناء المساجد والقناطر، ويشكل على تعليلهم بأن القربة إذا صدرت من أهلها وقعت عنه، فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة من غيره الحج عن الغير؛ لأنه يقع عن الأمر على الصحيح مع أن نية الأمر ليست بشرط، وكان العامل عاملا لآمره لا لنفسه مع أنه طاعة، وعلى قول محمد: لا يقع له إلا ثواب النفقة، فيبقى الإشكال بأن ثوابه وقع لغير الفاعل مع أنه قربة، فيشكل على قولهم: "القربة متى وقعت يقع ثوابها لفاعلها لا لغيره، وتخصيص تعليم القرآن والفقه يشير إلى أنه لو استأجر لتعليم الخط أو الكتابة أو علم الأدب أو الشعر أو الحساب أو الطب جاز كذا في "الفتح" و"ملا مسكين". على جواز الاستئجار : هذا هو مذهب المتأخرين من مشايخ بلخ استحسنوا ذلك؛ لظهور التواني في الأمور الدينية، وكسل الناس في الاحتساب، وكذا يجوز على الإمامة في هذا اليوم؛ لأن للأئمة كانت لهم عطيات في بيت المال، وانقطعت اليوم بسبب استيلاء الظلمة عليها، وفي روضة الزندويستي : كان شيخنا أبو محمد عبد . الخيز اخزي يقول: في زماننا يجوز للإمام والمؤذن والمعلم أخذ الأجرة، ولا يجوز استئجار المصحف وكتب الفقه؛ لعدم التعارف. (عيني) لتعليم القرآن: اعلم أن في أكثر المتون اقتصروا على ذكر تعليم القرآن لكن زيد عليه كما في "الدر المختار" وغيره تعليم الفقه والإمامة والأذان والإقامة والوعظ، فهذا مجموع ما أفتى به المتأخرون من مشايخنا، وهم البلخيون على خلاف ما ذهب إليه الإمام وصاحباه واتفقت كلمتهم في الشروح والفتاوى على التعليل بالضرورة، وهي خشية ضياع القرآن وصرحوا بأن أصل المذهب عدم الجواز.
And the fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran, and it is not permissible for singing and wailing [since that] is something not capable of being delivered, so it is not valid. End. Al-Ijarah. Then the madhhab with us: that every act of obedience specific to a Muslim, hiring for it is invalid, contrary to building mosques and bridges. And it is problematic with their reasoning that when an act of worship is performed by its person, it counts for them, so it is not permissible to take wages from others, like Hajj on behalf of another; because it counts for the one directed, according to the sound view, even though the intention of the director is not a condition, and the worker acts for his commander, not for himself, while it is an act of obedience. And according to Muhammad's saying: nothing gets him except the reward of the expenditure, so the problem remains that his reward occurred for someone other than the doer even though it is an act of worship, so it is problematic against their saying: 'When an act of worship occurs, its reward occurs for its doer, not for another.' And the specification of teaching Quran and fiqh indicates that if one hires for teaching calligraphy, writing, literature, poetry, arithmetic, or medicine, it is permissible, as in al-Fath and Mulla Miskin. On the permissibility of hiring: this is the madhhab of the later scholars from the teachers of Balkh; they deemed it good due to the apparent slackness in religious matters and people's laziness in voluntary acts. And similarly, it is permissible for imamah in this time because imams used to have stipends from the treasury, but today they have been cut off due to the usurpers' takeover. And in Rawdat al-Zandawistī: our teacher Abu Muhammad 'Abd... al-Khayz Akhzī said: in our time it is permissible for the imam, mu'adhdhin, and teacher to take wages, but it is not permissible to hire the mushaf and fiqh books due to lack of custom. (Aynī) For teaching the Quran: know that in most main texts they restricted themselves to mentioning teaching the Quran, but it has been increased, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others, to teaching fiqh, imamah, adhan, iqamah, and preaching. So this is the total of what the later scholars from our teachers, the Balkhis, gave fatwa on, contrary to what the Imam and his two companions held, and their word agreed in the commentaries and fatwas on the reasoning of necessity, which is fear of loss of the Quran, and they stated that the original madhhab is non-permissibility.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a complex expansion on the ruling of hiring for teaching the Quran. It begins by stating the contemporary fatwa that permits hiring for teaching the Quran and prohibits it for singing. Then it discusses the Hanafi principle that any act of worship specific to Muslims cannot be hired for, citing the problematic case of Hajj on behalf of another. The text then notes that the later scholars of Balkh permitted hiring for teaching due to necessity, even though the original madhhab (of Abu Hanifa and his companions) held it invalid. The reasoning for the later fatwa is the fear that Quranic knowledge would be lost. The passage also includes various exceptions and detailed discussions from commentaries.

Key Terms
الاستئجار (al-isti'jār): Hiring or renting services
القربة (al-qurbah): Act of worship or drawing near to Allah
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): Necessity that permits an otherwise prohibited act
التواني (al-tawānī): Laziness or negligence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a confirmed sunnah
B) To prevent loss of Quranic knowledge
C) Because teaching is not an act of worship
D) Because the Quran says so

Key Takeaway
Teaching the Quran is a qurbah, but the Hanafi school permits hiring to teach it due to the overriding necessity of preserving Islamic knowledge.

Hiring for Quran Recitation at Graves: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-madhhab dispute on hiring for Quran recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on hiring for Quran recitation at graves and identify the mufta bihi position along with its rationale.

Core Idea
Hiring for Quran recitation at graves is firmly prohibited in the later Hanafi school because it trades reward for wages.

This lesson unpacks a contested ruling within the Hanafi school: the permissibility of hiring a reciter to read Quran at a grave for a fixed period. Some early Hanafi authorities considered it permissible (mukhtār), but later luminaries like Taj al-Shari'ah and al-Ayni explicitly rejected it, and the Ḥanafī muftā bihī (operative position) is now prohibition. Understanding this dispute clarifies how later scholars weighed evidence and adjusted the fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position(s)
Identify the two conflicting views reported in the passage: one group claims the chosen view (mukhtār) is permissibility; the other group (Taj al-Shari'ah, al-Ayni, Radd al-Muhtar) insists on prohibition.
The 'mukhtār' here refers to the preferred view according to some, not the eventual muftā bihī.
2
Identify the opponents and their proof
Note that the opponents are fellow Hanafis – Taj al-Shari'ah and al-Ayni. Their proof is that reciting Quran for wages does not earn reward either for the deceased or the reciter, implying the act is legally ineffective.
They rely on a principle: worship rewarded must be free of worldly compensation.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the permissibility view
The passage does not give a response from the permissibility camp. Instead, it records the rejection from Radd al-Muhtar and Tabyīn al-Maḥārim. Later scholars clearly overruled the permissibility view.
The tarjih is not based on a proof from the permissibility side; the later authors simply refute it with stronger narratives.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the contract is allowed, the payments and recitations are valid; if prohibited, the contract is invalid (fasid) and earnings are unlawful. This affects real funeral arrangements.
The dispute directly impacts what families can be advised.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its authority
The mufta bihi is prohibition, supported by the weight of later Hanafi masters (Radd al-Muhtar, Tabyīn al-Maḥārim) and the explicit statements of Taj al-Shari'ah and al-Ayni.
Authority weight: fatawa_mutakhkhirin (later scholars).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في "الفتح" نقلا عن "الجوهرة": واختلفوا في الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن على القبر مدة معلومة، والمختار أنه يجوز، ورده في رد المحتار" بكلام طويل، وقال قد أطنب في رده صاحب "تبيين" المحارم" مستندا إلى النقول الصريحة، فمن جملة كلامه قال تاج الشريعة في شرح "الهداية": إن القرآن بالأجرة لا يستحق الثواب لا للميت ولا للقاري. وقال العيني في شرح الهداية: ويمنع القاري للدنيا والآخذ والمعطي آلمان انتهى بقدر الحاجة، والتفصيل فيه فليطالع لمه.
He said in al-Fath, quoting from al-Jawharah: They differed regarding hiring for recitation of the Quran at the grave for a known period, and the chosen view is that it is permissible. But he refuted it in Radd al-Muhtar with lengthy speech, and he said: The author of Tabyīn al-Maḥārim has elaborated in his refutation, relying on explicit transmissions. So from his speech, Taj al-Shari'ah said in Sharh al-Hidayah: The Quran with wages does not deserve reward, neither for the deceased nor for the reciter. And al-Ayni said in Sharh al-Hidayah: The reciter for the world, and the taker and giver are both blameworthy. End to the extent of need, and the detail is therein, so let one read it.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a brief mention of a dispute regarding hiring for Quran recitation at graves. It reports that the preferred view (mukhtār) in al-Jawharah is permissibility, but later, Radd al-Muhtar strongly refuted this. Taj al-Shari'ah and al-Ayni are quoted supporting the prohibition, stating that the reciter does not get reward and both parties are blameworthy. The text directs the reader to look up the details.

Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtār): The preferred or chosen view among Hanafi scholars

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The reciter does not get reward for the deceased or himself
C) It is obligatory
D) Only the deceased gets reward

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi school decisively prohibits hiring for Quran recitation at graves because wages nullify the spiritual reward, making the contract invalid.

Prohibition of Hiring for Sinful Acts (Ijara `ala al-Ma`asi)
Explicit prohibition of ijarah for sinful acts with examples and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ijarah for sinful acts and identify exceptions for permissible uses like drums in weddings.

Core Idea
Hiring for sin is void — Islamic law cannot obligate disobedience.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes a fundamental principle: any ijarah contract whose subject matter is a sinful act is void (batil). The reasoning is that Shari'ah cannot require a person to commit a sin. The text provides examples and an important exception for drums used in permissible contexts like weddings or war.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is entering into an ijarah (hiring) contract for a sinful act like singing or wailing. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz) and the contract is batil (void).
Batil means it produces no legal effects; any wage paid must be returned.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a general principle: Shari'ah cannot obligate a person to commit sin. The passage states: 'It is not permissible that a person be obligated to something by which he becomes disobedient; so that disobedience be attributed to the Shari'ah.'
This is a logical deduction (qiyas jaliy) from the overarching purpose of Shari'ah.
3
Note the examples given
The text lists singing, wailing (nawh), flutes (mazamir), drum if used for amusement, driving camels (hida'), and reciting poetry. All these are considered sinful if done in the context of amusement or prohibited practice.
Some of these, like poetry, might be permissible in other contexts, but here they refer to specific sinful uses.
4
Distinguish the exception
The drum is explicitly exempted when used for permissible purposes: the drum of warriors, wedding drum, and caravan drum. This shows that the prohibition is tied to intention and context, not the instrument itself.
The exception is important for practical fatwa.
5
Apply the principle to other sinful acts
The same ruling applies to any ijarah contract for an act that is haram: e.g., brewing alcohol, writing false testimony, performing magic. The contract is void ab initio.
The wage is not earned and must be returned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز على الغناء [البكاء على الميت وتعديد محاسنه] لأنها معصية، وعقد الإجارة يستحق بها تسليم المعقود عليه شرعا ولا يجوز أن يستحق على المرء شيء يكون به عاصيا؛ كي لا تصير المعصية مضافة إلى الشرع، فلا يجب الأجر بهذا العقد، وإن أعطاء الأجر وقبضه لا يحل له ويجب عليه رده على صاحبه، وفي "شرح الكافي": لا تجوز الإجارة على شيء من الغناء والنوح والمزامير والطبل أو شيء من اللهو، ولا على الحداء وقراءة الشعر ولا غيره، ولا أجر في ذلك، والطبل إنما كان منهيا إذا كان للهو، أما إذا كان لغيره فلا بأس به كطبل الغزاة وطبل العرس والقافلة من العيني وحواشي الهداية) والملاهي.
And it is not permissible for singing [wailing over the dead and enumerating their virtues] because it is disobedience, and the contract of ijarah makes it due to deliver what is contracted upon, and it is not permissible that a person be obligated to something by which he becomes disobedient; so that disobedience not be attributed to the Shari'ah. Thus, the wage is not obligatory by this contract, and if he gives the wage and receives it, it is not lawful for him, and he must return it to its owner. And in Sharh al-Kafi: Ijarah is not permissible for anything of singing, wailing, flutes, drum, or anything of amusement, nor for driving camels, reciting poetry, etc., and there is no wage in that. The drum is only prohibited if it is for amusement; if for other purposes, there is no problem, like the drum of warriors, wedding drum, and caravan, from al-Ayni and Hashiyat al-Hidayah). And musical instruments.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: hiring for acts that are sinful (ma'siyah) is invalid. The reasoning is that Islamic law cannot obligate sinful acts. Therefore, the contract is void, and no wage is due; if paid, it must be returned. The text then specifies examples: singing, wailing, musical instruments, and any amusement. It also makes a distinction regarding drums: drums for permissible purposes like war or weddings are not included in the prohibition.

Key Terms
المعصية (al-ma'siyah): Disobedience to Allah; a sinful act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on ijarah for singing?
A) Valid but disliked
B) Invalid, and any wage received must be returned
C) Valid only if the singer is male
D) Permissible with conditions

Key Takeaway
Hiring for any sinful act renders the ijarah contract null and void; any payment made must be returned, as Islamic law cannot obligate disobedience.

Hiring a Wet Nurse: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling with proof on hiring a wet nurse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a wet nurse, explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas, and identify the conditions for valid payment and termination of the contract.

Core Idea
Hiring a wet nurse is valid by istihsan despite qiyas; payment with food/clothing is permitted by Abu Hanifa, and the contract is cancellable for harm to the child.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the rulings on hiring a wet nurse (zā'ir). It addresses the permissibility of the contract, the payment method, the husband's rights, and when the contract may be canceled. Understanding these rules is essential for ensuring valid contracts that protect the rights of both parties and the welfare of the child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that hiring a wet nurse (استئجار الظئر) with a known wage and period is valid (صح) by istihsan
The default qiyas would invalidate it because it involves consumption of milk, like hiring a cow for milk.
2
Locate the dalil for istihsan
The Quranic verse (65:6) commands giving wages to wet nurses, and there is consensus (ijma) and continuous practice.
The verse: 'فَإِنْ أَرْضَعْنَ لَكُمْ فَأْتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ'.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on payment
Abu Hanifa permits payment with food and clothing without specifying type or quantity; Sahibayn require specification. The passage explains the reasoning of each.
Imam's view relies on custom (urf) and lack of potential dispute; Sahibayn consider the wage unknown (gharar).
4
Understand the husband's role and contract termination
The husband cannot be prevented from intercourse unless the wife is in the lessee's house. The husband may cancel the contract if he did not consent. The contract terminates if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, or for other excuses harming the child.
Termination is based on preventing harm (darar).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The permissibility of hiring is agreed upon. For payment with food/clothing, Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon (tarjih).
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah; Imam's view preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح استئجار الظئر بأجرة معلومة كالمزمار والطبل استحسانا اتفاقا. هي المرضعة. وبطعامها وكسوتها، ولا يمنع زوجها من وطئها، فإن حبلت أو مرضت فسخت، وعليها الظئر الإجارة على الظئر كة تمليك. وفسد إلخ: مطلقا فيما ينقسم وفيما لا ينقسم عند أبي حنيفة وزفر (مسكين صورته: أن يؤجر نصف دار مشتر بينه وبين آخر من رجل يسكنها، لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة إلا من شريكه، وقالا: لا يجوز مطلقا؛ لأنه نوع فيجوز كالبيع، وبه قال الشافعي ومالك. وله: أنه عقد، والغرض منه الانتفاع وهو لا يتصور بالمشاع، فلابد من التهايؤ، فيصير كل منهما نائبا عن الآخر في النصف في نوبته والمالك لا يصح : نائبا عن المستأجر، والحيلة في جواز إجارة المشاع أن يستأجر الكل، ثم يفسخ في النصف، فإنه يجوز؛ لأن شيوع الطارئ لا يفسد كما في الهبة، أو يحكم الحاكم بجوازه ، وفي "المغني": والفتوى في إجارة المشاع على قولهما. رمز الحقائق: ٢٧٩/٢] استئجار الظئر إلخ : أي إذا استأجر مرضعة ليرضع ابنه صح ذلك الاستئجار وطاب لها الأجر إذا كان بأجرة معلومة ويكون المدة معلومة وهذا بالاتفاق وكان القياس أن لا تصح؛ لأنها ترد على استهلاك، وهو اللبن، فصار كاستئجار البقرة والشاة لشرب لبنها، والبستان ليأكل ثمرته لكن الاستحسان ،جوزه، ودليله: قوله تعالى: فَإِنْ أَرْضَعْنَ لَكُمْ فَأْتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ﴾ (الطلاق: ٦) والإجماع في ذلك، وجرى التعامل به في الأعصار. وهذا مختصر ما في التكملة مع توضيح من المحشي والتحقيق فيه فليرجع إليها. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤/٨] وبطعامها إلخ: أي صح استئجار الظئر بطعامها وكسوتها بلا بيان الجنس والقدر ولها الوسط وهذا عند الإمام، وقالا: لا يجوز، وهو القياس، وجه قولهما: أن الأجرة مجهولة، فصار كما إذا استأجر للطبخ والخبز، وله: أن الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأن العادة جارية بالتوسعة على الظئر شفقة على الولد. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥/٨] ولا يمنع [ أي في غير منزل المستأجر، وأما في منزله فله أن يمنع] لأنه حقه، فلا يمكن المستأجر من إبطاله، ولهذا كان للزوج أن يفسخ هذا العقد إذا لم يعلم، سواء كان يشينه إجارتها بأن كان وجيها بين الناس أو لم يشينه، وهو الأصح تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥/٨] وهذا إذا كان الزوج معروفا، فأما إذا كان لا يعرف أنها امرأته إلا بقولها، فليس له أن ينقض الإجارة، وللمستأجر أن يمنعه من غشيانها في منزله، سواء كان الزوج معروفا أو غير معروف. (ملخص من التكملة وملا مسكين والفتح) فسخت إلخ: لأن لبن الحبل والمريضة يضر بالصغير، وهي أيضا يضرها الرضاع فكان لها، ولهم الخيار دفعا للضرر عنها وعن الصبي؛ لأن الإجارة تفسخ بالأعذار كما لو تقيأ الصبي لبنها؛ لأنه يضر به أو كانت سارقة أو فاجرة بائنا فجورها، بخلاف ما إذا كانت كافرة؛ لأن كفرها في اعتقادها ولا يضر بالصبي، وكذا إذا كان الصبي لا يأخذ ثديها إلى غير ذلك من الأعذار والتفصيل في "الفتح والعيني". [رمز الحقائق: ٢٧٩/٢]
And the hiring of the wet nurse with a known wage is valid like flute and drum by istihsan unanimously. She is the wet nurse. And with her food and clothing, and her husband is not prevented from having intercourse with her. If she becomes pregnant or ill, the contract is canceled. And upon her is the wet nurse ... And it is void etc.: absolutely, whether divisible or indivisible, according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar ... [repeated musha' text] ... Hiring the wet nurse etc.: That is, if he hires a wet nurse to suckle his son, that hiring is valid and her wage is good if it is a known wage and the period is known, and this is by agreement. The qiyas would be that it is not valid because it is for consumption of the milk, similar to hiring a cow for its milk or a garden for its fruit. But istihsan permits it, and its proof is the verse: 'Then if they suckle for you, give them their wages' (65:6), and consensus, and it has been practiced in all ages. This is a summary from al-Takmilah with clarification. And with her food and clothing: That is, hiring the wet nurse with her food and clothing without specifying type and quantity is valid, and she gets the average. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). They (Sahibayn) said it is not valid, and that is the qiyas. Their reasoning: the wage is unknown, making it like hiring for cooking and baking. His reasoning: ignorance does not lead to dispute because custom is to be generous to the wet nurse out of tenderness for the child. And he (the husband) does not prevent [meaning other than in the lessee's house; in his house he may prevent] because it is his right, so the lessee cannot invalidate it. Therefore the husband has the right to cancel this contract if he did not know, whether it brings shame to him or not, and this is the most sound view. This is when the husband is known; if she is not known to be his wife except by her word, then he cannot cancel the contract. And the lessee can prevent him from coming to her in his house, whether the husband is known or unknown. (Summarized from al-Takmilah, Mulla Miskin, and al-Fath). It becomes canceled etc.: Because the milk of the pregnant and ill woman harms the infant, and also harms her, so she has the option, and they have the option to remove harm from her and the infant. The contract is canceled due to excuses, like if the infant vomits her milk, because it harms him, or if she is a thief or immoral openly, contrary to if she is a disbeliever because her disbelief is in her belief and does not harm the infant, and likewise if the infant does not take her breast, and other excuses. Details are in al-Fath and al-Ayni.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings on hiring a wet nurse (zā'ir). Despite the messy OCR, the core rulings are: 1) Hiring is valid with a known wage and period, by istihsan despite qiyas. 2) Payment with food and clothing without specification is valid according to Abu Hanifa (Sahibayn disagree). 3) The husband cannot be prevented from intercourse with his wife unless she is in the lessee's house, where the lessee can prevent him. The husband may cancel if he did not consent. 4) The contract can be terminated if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, as it harms the infant. Also other excuses like infant vomiting milk, or wet nurse being openly sinful (but not if she is a disbeliever). The proof is the Quranic verse on suckling wages.

Key Terms
الظئر (al-zā'ir): Wet nurse; a woman hired to breastfeed a child
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juridical preference; a method to override qiyas for a stronger reason
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The average; in the context of payment, the wet nurse receives the customary average of food and clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Surah al-Talaq: 'If they suckle for you, give them their wages'
C) Surah al-Nisa: 'And marry those among you who are single'
D) Surah al-Ma'idah: 'This day I have perfected for you your religion'

Key Takeaway
Hiring a wet nurse is valid by istihsan, and its conditions—payment, husband's rights, and termination—are governed by custom and the principle of preventing harm.

Hiring Undivided Shares: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with analysis of proofs and practical stratagems.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on hiring co-owned property, analyze their proofs, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Hiring a co-owned share is invalid in strict analogy, but the fatwa permits it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a key point of divergence within the Hanafi school: the validity of hiring out an undivided share (musha') in jointly owned property. The matn rules it invalid except when the lessee is the co-owner, but the commentator expands on the dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this issue requires examining the nature of the hire contract, the purpose of benefit, and the use of analogical reasoning (qiyas) to distinguish hire from sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states: hiring musha' is invalid except from the partner. This is the initial position from which the dispute arises.
2
Contrast the positions
Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold it invalid absolutely (including from partner? Actually Abu Hanifa excepts partner). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold it invalid absolutely (no exception for partner). So there is disagreement within the school.
Abu Hanifa's exception for the co-owner is based on the possibility of benefit through time-division.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa: Benefit from musha' is not achievable without time-division (tahayyu), and the owner cannot deputize the lessee. Sahibayn: Analogy to sale, which is valid for musha'.
The Sahibayn use qiyas jali (clear analogy) while Abu Hanifa uses qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) focusing on the specific nature of benefit.
4
Examine the response and stratagems
The commentator presents a hila: rent the whole, then cancel half. Also a judge may permit it. These show practical ways to achieve the contract despite the strict ruling.
The hila is a recognized method in Hanafi fiqh to avoid prohibitions while achieving a permissible end.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Mughni states the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's saying, meaning permissibility. So the operative ruling allows hiring musha' despite the strict position.
This shift shows the evolution of the school's position over time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفسد إجارة المشاع إلا من الشريك. وفسد إلخ: مطلقا فيما ينقسم وفيما لا ينقسم عند أبي حنيفة وزفر (مسكين صورته: أن يؤجر نصف دار مشتر بينه وبين آخر من رجل يسكنها، لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة إلا من شريكه، وقالا: لا يجوز مطلقا؛ لأنه نوع فيجوز كالبيع، وبه قال الشافعي ومالك. وله: أنه عقد، والغرض منه الانتفاع وهو لا يتصور بالمشاع، فلابد من التهايؤ، فيصير كل منهما نائبا عن الآخر في النصف في نوبته والمالك لا يصح : نائبا عن المستأجر، والحيلة في جواز إجارة المشاع أن يستأجر الكل، ثم يفسخ في النصف، فإنه يجوز؛ لأن شيوع الطارئ لا يفسد كما في الهبة، أو يحكم الحاكم بجوازه ، وفي "المغني": والفتوى في إجارة المشاع على قولهما.
And invalid is the hiring of co-owned property except from the partner. And 'invalid etc.': absolutely in what is divisible and what is not divisible according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar. (Miskin: its image is that he rents out half a house jointly owned between him and another to a man to reside in; it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa except from his partner; and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not permissible absolutely, because it is a type (of contract) so it is permissible like sale, and al-Shafi'i and Malik said the same. And for him (Abu Hanifa): it is a contract, and the purpose is benefit, and that is not conceivable in co-owned property, so division of time is necessary, so each becomes a deputy for the other in half in his turn, and the owner cannot be a deputy for the lessee. And the legal stratagem for the permissibility of hiring co-owned property is that one rents the whole, then cancels half, then it is permissible because subsequent co-ownership does not invalidate as in gift, or the judge rules on its permissibility. And in al-Mughni: the fatwa for hiring co-owned property is according to their (Sahibayn's) saying.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of hiring out an undivided share (musha') in co-owned property. The matn states that such a hire is invalid except when the lessee is the co-owner himself. The commentator clarifies that this ruling applies universally, whether the property is divisible or not, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, holding that hiring a co-owned share is absolutely invalid, drawing an analogy to the sale of a co-owned share, which is permissible. This view is also held by al-Shafi'i and Malik. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the purpose of a hire contract is to transfer the benefit of the property, and benefit from a co-owned share is not practically feasible without a mutual agreement on division of time (tahayyu). Consequently, the owner cannot serve as a deputy for the lessee in gaining benefit. The commentator then presents legal stratagems (hiyal) to circumvent this prohibition: one can rent the entire property and then cancel the lease for half, because subsequent co-ownership does not invalidate the contract, analogous to a gift. Alternatively, a judge may rule its permissibility. Finally, the fatwa in al-Mughni adopts the position of the Sahibayn, indicating that the relied-upon position for legal practice is the permissibility of hiring co-owned property.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-musha'): An undivided share in jointly owned property, where the share is not physically delineated.
التهيؤ (al-tahayyu'): Mutual division of time between co-owners for using the co-owned property.
الحيلة (al-hilah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible result while avoiding a prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible only if the lessee is the co-owner.
B) It is invalid absolutely.
C) It is permissible absolutely.
D) It is valid only if the property is divisible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position permits hiring undivided shares, despite early rulings to the contrary.

Hiring a Wet Nurse with Fixed Wages
Ruling with proof: istihsan for hiring wet nurse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates the hiring of a wet nurse by istihsan, citing the Quranic verse (65:6) and contrasting it with the qiyas that would invalidate the contract.

Core Idea
The Quranic command to pay wet nurses overrides the general qiyas that would invalidate such a contract.

In this passage, the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a ruling on hiring a wet nurse (al-zhi'r) that appears to contradict standard qiyas in contracts of ijarah. The default analogy would render the contract invalid because it involves the consumption of milk, akin to hiring an animal for its milk. However, the Hanafi school, relying on istihsan and a clear Quranic text, affirms the validity. Let's examine the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the central ruling: hiring a wet nurse with a known wage and known duration is valid (sahih) by istihsan, unanimously agreed upon.
2
Identify the qiyas that would invalidate
Understand the default qiyas: by analogy, the contract would be invalid because it involves consumption (istikhlak) of milk, like hiring a cow for its milk or an orchard for its fruit, which is uncertain.
The qiyas is based on the general principle that ijarah on consumables is invalid due to gharar.
3
Apply istihsan
Recognize that istihsan overrides the qiyas. The proof is the Quranic verse (65:6) commanding payment to wet nurses, consensus (ijma'), and continuous practice of Muslims.
Istihsan is not arbitrary; it is grounded in stronger evidence (nas, ijma', and established custom).
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine the Quranic text: 'fa'tuhunna ujurahunna' (give them their wages). The imperative indicates wujub (obligation), and 'ujurahunna' implies compensation for the service (act of breastfeeding), not for the milk itself.
This shifts the contract from a sale of milk to a hire of service, avoiding the qiyas on consumables.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
Conclude that the ruling is firmly established (mufta bihi) with no intra-madhhab dispute; it is a binding position for fatwa.
The text says 'bil-ittifaq' (unanimously), indicating strong consensus even across schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح استئجار الظئر بأجرة معلومة استحسانا اتفاقا. استئجار الظئر إلخ: أي إذا استأجر مرضعة ليرضع ابنه صح ذلك الاستئجار وطاب لها الأجر إذا كان بأجرة معلومة ويكون المدة معلومة وهذا بالاتفاق وكان القياس أن لا تصح؛ لأنها ترد على استهلاك، وهو اللبن، فصار كاستئجار البقرة والشاة لشرب لبنها، والبستان ليأكل ثمرته لكن الاستحسان جوزه، ودليله: قوله تعالى: فَإِنْ أَرْضَعْنَ لَكُمْ فَأْتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ﴾ (الطلاق: ٦) والإجماع في ذلك، وجرى التعامل به في الأعصار. وهذا مختصر ما في التكملة مع توضيح من المحشي والتحقيق فيه فليرجع إليها.
And valid is hiring a wet nurse with a known wages, by istihsan, unanimously. 'Hiring the wet nurse etc.': i.e., if a man hires a wet nurse to breastfeed his son, that hire is valid and the wages are permissible for her, if it is with a known wage and the period is known, and this is by consensus. And the analogy would be that it is not valid because it is a contract on consumption, i.e., milk, so it becomes like hiring a cow or sheep to drink its milk, or an orchard to eat its fruit. But istihsan allowed it, and its proof is the verse: 'Then if they give suck for you, give them their due recompense' (65:6), and consensus on that, and the practice has continued through the ages. And this is a summary of what is in al-Takmilah with clarification from the commentator and verification, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the validity of hiring a wet nurse (zhi'r) to breastfeed a child, with a fixed wage and known duration. The matn states it is valid unanimously by istihsan. The commentator explains that the default qiyas would render the contract invalid because it involves consumption of milk, which is akin to hiring an animal for its milk or a garden for its fruit, where the benefit is the consumption of the thing itself, leading to gharar (uncertainty). However, the Hanafi school employs istihsan based on the Quranic verse (al-Talaq 65:6) which commands hiring wet nurses, indicating the permissibility of paying them for this service. Additionally, there is consensus (ijma') on its validity, and the practice of Muslims across generations supports it. The commentator refers to al-Takmilah for a detailed discussion. The key point is that the contract is on the act of breastfeeding (a service), not on the milk itself, so the analogy to consuming the object is imperfect, and the Quranic text overrides the qiyas.

Key Terms
الظئر (al-zhi'r): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A legal method preferring a ruling due to equity, custom, or stronger evidence over qiyas.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The Quranic verse in Surah al-Talaq
C) The practice of the people of Madinah
D) The saying of Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
Hiring a wet nurse with fixed wages and duration is unanimously valid by istihsan, overriding qiyas due to the Quranic text and consensus.

Hiring a Wet Nurse with Unspecified Food and Clothing: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on unknown wages in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa permits hiring a wet nurse with unspecified food and clothing and distinguish the Sahibayn's position based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Custom overrides strict qiyas: uncertainty in wages is tolerated when social norms prevent disputes.

The Hanafi school is known for its pragmatic use of custom (urf) to temper strict analogical reasoning. This lesson examines a classic case where Imam Abu Hanifa upholds a contract despite an unknown wage, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, reject it on the basis of qiyas. The ruling hinges on the social context: hiring a wet nurse involves compassion for the child, which customarily prompts generosity and avoids disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its variation
Identify the ruling in the matn: hiring a wet nurse with her food and clothing is valid (sahih) without specifying type or quantity. Note that this is Imam Abu Hanifa's view, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) deem it invalid.
The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) presents Abu Hanifa's view as the operative position.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof: qiyas to similar contracts
The Sahibayn argue that the wage is unknown (majhul), which generally invalidates an ijarah contract. They analogize to hiring someone for cooking or baking without specifying the wage, which is unanimously invalid. Identify the 'asl (original case) and the 'illah (cause): unknown wage leads to gharar and dispute.
The text says 'وهو القياس' – this analogy is the qiyas.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response: custom overrides qiyas
Abu Hanifa argues that the uncertainty here does not lead to dispute because social custom (urf) ensures the employer will be generous to the wet nurse out of compassion for the child. This custom removes the effective cause ('illah) of the analogy. Thus, the analogy fails and the contract is valid.
The text states: 'أن الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأن العادة جارية بالتوسعة على الظئر شفقة على الولد.'
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the contract is held valid (Abu Hanifa), the wet nurse is entitled to the average (al-wasat) of food and clothing. If invalid (Sahibayn), she would be entitled to the actual value (ujrat al-mithl) as compensation for her work, but the contract itself is void. Note that the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The mufta bihi is likely Abu Hanifa's view as per the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطعامها وكسوتها. وبطعامها إلخ: أي صح استئجار الظئر بطعامها وكسوتها بلا بيان الجنس والقدر ولها الوسط وهذا عند الإمام، وقالا: لا يجوز، وهو القياس، وجه قولهما: أن الأجرة مجهولة، فصار كما إذا استأجر للطبخ والخبز، وله: أن الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأن العادة جارية بالتوسعة على الظئر شفقة على الولد.
And with her food and her clothing. 'And with her food etc.': i.e., valid is hiring a wet nurse with her food and her clothing without specification of type and quantity, and she gets the average. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And they two (Sahibayn) said: it is not permissible, and that is the qiyas. The basis of their statement: that the wage is unknown, so it becomes like when one hires for cooking and baking. And for him (Abu Hanifa): that the ignorance does not lead to dispute because custom runs on generosity towards the wet nurse out of compassion for the child.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of hiring a wet nurse in exchange for providing her food and clothing, without specifying the type or amount. The matn presumes validity. The commentator explains that Imam Abu Hanifa rules it valid, and the wet nurse receives the 'average' (al-wasat) in terms of quality. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that it is invalid because the wage (food and clothing) is unknown, leading to gharar. They analogize it to hiring someone for cooking or baking without specifying the wages, which is invalid. Abu Hanifa's argument is that the uncertainty here does not lead to disputes because custom (urf) dictates that the employer will be generous to the wet nurse out of care for the child, and thus the parties will not quarrel. This is an exception to the general rule that wages must be known. The passage highlights how the Hanafi school considers custom and social context in overriding strict qiyas.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasat): The average or moderate level of food and clothing; not the best nor the worst.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the wage, which typically invalidates a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the food and clothing are always worth the same amount.
B) Because custom ensures the employer will be generous, avoiding disputes.
C) Because the wet nurse can demand any amount she wants.
D) Because the contract is considered a gift, not a hire.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) can override strict qiyas in Hanafi fiqh when it eliminates the potential for dispute, as seen in hiring a wet nurse with unspecified wages.
