Husband's Right to Rescind the Wet Nurse's Contract
Conditional ruling on husband's authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a husband can rescind his wife's contract as a wet nurse and identify when the lessee may prevent conjugal relations.

Core Idea
The husband's marital right does not automatically void the employment; location and knowledge determine the ruling.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a nuanced intersection of marriage and hire. The matn gives a general principle – the husband is not prevented from intercourse – but the commentary reveals critical exceptions. We will parse these conditions step by step to understand when the husband may rescind the contract and when the lessee may prevent access.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal ruling from the matn
The matn states: 'ولا يمنع زوجها من وطئها' – her husband is not prevented from having intercourse. This is the default rule: the husband's conjugal right is not suspended by the hire contract.
This applies when the wife is working outside the lessee's home.
2
Locate the location-based exception
The commentary adds: 'أما في منزله فله أن يمنع' – in the lessee's home, the lessee may prevent the husband. The lessee's right to privacy and undisturbed use of his rented property overrides the husband's access.
The default rule applies only outside the lessee's home.
3
Determine the condition for rescission
The husband may rescind the contract if he did not know about it at the time of hiring. This is unconditional regarding shame: 'سواء كان يشينه إجارتها... أو لم يشينه' – whether the hiring brings shame or not.
Ignorance of the contract is the key factor.
4
Note the identity condition for rescission
The rescission right depends on the husband being known (i.e., his marriage is publicly known). If he is not known as her husband except by her word, he cannot rescind. In that case, the lessee may prevent him from approaching her in his home, regardless of the husband's fame.
Unverifiable marital status protects the lessee's reasonable reliance on the contract.
5
Distil the practical consequence
The thamarah: The lessee can protect his home from intrusion; the husband can protect his marital right by rescinding the contract if he was unaware, but only if his marriage is known. If the husband is unknown, he cannot rescind and must accept the lessee's restriction in the lessee's home.
This balances the rights of husband, wife, and lessee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يمنع زوجها من وطئها. ولا يمنع [ أي في غير منزل المستأجر، وأما في منزله فله أن يمنع] لأنه حقه، فلا يمكن المستأجر من إبطاله، ولهذا كان للزوج أن يفسخ هذا العقد إذا لم يعلم، سواء كان يشينه إجارتها بأن كان وجيها بين الناس أو لم يشينه، وهو الأصح تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥/٨] وهذا إذا كان الزوج معروفا، فأما إذا كان لا يعرف أنها امرأته إلا بقولها، فليس له أن ينقض الإجارة، وللمستأجر أن يمنعه من غشيانها في منزله، سواء كان الزوج معروفا أو غير معروف.
And her husband is not prevented from having intercourse with her. 'And he is not prevented' [i.e., in the lessee's home? Actually, the bracketed text clarifies: in other than the lessee's home, but in his home he may prevent] because it is his right, so the lessee cannot nullify it. For this reason, the husband may rescind this contract if he did not know, whether her being hired is shameful to him (if he is a notable among people) or not, and this is the most correct. [Takmilat Bahr al-Ra'iq 45/8] And this is when the husband is known; as for if she is not known to be his wife except by her statement, then he has no right to rescind the hire, and the lessee may prevent him from approaching her in his home, whether the husband is known or not.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage explains the husband's right regarding his wife's contract as a wet nurse. The matn states 'her husband is not prevented from intercourse with her.' The commentator clarifies that this applies when the wet nurse is working outside the lessee's home. However, if she is working in the lessee's home, the lessee can prevent the husband from entering to have intercourse. The husband's right to sexual relations is a marital right that the lessee cannot invalidate. Consequently, if the husband was unaware of the hiring, he may rescind the contract, regardless of whether the hiring causes him shame (e.g., if he is a dignified person). This is the most correct view. However, if the husband is not known (i.e., her claim of being married is unverified), he cannot rescind the hire. Additionally, the lessee can prevent the husband from approaching her in the lessee's home, whether the husband is known or not.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse; the husband's conjugal right.
يشينه (yashinuhu): To disgrace or bring shame upon him.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract.
الغشيان (al-ghishyan): To approach sexually; euphemism for intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In the lessee's home only.
B) In any location.
C) Only in the husband's home.
D) He cannot prevent the husband at all.

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to rescind the wet nurse contract is conditional on his ignorance of the hire and his public marital status, while the lessee's right to prevent intercourse applies only within his rented home.

Grounds for Rescinding a Wet Nurse Contract
Ruling with examples of excuses for rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recognized excuses for rescinding a wet nurse contract in Hanafi fiqh and explain the underlying principle of harm prevention.

Core Idea
A wet nurse contract can be rescinded to prevent harm, but not for religious belief alone.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when a wet nurse contract can be rescinded. The matn gives two explicit examples—pregnancy and illness—and the commentary expands to other cases involving harm. You will learn the legal reasoning based on the principle of harm prevention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
The contract in question is the hire of a wet nurse (ijarah al-rada'). The lesson deals with when such a contract can be rescinded (faskh).
2
List the explicit excuses from the matn
The matn mentions two: pregnancy (hubl) and illness (marad).
These are the primary examples.
3
Identify the expanded excuses from the commentary
The commentary adds: the infant vomiting the nurse's milk, the nurse being a thief or open adulteress, and the infant refusing to suckle.
These are based on the principle of harm.
4
Understand the exception
The contract is NOT rescinded if the nurse is a disbeliever (kafira) because her disbelief does not physically harm the infant.
Only tangible harm is considered.
5
Apply the principle of harm prevention
The unifying principle is that ijarah contracts can be rescinded for valid excuses (a'dhar) that cause harm to either party.
Derived from the maxim 'al-darar yuzal'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن حبلت أو مرضت فسخت. فسخت إلخ: لأن لبن الحبل والمريضة يضر بالصغير، وهي أيضا يضرها الرضاع فكان لها، ولهم الخيار دفعا للضرر عنها وعن الصبي؛ لأن الإجارة تفسخ بالأعذار كما لو تقيأ الصبي لبنها؛ لأنه يضر به أو كانت سارقة أو فاجرة بائنا فجورها، بخلاف ما إذا كانت كافرة؛ لأن كفرها في اعتقادها ولا يضر بالصبي، وكذا إذا كان الصبي لا يأخذ ثديها إلى غير ذلك من الأعذار والتفصيل في "الفتح والعيني".
Then if she becomes pregnant or falls ill, the hire is rescinded. 'Rescinded etc.': because the milk of the pregnant and sick woman harms the infant, and breastfeeding also harms her, so she and they (the lessor?) have the option to avoid harm to her and the infant. This is because the hire is rescinded due to excuses, such as if the infant vomits her milk because it harms him, or if she is a thief or an adulteress whose adultery is apparent, unlike if she is a disbeliever because her disbelief is in her belief and does not harm the infant, similarly if the infant does not take her breast, and other excuses. The details are in al-Fath and al-Ayni.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage outlines the grounds for rescinding a wet nurse's contract. The matn gives two specific examples: if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or falls ill, the hire is terminated (fuskh). The commentator explains the reasoning: the milk of a pregnant or sick woman harms the infant, and breastfeeding itself may harm her. Therefore, both parties have the option (khiyar) to rescind to prevent harm. The principle is that hire contracts can be rescinded due to valid excuses. The commentator provides additional examples: if the infant vomits the milk because it harms him, if the wet nurse is a thief or an open adulteress (because her character may harm the child), but not if she is a disbeliever (kafira) because her disbelief does not physically harm the infant. Also, if the infant refuses to take her breast, that is an excuse. The passage emphasizes harm prevention as the basis for the ruling. Further details are found in al-Fath and al-Ayni.

Key Terms
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission of a contract due to a subsequent event, not a cancellation by mutual consent.
الأعذار (al-a'dhar): Excuses that permit rescission of a binding contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for rescinding a wet nurse contract according to this passage?
A) The nurse becomes pregnant.
B) The nurse falls ill.
C) The nurse is a disbeliever (kafira).
D) The infant vomits the nurse's milk.

Key Takeaway
The rescission of a wet nurse contract is based on tangible harm to the infant or nurse; religious belief alone does not justify termination.

Duties of the Wet Nurse
Ruling on wet nurse's duties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the customary duties of a wet nurse and explain why they are obligatory upon her.

Core Idea
A wet nurse must reform the child's food and clean his clothes by custom, not explicit contract.

This lesson covers the ancillary duties of a wet nurse beyond breastfeeding. The matn states she must 'reform' the child's food, and the commentator elaborates on this and other customary obligations. Understanding these duties helps clarify the scope of the hire contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of 'islah'
Find the term 'إصلاح طعام الصبي' in the source. The commentator explains it as chewing food for the child or ensuring the nurse's diet does not harm the child.
This is a duty by custom (urf).
2
List the other duties mentioned
From the commentary, note that washing clothes from urine and stool, and preparing the child's food are also obligatory.
But washing from mere dirt is not obligatory.
3
Understand the basis of obligation
The commentary states these duties are obligatory 'because serving the child is obligatory upon her by custom' (عرفا). Recognize that urf can create legal obligations in Hanafi fiqh.
This is not from the explicit contract but from custom.
4
Distinguish obligatory from non-obligatory tasks
Note the distinction: cleaning urine/stool is wajib, but cleaning dirt is not. This shows the scope of customary duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إصلاح طعام الصبي، فإن أرضعته بلبن شاة، فلا أجر. إصلاح إلخ بأن تمضغ المرضعة طعامه ليأكل أراد به المضغ أي أن تمضغ الطعام للصبي، وقيل: أراد بالإصلاح أن لا تأكل ما يضر بالصبي، ولا تتغذى بغذاء يخالف مزاج الصبي، وهو الظاهر والحاصل: أنه يجب عليها إصلاح طعام الصبي؛ لأن خدمة الصبي واجبة عليها عرفا، وكذا غسل ثيابه عن البول والغائط عليها، لا عن الوسخ، وكذا تهيئة طعام الصبي على الظئر. (هذا) خلاصة ما في الفتح والتكملة وغيرهما) فإن أرضعته إلخ : أي إذا استأجر رجل ظئرا ليرضع ولده فأرضعته لبن شاة، وثبت ذلك بإقرارها أو بالبينة قامت على إرضاعها بلبن البهائم لا على عدم إرضاعها لبن نفسها، فإنها شهادة على النفي لا أجر لها؛ لأنها لم تأت الواجب عليها من العمل، وهو الإرضاع، وهذا إيجار لا إرضاع، والإيجار صب شيء في الفم، وإنما أطلق عليه لفظ الإرضاع للمشاكلة، قال في "التكملة": وإنما قيد بلبن الشاة؛ لأنها لو أرضعته بلبن خادمتها أو جاريتها أو بلبن ظئر استأجرتها بلا عقد، فلها الأجر كما تقدم. أقول في هذه المسألة خلاف ذكره في "الفتح": قال في "فتح الله المعين" بقي أن يقال: ما ذكره المصنف . لا أجر لها إذا أرضعته بلبن شاة ظاهر على اختيار شمس الأئمة حيث قال: الأصح أن العقد يرد على اللبن؛ لأنه د، وما سواه من القيام بمصالحه ،تبع وأما على اختيار صاحب "الهداية" المقصود، أن المعقود عليه المنفعة، وهو القيام بخدمة الولد ففيه نظر؛ لأنه جعل الإرضاع مستحقا تبعا للخدمة، فكيف يسقط كل الأجر بتركه، كذا في "الشرنبلالية" عن "البرهان. انتهى، قال العيني: وفي "المحيط": لو استأجر شاة لترضع صبيا لا يجوز؛ لأن للبن البهائم قيمة وقعت الإجارة عليه، وهو مجهول، وليس للبن المرأة قيمة فلا تقع الإجارة عليه، وإنما تقع على فعل الإرضاع والتربية والحضانة.
Reforming the child's food, so if she nurses him with sheep's milk, then no wage. 'Reforming etc.' by the wet nurse chewing his food to eat. He intended chewing, i.e., she chews the food for the child. And it was said: He intended by 'reforming' that she does not eat what harms the child, nor feed herself with food contrary to the child's temperament, and that is apparent. The conclusion: it is obligatory upon her to reform the child's food because serving the child is obligatory upon her by custom, and similarly washing his clothes from urine and stool is upon her, not from dirt, and similarly preparing the child's food upon the wet nurse. This is the summary from al-Fath, al-Takmilah, etc. 'Then if she nurses him etc.': i.e., if a man hires a wet nurse to breastfeed his child, and she nurses him with sheep's milk, and that is proven by her confession or by evidence that she nursed with the milk of an animal, not on the absence of her own milk, then she has no wage because she did not perform the obligatory work, which is breastfeeding, and this is 'eejar' (pouring into the mouth) not breastfeeding, and it is only called 'irda' (breastfeeding) metaphorically. He said in al-Takmilah: he only qualified it with sheep's milk because if she nursed him with the milk of her maid or her neighbor or with the milk of a wet nurse she hired without a contract, she gets the wage as before. I say regarding this issue there is a dispute mentioned in al-Fath: he said in Fath Allah al-Mu'in: what the author mentioned—that she gets no wage if she nurses with sheep's milk—is apparent according to the choice of Shams al-A'imma where he said: the most correct is that the contract is on the milk because it is wealth, and what else of serving its interests is subsidiary. And according to the choice of the author of al-Hidayah, the intended object is the benefit, which is serving the child, so there is consideration; because he made breastfeeding a right subsidiary to service, so how does all wage fall by leaving it? As in al-Shurnubalaliyya from al-Burhan. End. Al-Ayni said: In al-Muhit: if one hires a sheep to suckle a child, it is not valid because the milk of animals has value, and the hire is upon it, and it is unknown, and woman's milk has no value, so hire is not upon it, but rather upon the act of breastfeeding, upbringing, and custody.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage covers two related sub-issues: the duties of a wet nurse and the consequence of nursing with sheep's milk. First, the matn states that the wet nurse must 'reform' the child's food. The commentator explains this as chewing food for the child (predigestion) and, more broadly, ensuring she does not eat harmful foods that could affect her milk. Customarily, she must also clean the child's clothes from urine and stool and prepare his food. This is obligatory upon her by custom (urf). Second, if she nurses the child with sheep's milk instead of her own, she forfeits her wage entirely. This is proven by her confession or by evidence that she used animal milk. The reason is that the contracted service is breastfeeding (from her breast), not pouring milk into the mouth. The milk of a sheep is a different substance, and the contract is on her act of breastfeeding. The commentator notes a dispute regarding the object of the contract: some scholars (like Shams al-A'imma) hold that the contract is on the milk itself, while others (like the author of al-Hidayah) hold it is on the service of child care. According to the latter, the wage should not be entirely forfeited because breastfeeding is subsidiary to the service. However, the passage also mentions that if she uses milk from a source she has hired (like a maid), she still gets the wage because she is still performing the service. The discussion emphasizes that the milk of women has no market value, so the hire is on the act, not the milk. This is contrasted with hiring an animal for its milk, which is invalid due to gharar.

Key Terms
الإصلاح (al-islah): Reforming the child's food by chewing it or ensuring it is suitable for the child's health.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a customary duty of a wet nurse?
A) Reforming the child's food
B) Washing the child's clothes from urine and stool
C) Washing the child's clothes from ordinary dirt
D) Preparing the child's food

Key Takeaway
Customary duties of a wet nurse are obligatory by urf, even if not explicitly stated in the contract.

Nursing with Sheep's Milk: Forfeiture of Wage and Dispute on Contract Object
Ruling on sheep's milk nursing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a wet nurse loses her wage if she nurses with animal milk, and compare the two Hanafi views on the object of the hire contract.

Core Idea
The wet nurse forfeits her wage because she did not perform the contracted breastfeeding; the contract is on the act, not the milk.

This lesson examines the ruling when a wet nurse substitutes sheep's milk for her own. The matn clearly states she gets no wage, but commentators debate the underlying reason: is the contract for the milk or for the service? This intra-Hanafi dispute has practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling in the matn
The matn says: 'فإن أرضعته بلبن شاة، فلا أجر' (if she nurses him with sheep's milk, no wage).
2
Identify the reason given by the commentator
The commentator explains: because she did not perform the obligatory work, which is breastfeeding (الإرضاع). Pouring milk into the mouth (الإيجار) is different.
She performed a different act.
3
Understand the linguistic distinction
The text distinguishes between 'irda' (breastfeeding from the breast) and 'eejar' (pouring liquid). The contract requires 'irda'.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute
Shams al-A'imma holds that the contract is on the milk itself, while the author of al-Hidayah holds it is on the service. The dispute affects whether partial wage might be owed.
The matn's ruling supports the service view.
5
Note the exception: milk from hired helper
If she uses milk from a maid or a wet nurse she hired without a contract, she still gets wage because she is performing the service.

Invalid Ijarah: Wage as Part of the Product
First two cases of invalid ijarah with wage part of output

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify ijarah contracts where the wage is part of the output and state why they are invalid according to the Hanafi school, and note the exception for custom.

Core Idea
Wages consisting of a portion of the product are invalid due to the prohibition of the miller's qafiz.

This lesson examines two common ijarah scenarios: giving yarn to a weaver for a share of the cloth, and hiring a porter with a portion of the carried food. Though superficially convenient, such contracts are unanimously invalid in the Hanafi school because the wage is part of the very thing produced, analogous to the prohibited miller's qafiz. However, scholars of Balkh and Nasaf permitted them based on custom, showing an important exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contracts
The text presents two cases: (a) giving yarn to a weaver to weave for half or one third of the cloth, and (b) hiring a porter to carry food for a qafiz of the carried food. Note that in both, the wage is a portion of the output of the work.
The wage is not a separate known object.
2
State the ruling and reason
Both contracts are invalid (fasid) by consensus. The reason: the wage is part of what results from the work, falling under the prohibition of the 'miller's qafiz' (hiring a miller with a portion of the flour). This is based on a hadith prohibition.
The analogy is qiyas jaliy: the illa is that the wage is a portion of the output.
3
Understand the consequence
If the work is done (cloth woven or food carried), the laborer is entitled to the 'ujr al-mithl (fair wage), not to exceed the named wage. The contract is not void but fasid, so compensation for the work is required.
This distinguishes fasid from batil.
4
Note the exceptional view
The scholars of Balkh and Nasaf allowed these contracts due to the custom ('urf) of the people in their lands. This shows that custom can override the general rule in contracts, but the default Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) holds them invalid.
Custom ('urf) is a recognised source in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو دفع غزلا لينسجه بنصفه. ولو دفع غزلا إلخ: هذه ثلاث مسائل حكمها عدم الجواز عند أبي حنيفة له، ووافقه صاحباه في الأوليين، وخالفاه في الأخيرة، بيان المسألة الأولى والثانية: أن رجلا دفع إلى نساج غزلا ينسجه ثوبا بنصف الثوب أو ثلثه، أو استأجر رجلا ليحمل طعامه إلى بيته بقفيز من الطعام المحمول بأن جعل نصف الثوب وثلثه، وفقيزا من الطعام أجرته، وحكمهما عدم الجواز بالاتفاق؛ لأنه جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، فصار في معنى قفيز الطحان، وقد نهى عنها عليه، وهو أن يستأجر ثورا ليطحن له حنطة بقفيز من دقيقه، وإن حمل الطعام أو نسج الثوب، فله أجره، لا يجاوز به المسمى ومشايخ بلخ و نسف يجوزون هذين العقدين؛ لتعامل أهل بلادهم بذلك. وبيان الثالثة: أن رجلا استأجر خبازا ليخبز له اليوم دقيقا وزنه كذا ،بدرهم وحكمها عدم الجواز عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المعقود عليه مجهول؛ لأن ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المنفعة معقود عليها، وذكر العمل يوجب كونه معقودا عليه، ولا ترجيح لأحدهما ونفع المستأجر في الثاني ونفع الأجير في الأول فيفضي إلى المنازعة، وقالا: هذه جائزة؛ لأن منه نصف النهار، فله الأجر كاملا، وإن لم يفرغ فعليه أن يعمل في الغد؛ العقد على العمل دون اليوم حتى إذا فرغ .
And if he gives yarn to weave it for half of it. 'And if he gives yarn etc.': these are three issues; their ruling is non-permissibility according to Abu Hanifa, and his two companions agreed with him in the first two, and differed in the last. Explanation of the first and second issues: that a man gives to a weaver yarn to weave into a cloth for half the cloth or one third, or hires a man to carry his food to his house for a qafiz of the carried food, meaning he made half or third of the cloth and a qafiz of food his wage. Their ruling is non-permissibility by consensus because he made the wage part of what results from his work, so it falls under the meaning of the miller's qafiz, which has been prohibited. And that is that he hires an ox to grind wheat for a qafiz of its flour. And if he carries the food or weaves the cloth, he gets his wage, not exceeding the named amount. And the scholars of Balkh and Nasaf allow these two contracts due to the practice of the people of their land. And explanation of the third: that a man hires a baker to bake for him today flour of a certain weight for a dirham. Its ruling is non-permissibility according to Abu Hanifa because the object of the contract is unknown; because mentioning time necessitates that the benefit is the object, and mentioning the work necessitates that the work is the object, and neither has priority, and the benefit of the lessee is in the second and the benefit of the hireling is in the first, leading to dispute. And they (Sahibayn) said: this is permissible because he (the hireling) works half the day, so he gets the full wage, but if he does not finish, he must work the next day; the contract is on the work, not on the day, until he finishes.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents three cases of potentially invalid ijarah contracts. The first two involve making the wage a part of the output of the work, such as giving yarn to a weaver in exchange for half the cloth, or hiring a porter to carry food for a qafiz of that food. These are unanimously invalid according to the Hanafi school because the wage is part of the very thing produced, analogous to the prohibited 'miller's qafiz' (hiring a miller with a portion of the flour). This is based on a hadith prohibition. However, the scholars of Balkh and Nasaf permit these contracts due to local custom. The third case is hiring a baker to bake a specific amount of dough for the day for a dirham. Here, Abu Hanifa considers it invalid because the contract is ambiguous: mentioning both the time (today) and the specific work creates confusion about whether the contract is on the time or the work, leading to potential disputes. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, considering it valid. Their reasoning: the contract is on the work, not the time, so if the baker finishes half the day, he gets full wage; if he does not finish, he must continue the next day. This dispute highlights the Hanafi attention to certainty in the object of contract.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): The practice of hiring a miller to grind wheat in exchange for a portion of the flour; prohibited by hadith.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): Fair wage determined by market rate for similar work in similar circumstances.
عرف (urf): Custom or established practice of the people, recognized as a source of law in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the first two cases (yarn for weaving and carrying food for a qafiz) invalid in the Hanafi school?
A) The wage is less than the market rate.
B) The wage is a portion of the output, analogous to the miller's qafiz.
C) The worker is not qualified.
D) The contract period is not specified.

Key Takeaway
Wages that are a portion of the product are invalid (fasid) due to uncertainty and analogy to the prohibited miller's qafiz, though custom may permit them.

Ijarah Dispute: Ambiguity Between Time and Work
Third case of invalid ijarah with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding ijarah contracts that mention both a specific time and a specific amount of work, and identify the reasoning of each side.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa invalidates a contract that ambiguously mentions both time and work; Sahibayn validate it by prioritizing work.

This lesson examines a third case of ijarah: hiring a baker for a day to bake a specific amount of dough for a dirham. Abu Hanifa considers this invalid because the contract's object is ambiguous—is it the time (day) or the work (baking the dough)? This ambiguity could cause disputes. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that the contract is on the work, not the time, and therefore valid. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify legal uncertainty (gharar) in contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the contract details
The contract: hire a baker to bake a specific amount of dough 'today' for a dirham. Two elements are mentioned: the time (today) and the specific work (baking a certain weight of dough).
The wage is fixed (one dirham), so the dispute is about the subject matter.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and reason
Abu Hanifa says the contract is invalid (fasid). Reason: the object of the contract is unknown (majhul) because mentioning the time suggests the benefit (manfa'ah) is the use of the baker's time, while mentioning the work suggests the work itself is the object. Neither has priority, leading to ambiguity which results in potential dispute.
This is a case of jahalah in the subject matter.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position and reason
The Sahibayn say the contract is valid. They argue that the contract is on the work, not on the day. So if the baker finishes work in half a day, he gets full wage; if he doesn't finish, he must continue the next day. The day is just a timeframe, not the subject matter.
They prioritize the work element because it is more specific and quantifiable.
4
Evaluate the difference
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): under Abu Hanifa, the contract is fasid and if work is done, baker gets ujr al-mithl. Under Sahibayn, the contract is valid and baker gets the named dirham, with obligation to complete work if needed.
The dispute is about how to resolve ambiguity when a contract mentions two potential objects.

Source Text

ولو دفع غزلا لينسجه بنصفه. ولو دفع غزلا إلخ: هذه ثلاث مسائل حكمها عدم الجواز عند أبي حنيفة له، ووافقه صاحباه في الأوليين، وخالفاه في الأخيرة، بيان المسألة الأولى والثانية: أن رجلا دفع إلى نساج غزلا ينسجه ثوبا بنصف الثوب أو ثلثه، أو استأجر رجلا ليحمل طعامه إلى بيته بقفيز من الطعام المحمول بأن جعل نصف الثوب وثلثه، وفقيزا من الطعام أجرته، وحكمهما عدم الجواز بالاتفاق؛ لأنه جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، فصار في معنى قفيز الطحان، وقد نهى عنها عليه، وهو أن يستأجر ثورا ليطحن له حنطة بقفيز من دقيقه، وإن حمل الطعام أو نسج الثوب، فله أجره، لا يجاوز به المسمى ومشايخ بلخ و نسف يجوزون هذين العقدين؛ لتعامل أهل بلادهم بذلك. وبيان الثالثة: أن رجلا استأجر خبازا ليخبز له اليوم دقيقا وزنه كذا ،بدرهم وحكمها عدم الجواز عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المعقود عليه مجهول؛ لأن ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المنفعة معقود عليها، وذكر العمل يوجب كونه معقودا عليه، ولا ترجيح لأحدهما ونفع المستأجر في الثاني ونفع الأجير في الأول فيفضي إلى المنازعة، وقالا: هذه جائزة؛ لأن منه نصف النهار، فله الأجر كاملا، وإن لم يفرغ فعليه أن يعمل في الغد؛ العقد على العمل دون اليوم حتى إذا فرغ .

Ruling on a Wet Nurse Feeding Child with Goat's Milk: Forfeiture of Wage and Customary Duties
Ruling on wet nurse's wage when she feeds child with animal milk, plus customary duties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on ijarah to determine when a wet nurse's failure to breastfeed from her own breast results in forfeiture of wages, and state the customary duties required of her.

Core Idea
A wet nurse's wage is forfeited if she feeds the child with any milk other than her own, because the contract is for the act of breastfeeding, not just feeding.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific case in ijarah: a wet nurse (ظئر) hired to breastfeed a child. The author first outlines her customary duties—preparing the child's food and washing clothes from impurities—then delivers the main ruling: if she feeds the child with goat's milk (or any animal milk), she forfeits her wage entirely. The commentary clarifies that 'breastfeeding' in the contract means suckling from her breast; pouring milk into the mouth is a different act. This distinction is rooted in the Hanafi understanding that the contract is for the service of breastfeeding, not for the milk itself (since human milk has no monetary value). We will dissect the ruling and explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement that surrounds it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracted service
The ijarah contract is for the act of breastfeeding (إرضاع) from the wet nurse's own breast. The passage emphasizes that this is the wajib (obligatory) work she must perform.
Customary duties (food preparation, washing) are subsidiary but still required.
2
Distinguish between real breastfeeding and mere feeding
The commentary introduces a linguistic distinction: إرضاع is sucking from the breast, while إيجار is merely pouring milk into the mouth. The word 'breastfeeding' in the contract is used by resemblance (مشاكلة), but the contract's subject is the former.
This linguistic analysis is key to understanding why goat's milk does not fulfill the contract.
3
Apply the consequence: forfeiture of wage
Since the wet nurse performed an act (إيجار) that is not the contracted service (إرضاع), she did not fulfill her obligation. Therefore, she is not entitled to any wage. The text states 'فلا أجر' (no wage).
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, based on Shams al-A'imma's view.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement: Shams al-A'imma holds that the contract is on the milk itself, so giving animal milk is a different subject, thus no wage. Al-Hidayah holds that the contract is on the service, and breastfeeding is a part of service; omitting it should reduce but not eliminate wage. The text follows the former.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether any wage is due at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إصلاح طعام الصبي، فإن أرضعته بلبن شاة، فلا أجر، ولو دفع غزلا لينسجه بنصفه، اعتبارا للعرف شرط أي الظئر الصبي في المدة جزاءه إصلاح إلخ بأن تمضغ المرضعة طعامه ليأكل أراد به المضغ أي أن تمضغ الطعام للصبي، وقيل: أراد بالإصلاح أن لا تأكل ما يضر بالصبي، ولا تتغذى بغذاء يخالف مزاج الصبي، وهو الظاهر والحاصل: أنه يجب عليها إصلاح طعام الصبي؛ لأن خدمة الصبي واجبة عليها عرفا، وكذا غسل ثيابه عن البول والغائط عليها، لا عن الوسخ، وكذا تهيئة طعام الصبي على الظئر. (هذا) خلاصة ما في الفتح والتكملة وغيرهما) فإن أرضعته إلخ : أي إذا استأجر رجل ظئرا ليرضع ولده فأرضعته لبن شاة، وثبت ذلك بإقرارها أو بالبينة قامت على إرضاعها بلبن البهائم لا على عدم إرضاعها لبن نفسها، فإنها شهادة على النفي لا أجر لها؛ لأنها لم تأت الواجب عليها من العمل، وهو الإرضاع، وهذا إيجار لا إرضاع، والإيجار صب شيء في الفم، وإنما أطلق عليه لفظ الإرضاع للمشاكلة، قال في التكملة: وإنما قيد بلبن الشاة؛ لأنها لو أرضعته بلبن خادمتها أو جاريتها أو بلبن ظئر استأجرتها بلا عقد، فلها الأجر كما تقدم. أقول في هذه المسألة خلاف ذكره في الفتح: قال في فتح الله المعين بقي أن يقال: ما ذكره المصنف لا أجر لها إذا أرضعته بلبن شاة ظاهر على اختيار شمس الأئمة حيث قال: الأصح أن العقد يرد على اللبن؛ لأنه د، وما سواه من القيام بمصالحه تبع وأما على اختيار صاحب الهداية المقصود، أن المعقود عليه المنفعة، وهو القيام بخدمة الولد ففيه نظر؛ لأنه جعل الإرضاع مستحقا تبعا للخدمة، فكيف يسقط كل الأجر بتركه، كذا في الشرنبلالية عن البرهان. انتهى، قال العيني: وفي المحيط: لو استأجر شاة لترضع صبيا لا يجوز؛ لأن للبن البهائم قيمة وقعت الإجارة عليه، وهو مجهول، وليس للبن المرأة قيمة فلا تقع الإجارة عليه، وإنما تقع على فعل الإرضاع والتربية والحضانة [رمز الحقائق: 280/2]
Fixing the child's food, and if she breastfeeds him with goat's milk, then no wage, and if he gives yarn to weave for half of it, consideration of custom... [Explanation:] Fixing etc. that she chews his food for him to eat; intended by chewing is that she chews food for the child. It is said: intended by fixing that she does not eat what harms the child, nor eat food that contravenes the child's temperament, and this is apparent. The gist: that she must fix the child's food because serving the child is obligatory on her customarily, and likewise washing his clothes from urine and stool is upon her, not from dirt, and likewise preparing the child's food is upon the wet nurse. As for if she breastfeeds him etc.: i.e., if a man hires a wet nurse to breastfeed his child and she feeds him goat's milk, and this is established by her confession or by evidence of her feeding with animal milk—not evidence that she did not feed her own milk—then that is testimony of a negative, so she has no wage because she did not perform the obligatory work, which is breastfeeding. This is pouring into the mouth, not breastfeeding, and it is called breastfeeding only by resemblance. In al-Takmila: he restricted it to goat's milk because if she feeds him with milk of her maid or neighbor or a hired wet nurse without a contract, she gets wage as before. I say there is a disagreement in this issue mentioned in al-Fath. ... [Continued]

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses a case in fasid (invalid) ijarah. The author first states that a wet nurse (ظئر) is obliged to prepare the child's food and wash clothes from impurities, as this is customary service. Then the main ruling: if she feeds the child with goat's milk (or any animal milk) instead of her own, she forfeits all wages because she failed to perform the contracted service (breastfeeding). The commentary clarifies that pouring milk into the mouth is not considered breastfeeding in the shari'i sense. The ruling is based on the fact that the contract is for the act of breastfeeding, not the milk itself (since women's milk has no monetary value). There is a disagreement among later scholars: according to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, the contract is on the milk itself, so if she gives animal milk, it is a different subject; but according to al-Hidayah, the contract is on the service, and breastfeeding is part of service, so omitting it reduces wage but does not cancel entirely? The text here sides with Shams al-A'imma. The additional note about hiring a goat for breastfeeding is also invalid because the milk is unknown and has value, making the ijarah invalid due to ignorance.

Key Terms
ظئر (dha'ir): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child.
إيجار (ījār): Pouring something into the mouth, not the act of breastfeeding.
المشاكلة (al-mushākala): Linguistic resemblance; the word 'lactation' is used figuratively here.

Invalidity of Ijarah When Wage is Part of the Product
Ruling on three cases where wage is a portion of the produced item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases of invalid ijarah where the wage is part of the output, explain the analogy to qafiz al-tahhan, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the third case.

Core Idea
Paying the worker with a share of his own product renders the ijarah invalid due to uncertainty (gharar).

This lesson examines three specific scenarios from Kanz al-Daqa'iq where an ijarah contract is ruled invalid because the wage consists of a portion of the item produced by the worker's labor. The first two cases are invalid by consensus of Abu Hanifa and his companions, drawing on the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan' precedent. The third case sparks an intra-madhhab dispute: Abu Hanifa deems it invalid due to ambiguity in the contract subject, while the Sahibayn consider it valid. Scholars from Balkh and Nasaf later allowed the first two based on local custom, illustrating how later Hanafi practice can accommodate 'urf in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Cases
List the three contracts: (1) giving yarn to a weaver to weave for half/third of the cloth; (2) hiring a carrier to transport food for a qafiz of the food itself; (3) hiring a baker to bake a specific amount of flour for a dirham for a day. Note that in each, the wage is part of the output or ambiguous in subject.
The first two share the pattern: wage = portion of the product. The third mixes time and work.
2
Understand the Prohibition of Qafiz al-Tahhan
The first two cases are analogized to the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan'—hiring a miller to grind grain and paying him with a qafiz of the flour. This is prohibited because the wage is uncertain (jahalah) and resembles riba. The same illa applies here: the wage is part of what the worker produces, creating gharar.
This is a clear qiyas jali: the miller case is the asl, the weaver/carrier are the far'.
3
Trace the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Third Case
Abu Hanifa: the contract is invalid because the subject is ambiguous—is it the work (baking) or the time (the day)? This ambiguity leads to potential dispute. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the contract is on the work; the time reference is merely a container (zarf), not a condition. They argue that if the baker finishes early, he gets full wage; if not, he must continue. A narration from Abu Hanifa allows it if the word 'fi' (in) is used, as it emphasizes the work within the day.
The practical difference: if the contract is valid, the baker gets full wage upon completion even before the day ends; if invalid, he gets wage commensurate with work done, not exceeding the named amount.
4
Consider the Custom-Based Exception
The scholars of Balkh and Nasaf allowed the first two contracts based on the customary practice of the people in their regions. This shows that later Hanafi jurists sometimes override the original ruling due to 'urf (custom) in mu'amalat, though the text notes this view without adopting it.
This is an example of how the madhhab evolves: Zahir al-Riwayah prohibits, but later fatwa may accommodate custom under necessity.

ولو دفع غزلا لينسجه بنصفه، أو استأجره ليحمل طعامه بقفيز منه، أو ليخبز له كذا اليوم بدرهم لم يجز. ولو دفع غزلا إلخ: هذه ثلاث مسائل حكمها عدم الجواز عند أبي حنيفة له، ووافقه صاحباه في الأوليين، وخالفاه في الأخيرة. بيان المسألة الأولى والثانية: أن رجلا دفع إلى نساج غزلا ينسجه ثوبا بنصف الثوب أو ثلثه، أو استأجر رجلا ليحمل طعامه إلى بيته بقفيز من الطعام المحمول بأن جعل نصف الثوب وثلثه، وقفيزا من الطعام أجرته، وحكمهما عدم الجواز بالاتفاق؛ لأنه جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، فصار في معنى قفيز الطحان، وقد نهى عليها عنه، وهو أن يستأجر ثورا ليطحن له حنطة بقفيز من دقيقه، وإن حمل الطعام أو نسج الثوب، فله أجره، لا يجاوز به المسمى ومشايخ بلخ و نسف يجوزون هذين العقدين؛ لتعامل أهل بلادهم بذلك. وبيان الثالثة: أن رجلا استأجر خبازا ليخبز له اليوم دقيقا وزنه كذا بدرهم وحكمها عدم الجواز عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المعقود عليه مجهول؛ لأن ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المنفعة معقود عليها، وذكر العمل يوجب كونه معقودا عليه، ولا ترجيح لأحدهما ونفع المستأجر في الثاني ونفع الأجير في الأول فيفضي إلى المنازعة، وقالا: هذه جائزة؛ لأن العقد على العمل دون اليوم حتى إذا فرغ منه نصف النهار، فله الأجر كاملا، وإن لم يفرغ فعليه أن يعمل في الغد؛ لأن المعقود عليه هو العمل، وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة أنه إذا سمى عملا، وقال في اليوم جازت الإجارة؛ لأن كلمة في للظرف لا لتقدير المدة، فلا تقتضي الاستغراق، فكان المعقود عليه هو العمل، وهو معلوم، بخلاف ما إذا حذفت في، فإنه يقتضي الاستغراق. لم يجز متعلق بالمسائل المذكورة أي لم يجز هذه الإجارات الثلاث
And if he gives yarn to weave for half of it, or he hires him to carry his food for a qafiz of it, or to bake for him for a day for a dirham, it is not permissible. 'And if he gives yarn etc.' These are three issues: their ruling is non-permissibility according to Abu Hanifa, and his two companions agreed with him on the first two, and disagreed on the last. Explanation of the first two issues: a man gives yarn to a weaver to weave a cloth for half or third of the cloth, or hires a man to carry his food to his house for a qafiz of the carried food—by making half/third of the cloth and a qafiz of food as his wage—their ruling is non-permissibility by consensus because he made the wage part of what comes out of his work, so it becomes like the qafiz of the miller, which is prohibited. If he carries the food or weaves the cloth, he gets his wage, not exceeding the named [wage]. The scholars of Balkh and Nasa allow these two contracts due to the custom of the people. Explanation of the third: a man hires a baker to bake for him today a certain weight of flour for a dirham; its ruling is impermissibility according to Abu Hanifa because the subject of the contract is unknown: mentioning time makes the benefit the subject, mentioning work makes the work the subject, no preference; benefit of the hirer in the second and benefit of the worker in the first leads to dispute. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: this is permissible because the contract is on the work, not the day, so if he finishes half the day, he gets full wage, and if he doesn't finish, he must work tomorrow; the subject is the work. In a narration from Abu Hanifa: if he specifies the work and says 'in the day' the ijarah is valid because 'in' is for container not for time limit.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq's sharh deals with three specific cases of fasid ijarah where the wage is a part of the item produced. The first two cases (weaver and carrier) are invalid by consensus of Abu Hanifa and his two companions because the wage is part of the product, analogous to the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan' (paying a miller for grinding with a qafiz of the flour). However, some later Hanafis from Balkh allow it based on custom. The third case (baker hired for a day at a fixed dirham) is invalid according to Abu Hanifa because there is ambiguity: does the contract center on the day (time) or the baking (work)? This leads to potential dispute. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, deem it valid, considering the contract to be on the work, not the day. There is even a narration from Abu Hanifa allowing it if the word 'fi' (in) is used, as it implies container, not full time. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the impermissibility according to Abu Hanifa for the third case as well, but later practice may follow the companions due to custom.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): A prohibited transaction where the miller's wage is a qafiz (measure) of the flour he grinds.
مشايخ بلخ و نسف (mashāyikh Balkh wa Nasaf): Senior Hanafi scholars from the regions of Balkh and Nasaf who allowed these contracts based on custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the contract of hiring a weaver to weave yarn for half of the cloth invalid?
A) The weaver is not a professional.
B) The wage is not specified in monetary terms.
C) The wage is part of the product of the weaver's labor, resembling qafiz al-tahhan.
D) The cloth may be defective.

Key Takeaway
Paying a worker with a share of the item he produces renders the ijarah invalid due to gharar; the first two cases are prohibited by consensus, while the third case involves a legitimate intra-madhhab disagreement.

Invalid Conditions in Land Ijarah (Double-Plowing, Digging Canals, etc.)
Ruling on four cases of invalid land ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four invalid conditions in land ijarah and explain why each invalidates the contract, distinguishing between cases where the condition is necessary or the lease is long.

Core Idea
A land lease is invalid if a condition gives lasting benefit to the owner beyond the lease term, unless the land needs it or the term is long.

This lesson examines four specific conditions that can invalidate a land lease (ijarah) according to the Hanafi school. While basic cultivation terms are valid, added requirements like double-plowing, digging large canals, or manuring the land may render the contract void if they provide ongoing benefit to the owner. The text also addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding rent paid as cultivation of another land. Understanding these nuances is crucial for ensuring ijarah contracts remain valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited conditions
List the four conditions from the passage: double-plowing (tathniya), digging large canals (karrī al-anhār), manuring (sarqana), and making the wage the cultivation of another land for the owner. Note that the first three share a common rationale.
2
Apply the general principle of invalidating conditions
A condition that is not required by the contract and provides lasting benefit to the owner invalidates the ijarah. Understand that the benefit survives the lease term, effectively giving the owner extra compensation.
This is based on the rule that ijarah is a contract for current benefit; lasting improvements belong to the owner but must not be paid for by the tenant via conditions.
3
Distinguish between lasting and temporary benefits
Examine how the lease duration and necessity affect validity. If the lease is long enough that the benefit is exhausted, or if the condition is necessary for cultivation (e.g., digging small streams, initial plowing), the condition is valid. For large canals and manuring, the effect typically lasts beyond a short lease.
The text mentions that if the period is long the condition may not invalidate. Also, the land's need for two plowings or the necessity of digging small streams saves the contract.
4
Analyze the fourth case: exchange of identical benefits
The fourth case involves paying rent by cultivating another land for the owner. The Hanafi view is that this is invalid because it is selling a benefit (cultivation) for its like on credit, which resembles riba. Ijarah is only allowed when the types differ.
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering the benefit as existent and thus a valid sale of existent for existent.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i opinion and Hanafi response
Understand the basis of the dispute: Shafi'i views the determined benefit as existent, making the exchange like a spot sale. Hanafi counters that ijarah is an exception from normal sale rules due to necessity, and no necessity exists when the benefit type is identical.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi practice such a contract is fasid and the tenant must pay ujrat al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استأجر أرضا على أن يكربها ويزرعها، أو يسقيها ويزرعها، صح، فإن شرط أن يثنيها أو يكري أنهارها أو يسرقنها أو يزرعها للمؤجر أرضا أخرى بأن يجعل أجرها زراعة أرض أخرى لم يجز. هذه أربع مسائل حكمها عدم جواز الإجارة. بيان الثلاثة الأول: أن من استأجر أرضا ليزرعها، وشرط عليه المؤجر أن يثنيها المستأجر، أو يكري أنهارها أي يحفرها، أو يسرقنها أي يجعل فيها السرقين فهذه الإجارات ليست بجائزة؛ لأن فيها شروطا لا يقتضيه العقد، وكل شرط كذلك فهو مفسد الإجارة، فإن أثر التثنية وكري الأنهار والسرقنة يبقي فيه معنى عقد الإجارة، فيكون عقد فيه نفع لصاحب الأرض، وهو شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، فيفسد، ولأن الأرض يصير مستأجرا منافع الأجير بعد مضي المدة، فتصير صفقة في صفقة، فلا يجوز. وهذا الحكم أي عدم الجواز إذا لم يكن المدة طويلة، وأما إذا كانت المدة طويلة حيث لا يبقى أثر الكري والتثنية والسرقنة، أو كان الريع لا يحصل إلا به لا يفسد اشتراطه؛ لأنه مما يقتضيه العقد. واختلفوا في المراد بالتثنية، فقيل: يردها المستأجر مكروبة، فهذا لا شبهة في فساده في كل حال، وقيل: أن يكربها مرتين، وفيه تفصيل فإن كانت الأرض لا تحتاج إلى الكراب مرتين، وكانت المدة قصيرة، يفسد، وإن كانت الأرض تحتاج إلى الكراب مرتين، أو لا يحتاج ولكن المدة طويلة لا يبقى أثره بعد مضيها، لا يفسد كما أشرنا إليه أولا. ثم المراد بكري الأنهار، الأنهار العظام لا الجداول؛ لأن كري الجداول لا بد منه للزراعة، فيكون من مقتضيات العقد، ولا يبقى أثره بعد العام، بخلاف كري الأنهار العظام، فإنه يبقى أثره إلى القابل، فيكون مفسدا. وبيان الأخيرة: أن رجلا استأجر أرضا ليزرعها، وجعل أجرها زراعة أرض أخرى بأن يزرعها المستأجر للمؤجر، فهذه الإجارة أيضا غير صحيحة عندنا، وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: جائزة؛ لأن المنفعة جعلت موجودة، فيكون بيع الموجود بالموجود، ولنا أنه بيع الشيء بجنسه نسيئة وهو حرام؛ لأن الإجارة جوزت بخلاف القياس؛ للحاجة، ولا حاجة عند اتحاد الجنس، بخلاف ما إذا اختلف جنس المنفعة
And if he hires land to plow and cultivate it, or to water and cultivate it, it is valid. But if he stipulates that he double-plow it, or dig its canals, or manure it, or cultivate for the owner another land by making its wage the cultivation of another land, it is not permissible. These are four issues: their ruling is non-permissibility. Explanation of the first three: a man hires land to cultivate, and the owner stipulates that the tenant double-plow, dig canals, or manure—these ijarahs are not permissible because they contain conditions not required by the contract, and every such condition invalidates the ijarah. The effect of double-plowing, digging canals, and manuring remains after the lease, so the contract includes benefit for the owner, which is a condition not required by the contract, thus it invalidates. Also, the land becomes hiring the benefits of the worker after the period, making a sale in sale. This ruling (non-permissibility) applies if the period is not long; if the period is long such that the effect disappears, or the profit cannot be obtained without it, then it does not invalidate because it is required by the contract. There is disagreement on the meaning of 'tathniya': some say the tenant returns the land plowed; this is invalid in all cases. Others say to plow twice; if the land does not need two plowings and the period is short, it invalidates; if the land needs two plowings or the period is long so effect vanishes, it does not invalidate. By 'digging canals' means large canals, not small streams; digging streams is necessary for cultivation, so it is required by the contract, and its effect does not last after the year, unlike large canals. Explanation of the last: a man hires land to cultivate and makes its wage the cultivation of another land (the tenant cultivates for the owner); this ijarah is invalid according to us. Al-Shafi'i said it is valid because the benefit is made existent, so it is a sale of existent for existent. Our argument: it is selling a thing for its type on credit, which is prohibited because ijarah is allowed contrary to qiyas due to necessity, and there is no necessity when the type is the same, unlike when the type of benefit differs.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage discusses four types of invalid land lease conditions. The first three involve the lessee agreeing to double-plow the land, dig its canals, or spread manure. These conditions are invalid unless the lease period is long enough that the benefit is exhausted within the period (i.e., the improvement does not survive the lease). If the condition provides lasting benefit to the owner beyond the term, it constitutes an extra consideration and invalidates the contract. The fourth case is when the rent is paid in the form of cultivating another piece of land for the owner—this is invalid because it is exchange of the same type of benefit (cultivation) on credit, resembling riba. Imam al-Shafi'i allows it because he considers the benefits as existing items (since they are determinable), so it is a valid sale. The Hanafi response is that ijarah is an exception to qiyas based on need; when the types are identical, there is no need for the exception, so the contract is forbidden.

Key Terms
تثنية (tathniya): Double-plowing the land; a condition where the tenant must plow the land twice.
سرقنة (sarqana): Spreading manure (sarqin) on the land.
كري الأنهار (karrī al-anhār): Digging or dredging large canals; small streams (jadawil) are exempt as necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the condition of digging large canals in a land lease invalidate the ijarah?
A) Because digging is hard work and the tenant should not be forced to do it.
B) Because the benefit of digging large canals remains after the lease term, providing lasting benefit to the owner.
C) Because the owner must do it himself.
D) Because digging canals is not related to cultivation.

Key Takeaway
A land lease is invalid if it includes a condition that gives the owner lasting benefit beyond the lease term and is not required by the contract, unless the lease is long enough to exhaust the benefit or the condition is necessary for cultivation.

Three Invalid Hire Contracts and the Linguistic Nuance of 'Fi'
Ruling and linguistic analysis of three invalid ijarah cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three invalid hire contracts and explain the Hanafi linguistic analysis of the word 'fi' that can validate a contract when the work is specified.

Core Idea
Ambiguity in wage or duration invalidates a hire contract, but specifying work with 'fi' may salvage it.

The Hanafi school strictly requires clarity in hire contracts. This passage presents three classic cases where ambiguity renders the contract invalid, then explores a nuanced exception: using the word 'fi' (in) can indicate a container, not a measure, thus not requiring the entire duration, potentially validating the contract if the work is specified. Let's examine the rulings and the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
List the three invalid hire contracts
Identify each case from the passage: (1) hiring to carry food in exchange for a qafiz of that food, (2) hiring to bake for a certain day for a dirham without specifying the day, (3) hiring a man with a wage from the flour being transported.
All three involve ambiguity (jahalah) in the wage or duration.
2
State the hukm for each contract
The passage states 'lam yajuz' (it is not permissible). The hukm level is fasid (invalid) due to the ambiguity.
Hanafi distinguishes fasid from batil; fasid contracts can sometimes be rectified.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that if the hirer specifies the work and says 'fi al-yawm' (in the day), the contract is valid. This is an exception.
This shows that the ruling is not absolute; the wording matters.
4
Analyse the linguistic proof for 'fi'
The word 'fi' is a preposition meaning 'in', which functions as a container (zarf) not a measure of duration. It does not imply the entire day, so the contract can be valid if the work is known.
If 'fi' is omitted, the phrase implies the entire duration, causing ambiguity.
5
Apply the distinction to the three cases
In the given cases, 'fi' is not used to specify the work, so they remain invalid. If the hirer had said 'carry my food in the day for a qafiz' and the work was specified, it could be valid per the narration.
The key is whether the work is specified and 'fi' is used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو استأجره ليحمل طعامه بقفيز منه، أو ليخبز له كذا اليوم بدرهم لم يجز، وإن استأجر أي رجلا بأن جعل القفيز أجرته من الدقيق، وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة أنه إذا سمى عملا، وقال في اليوم جازت الإجارة؛ لأن كلمة "في" للظرف لا لتقدير المدة، فلا تقتضي الاستغراق، فكان المعقود عليه هو العمل، وهو معلوم، بخلاف ما إذا حذفت "في"، فإنه يقتضي الاستغراق. لم يجز متعلق بالمسائل المذكورة أي لم يجز هذه الإجارات الثلاث.
Or if he hires him to carry his food for a qafiz of it, or to bake for him such-and-such a day for a dirham, it is not permissible. And if he hires a man by making the qafiz his wage from the flour, and in a narration from Abu Hanifa that if he specifies a work and says 'in the day' the hire is permissible, because the word 'fi' is for the container not for estimating the duration, so it does not require continuity, so the contracted object is the work, and it is known, unlike if 'fi' is omitted, then it requires continuity. 'Lam yajiz' pertains to the mentioned cases, i.e., these three hire contracts are not permissible.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ijarah presents three cases of invalid (fasid) hire contracts. The first: a man hires someone to carry his food and pays him with a qafiz of that same food — this creates ambiguity in the wage. The second: hires someone to bake for a certain number of days for a dirham, but the duration is unspecified. The third: hires a man and makes his wage a qafiz from the flour being transported. All three are invalid because the consideration is uncertain. The commentary then explains a nuance: if the hirer says 'in the day' (fi al-yawm), the word 'fi' indicates a container, not a precise measure of time, so it does not imply the entire day, thus the contract could be valid if the work is clearly specified. However, in these cases, the contracts are invalid because of the ambiguity. This ruling is from Abu Hanifa with a differing narration that allows it if the work is specified.

Key Terms
في (fi): A preposition meaning 'in', analyzed as a container (zarf) not a duration indicator.
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): An invalid hire contract due to a defect like ambiguity or prohibited condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ambiguity (jahalah) in the wage or duration
C) The work is impossible
D) The contract is for a prohibited act

Key Takeaway
A hire contract must have a known wage and duration; ambiguity invalidates it, but using the word 'fi' can specify the work and salvage the contract per one Hanafi narration.

Valid Hire of Land with Conditions Inherent to the Contract
Ruling on valid ijarah when condition is inherent to the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that conditions inherent to the contract (muqtadayat al-'aqd) do not invalidate an ijarah contract, and distinguish between valid and invalid conditions in hiring land.

Core Idea
A condition that is necessary for the purpose of the contract does not invalidate it—it is part of the agreement.

This passage presents a clear ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the validity of hiring land with conditions to plow and sow. The key principle is that conditions which are inherent to the contract (muqtadayat al-'aqd) do not invalidate the hire. Since agriculture requires plowing and watering, requiring the lessee to perform these acts is not an extra burden but part of the contracted work. Understanding this principle helps you determine when conditions in ijarah contracts are valid or invalid under Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stipulated condition
Read the passage and identify the conditions mentioned: plowing and sowing, or watering and sowing.
The condition is that the lessee must perform these agricultural tasks.
2
Assess whether the condition is inherent to the contract's purpose
Determine if the condition is necessary to achieve the goal of the contract—here, cultivation.
Agriculture cannot be accomplished without plowing and watering.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
Recall the principle: any condition that is a requirement of the contract (muqtadayat al-'aqd) does not invalidate it.
This is a derived rule from the school's usul.
4
State the ruling
Conclude that the hire is valid (sahih) because the conditions are inherent.
The commentator affirms this as the relied-upon position.
5
Distinguish from non-inherent conditions
Consider a condition that is not necessary for the contract's purpose, e.g., painting a fence. Such a condition would invalidate the hire.
This distinction is crucial for applying the rule correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استأجر أرضا على أن يكربها ويزرعها، أو يسقيها ويزرعها، صح. هذه المسألة مبنية على أن كل شرط يكون من مقتضيات العقد لا يفسد الإجارة، وصورتها أن يستأجر أحد أرضا على أن يكريها المستأجر، ويزرعها، فهذه الإجارة صحيحة؛ لأنه شرط يقتضيه العقد؛ لأن الزراعة لا تأتي إلا بالكراب والسقي. أن يكربها من باب طلب وهو إثارة الأرض وقلبها للزراعة.
And if he hires land on condition that he plows it and sows it, or waters it and sows it, it is valid. This issue is based on the principle that any condition that is a requirement of the contract does not invalidate the hire. Its scenario is that a man hires land on condition that the lessee plows it and sows it; this hire is valid because it is a condition required by the contract, since agriculture is not accomplished except by plowing and watering. 'Yakribuha' is from the root meaning to stir the earth and turn it over for cultivation.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage states a valid hire contract: hiring land for plowing, sowing, or watering and sowing. The validity hinges on the principle that conditions inherent to the purpose of the contract do not invalidate it. Plowing and watering are essential for agriculture, so requiring them is not an extra burden but a necessary part of the work. The commentator clarifies that 'yakribuha' means to stir the soil for planting. This establishes the Hanafi rule that conditions that are part of the contracted work (muqtadayat al-'aqd) keep the contract valid.

Key Terms
مقتضيات العقد (muqtadayat al-'aqd): Conditions that are logically required by the nature of the contract.
يكربها (yakrubuha): To plow or stir the soil for cultivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because the condition is written.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, conditions that are inherently required by the nature of the contract (muqtadayat al-'aqd) do not invalidate the contract; they are considered part of the agreement.

The Ruling on Invalid Ijarah: Named Wage by Istihsan
Discusses the ruling for invalid ijarah and the proof for named wage by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an invalid ijarah when the benefit is realized, and explain why the named wage is due by istihsan over the fair wage by qiyas.

Core Idea
An invalid hire contract becomes valid upon use, and the agreed wage is due by istihsan, not the fair wage.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a critical issue: when a hire contract (ijarah) is invalid due to uncertainty (jahalah), what wage is owed after the service is performed? The Hanafi school, relying on istihsan, rules that the named wage (musamma) is payable, in contrast to the qiyas which would mandate the fair market wage. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind istihsan and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The author states: 'If the term expires, he receives the named wage.' Identify that this applies when the benefit has been realized (e.g., the period of hire has passed).
2
Recognize the basis of invalidity
The contract was fasid due to uncertainty (jahalah) e.g., not specifying the load or crop. Understand that jahalah prevents validity.
3
Understand the removal of the impediment
Once the benefit is realized (use occurs), the uncertainty is resolved, so the contract can become valid.
4
Analyze the proof: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Qiyas would give the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) because the contract was initially invalid. Istihsan gives the named wage because the impediment (potential dispute) is removed and the contract is restored. This is the basis of the dispute with Imam Zufar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
الإجارة الفاسدة
ومضى الأجل، فله المسمى، وإن استأجر حمارا إلى مكة، ولم يسم ما يحمل، فحمل ما يحمل الناس، فنفق لم يضمن، وإن بلغ مكة، فله المسمى، فإن تشاحًا قبل الذرع على الحمار على مثله أي هلك في الطريق والحمل، نقضت الإجارة دفعا للفساد.
وقيل الحمل في الثانية للمؤجر أي اختصما إلى القاضي في الأولى ومضى الأجل لا يقال: مضي الأجل ليس بشرط لعود العقد إلى الصحة بل إذا زرع ارتفعت الجهالة قبل تمام العقد، فكيف قيد المصنف بمضي الأجل، ولهذا قال في "الدر": لو حذف قوله: "فمضى الأجل" كقاضي خان لكان أولى؛ لأنا نقول: لم يقيد المصنف بمضي الأجل؛ لأنه شرط عود العقد إلى الصحة بل لتتوجه المطالبة بالأجر؛ إذ لا طلب له عليه بالأجرة قبل انقضاء وقتها، فتدبر كذا في "الفتح" بتغيير يسير.
فله المسمى استحسانا، وفي القياس له أجر المثل وبه قال زفر. (المحشي)] لأن الجهالة الموجبة للفساد قد ارتفعت، قال في "النهاية": فإن قيل: إذا ارتفعت الجهالة بمجرد الزراعة لم يرتفع ما هو الموجب للفساد، احتمال أن وهو يزرع فيها ما يضر بالأرض، فكيف ينقلب إلى الجواز؛ ولأن المعقود عليه إذا كان مجهولا لا يتعين إلا بتعيينهما صونا عن الإضرار بالآخر، ولا ينفرد به أحدهما؟ قلت: الأصل إجازة العقد عند انتفاء المانع؛ لأن العقود تصح بقدر الإمكان، والمانع الذي فسد العقد باعتباره توقع المنازعة بينهما، وعند استيفاء المنافع يزول هذا. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٢/٨]
وإن استأجر حمارا إلخ: هذه الصورة أيضا من الإجارات التي تفسدها الجهالة أي إذا استأجر أحد حمارا إلى مكة بدينار ولم يبين ما يحمل عليه، فالإجارة فاسدة؛ لجهالة المعقود عليه، فإذا حمل عليه ما يحمل الناس على مثله، وهلك الحمار في الطريق لا يضمن المستأجر ؛ لأن الإجارة وإن كانت فاسدة لكن العين أمانة في يده، و لم يتعد فلا ضمان، وأما إذا تعدى ضمن ولا أجر عليه، وإن بلغ مكة فله المسمى؛ لأن الفساد كان لجهالة ما يحمل عليه، فإذا حمل شيئا يحمل على مثله تعين ذلك، فانقلب صحيحا، وأما إذا كان زائدا على ما يحمل على مثله لا يجب المسمى بل أجر المثل من "الفتح" بتوضيح. ولم يسم: المستأجر فالإجارة فاسدة للجهالة. فإن تشاحًا إلخ: أي إن اختصم المؤجر والمستأجر إلى القاضي قبل أن يحمل على الحمار في ما إذا استأجره، و لم يبين ما يحمل عليه، وقبل أن يزرع فيما إذا استأجر أرضا و لم يبين أنه يزرعها أو أي شيء يزرعها، نقضت الإجارة دفعا للفساد؛ إذ الفساد باق قبل أن ترتفع الجهالة بالتعيين بالزرع والحمل، فإن في "التكملة" فإن قلت: حكم الإجارة الفاسدة نقضها قبل تمام المدة ووجوب الأجرة بعد الاستعمال فكان ينبغي أن يقدم هذه المسألة على وجوب الأجرة بعد الاستعمال؟ قلنا : قدم الأجرة لكثرة وقوعها فتأمل ولا يخفى أن رفع الفاسد تشاحا أو لم يتشاحا فكان عليه أن لا يقيده بذلك، ولو قال وعليهما أن يرفعا العقد لكان أولى. دفعا للفساد قلت الأولى أن يقال: رفعا للفساد بالراء لا بالدال. (فتح)
Book of Ijarah. Invalid Ijarah. And if the term expires, he receives the named wage. And if one hires a donkey to Mecca without specifying what to load, then loads what people usually load on its like, and it dies, he does not guarantee, and if he reaches Mecca, he receives the named wage. If they dispute before loading, the contract is annulled to prevent corruption. And it was said about the second: the load is for the lessor. And the term expires—it is not said that expiration is a condition for the contract to return to validity, but rather if he plants, the uncertainty is removed before the contract ends, so why did the author restrict it to the expiration of the term? Therefore, it is said in al-Durr: if he had omitted the phrase 'so the term expires' like Qadi Khan, it would have been better. We say: the author did not restrict it to the expiration because it is a condition for the contract to return to validity, but rather to allow the demand for the wage, since there is no demand for the wage before its time ends. So ponder, as in al-Fath with slight change. So he receives the named wage by istihsan, and by qiyas he receives the fair wage, and Zufar said so. Because the uncertainty that causes invalidity has been removed. It is said in al-Nihayah: if it is said: when the uncertainty is removed by mere planting, the cause of invalidity is not removed, because he may plant something harmful to the land, so how does it become valid? And because the object of the contract if unknown cannot be determined except by mutual specification to prevent harm to the other, and neither party can specify alone? I say: the principle is to permit the contract when the impediment is absent, because contracts are made valid as much as possible, and the impediment that invalidated the contract is the potential for dispute, and when the benefits are realized this disappears. And if one hires a donkey etc.: this is also an example of ijarah invalidated by uncertainty. If one hires a donkey to Mecca for one dinar without specifying what to load, the ijarah is invalid due to uncertainty of the object. If he loads what people load on its like and the donkey dies on the way, the hirer does not guarantee, because although the ijarah is invalid, the thing is an amana in his hand and he did not transgress, so no liability. If he transgresses he guarantees and no wage. If he reaches Mecca, he receives the named wage because the invalidity was due to uncertainty of the load, and when he loads something that is loaded on its like, the load is specified, so it becomes valid. If the load is more than what is usually loaded on its like, the named wage is not due but the fair wage. And if they dispute before loading: if the lessor and hirer dispute before loading in the case of the donkey, or before planting in the case of land, the ijarah is annulled to prevent corruption, because the invalidity remains until the uncertainty is removed by specification through planting or loading. For in al-Takmilah: if you say: the ruling of invalid ijarah is to annul it before the end of the term and to give wage after use, so it would be appropriate to present this issue before the obligation of wage after use? I say: he presented the wage because it occurs frequently, so ponder. And it is not hidden that the removal of the invalid contract is the same whether they dispute or not, so he should not have restricted it to dispute. And if he had said: both must annul the contract, it would have been better. 'Defa'an lil-fasad'—I say it should be pronounced with ra' not dal (as in raf'an).
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage addresses the rulings of invalid (fasid) hire contracts in the Hanafi school. The author first states that if the term of an invalid ijarah expires, the hirer is entitled to the named wage, not the fair wage, based on istihsan (juristic preference). The example given is a hire of a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load. If the hirer loads what is customary and the donkey dies, he is not liable because the donkey is an amana in his possession and there is no transgression. However, if he reaches Mecca, he receives the named wage because the uncertainty (jahalah) was removed by loading the customary load, thus the contract becomes valid. If a dispute arises before loading, the contract should be annulled to prevent corruption. The text then addresses a potential objection: why did the author condition validity on the expiration of the term? The response clarifies that expiration is not a condition for validity but for the right to demand the wage. The passage also includes a discussion of the qiyas position (held by Imam Zufar) that the fair wage is due, but the relied-upon position is istihsan giving the named wage. The second example involves leasing land without specifying the crop; if the lessee plants, the contract becomes valid. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explains the reasoning: the impediment to validity is the potential for dispute, which is eliminated when the benefits are realized. The passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi ruling on invalid ijarah, covering both the rule and the underlying rationale.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is invalid due to a defect such as uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter.
المسمى (al-musamma): The wage or rent agreed upon by the parties at the time of contract.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference—departing from the apparent qiyas (analogy) in favor of a ruling that is more equitable or conducive to public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an ijarah contract is invalid due to uncertainty but the benefit is realized, the hirer must pay:
A) Nothing, the contract is void.
B) The fair market wage (ujrat al-mithl).
C) The named wage (al-musamma) by istihsan.
D) Double the named wage as penalty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an invalid ijarah can become valid upon realization of the benefit, and the named wage is due by istihsan, overriding qiyas.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Practical Consequences and Annulment of Invalid Ijarah
Practical examples and annulment rulings for invalid ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the liability of the hirer if the hired property is damaged in an invalid ijarah, and explain when the contract should be annulled.

Core Idea
In invalid ijarah, damage without transgression means no liability; annulment is required before use if the uncertainty persists.

The previous lesson established that an invalid ijarah can become valid through use. However, what happens if the hired property is damaged before the benefit is fully realized? And what if the parties dispute before use? This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq provides the Hanafi rulings on these practical issues, emphasizing the amana status of the hired property and the need to annul the contract if uncertainty remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage gives two examples: hiring a donkey without specifying the load, and leasing land without specifying the crop. Recognize the common element: uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter.
2
Determine liability for damage
If the donkey dies while being used with customary load, the hirer is not liable because the property is an amana (trust) in his hands, and there is no transgression. If there is transgression (e.g., overloading), he is liable and also loses entitlement to any wage.
3
Determine wage when benefit is realized
If the journey is completed, the hirer receives the named wage (per istihsan). But if he overloads, only the fair wage is due because the contract remains partially invalid.
4
Understand annulment before use
If parties dispute before any use (loading/planting), the contract must be annulled to prevent corruption, because the uncertainty remains. The author notes that annulment should be done whether they dispute or not.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage addresses the rulings of invalid (fasid) hire contracts in the Hanafi school. The author first states that if the term of an invalid ijarah expires, the hirer is entitled to the named wage, not the fair wage, based on istihsan (juristic preference). The example given is a hire of a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load. If the hirer loads what is customary and the donkey dies, he is not liable because the donkey is an amana in his possession and there is no transgression. However, if he reaches Mecca, he receives the named wage because the uncertainty (jahalah) was removed by loading the customary load, thus the contract becomes valid. If a dispute arises before loading, the contract should be annulled to prevent corruption. The text then addresses a potential objection: why did the author condition validity on the expiration of the term? The response clarifies that expiration is not a condition for validity but for the right to demand the wage. The passage also includes a discussion of the qiyas position (held by Imam Zufar) that the fair wage is due, but the relied-upon position is istihsan giving the named wage. The second example involves leasing land without specifying the crop; if the lessee plants, the contract becomes valid. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explains the reasoning: the impediment to validity is the potential for dispute, which is eliminated when the benefits are realized. The passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi ruling on invalid ijarah, covering both the rule and the underlying rationale.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is invalid due to a defect such as uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter.
أمانة (amanah): A trust; property held without liability for loss or damage as long as there is no transgression.
تعدى (ta'addi): Transgression; exceeding the boundaries of the contract or acting improperly with the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an invalid ijarah, if the hired object is damaged without transgression, the hirer:
A) Is liable for the damage.
B) Is not liable because the object is an amana.
C) Is liable only if the contract was explicit.
D) Must pay the fair wage anyway.

Key Takeaway
In invalid ijarah, the hired property is a trust, so no liability without transgression; annulment before use prevents corruption.
